Trick: "B.N. Rau = Constitutional Advisor = prepared initial draft." He's the unsung hero — did the groundwork that Ambedkar's committee refined. Think: Rau = Research (he studied other constitutions), Ambedkar = Architecture (he designed the final structure).
Q.150. The Constituent Assembly took how long to frame the Constitution? Ans: 2 years, 11 months, and 18 days
Explanation: First meeting: December 9, 1946. Adopted: November 26, 1949. Total sessions: 11. Total days of sitting: 165. Total expenditure: approximately Rs.64 lakhs. Had 389 members (reduced to 299 after partition).
Trick: "2 years, 11 months, 18 days." Remember as "almost 3 years." Started Dec 1946, ended Nov 1949. 165 sitting days out of ~1080 total days. Members debated extensively — that's why our Constitution is so detailed and comprehensive.

1.14 Recent Constitutional Developments

Q.151. 103rd Amendment (2019) provides: Ans: 10% reservation for Economically Weaker Sections (EWS) in education and employment
Explanation: First time reservation based on ECONOMIC criteria (not caste). EWS = family income <8 lakh/year, land <5 acres, house <1000 sq ft. Applies to general category only (SC/ST/OBC already have reservation). SC upheld it in Janhit Abhiyan case (2022) by 3:2 majority.
Trick: "103rd = EWS 10% (2019)." Total reservation now: SC(15%) + ST(7.5%) + OBC(27%) + EWS(10%) = 59.5%. Exceeds 50% cap set by Indra Sawhney case (1992), but SC allowed it as a separate category.
Q.152. 104th Amendment (2020) deals with: Ans: Extension of reservation for SCs/STs in Lok Sabha and State Assemblies till 2030 (and removed Anglo-Indian nomination)
Explanation: SC/ST seats in Parliament/Assemblies are reserved proportional to population. This reservation was originally for 10 years (1960), extended every 10 years. 104th extended it to 2030. Also abolished Anglo-Indian nominated seats.
Trick: "104th = SC/ST reservation extended to 2030 + Anglo-Indian seats removed." Anglo-Indian community had 2 nominated seats in LS since 1950 — now gone. SC/ST reservation has been extended 7 times since 1960.
Q.153. GST Council is constituted under: Ans: Article 279A
Explanation: GST Council decides tax rates, exemptions, and rules. Chaired by Union Finance Minister. Members: Union + all State Finance Ministers. Decisions by 3/4th majority (Centre has 1/3rd weightage, States have 2/3rd). Recommendations are not binding (SC ruled in 2022).
Trick: "279A = GST Council." Centre has 1/3 vote, all states together have 2/3. This means Centre alone can't decide — needs some states' support. But states alone (without Centre) also can't decide. Cooperative federalism in action.
Q.154. NITI Aayog replaced Planning Commission in: Ans: January 1, 2015
Explanation: NITI = National Institution for Transforming India. Unlike Planning Commission (which allocated funds top-down), NITI Aayog is a think tank that advises. It promotes cooperative federalism — states have more say. No fund allocation power.
Trick: "NITI Aayog = 2015 = think tank (not fund allocator)." Planning Commission (1950-2014) was extra-constitutional. NITI Aayog is also extra-constitutional (not in Constitution). PM is Chairman, CEO is appointed by PM.
Q.155. The Chairman of NITI Aayog is: Ans: Prime Minister
Explanation: PM = Chairman. Vice-Chairman = appointed by PM (equivalent to Cabinet Minister rank). CEO = appointed by PM (IAS officer usually). Governing Council = all CMs + LG of UTs. It's advisory — no binding power on states.
Trick: "NITI Aayog: PM=Chairman, has Vice-Chairman + CEO." Planning Commission: PM was Chairman too, but it had Deputy Chairman who was very powerful (allocated funds). NITI Aayog's Vice-Chairman has less power (only advisory).
Q.156. National Commission for Backward Classes is under: Ans: Article 338B (added by 102nd Amendment, 2018)
Explanation: Gave constitutional status to NCBC (earlier it was statutory under 1993 Act). NCBC examines requests for inclusion/exclusion from OBC list, advises on policy. Chairperson + Vice-Chairperson + 3 members appointed by President.
Trick: "338B = OBC Commission (102nd Amendment, 2018)." Remember the sequence: 338=SC, 338A=ST, 338B=OBC. All three now have constitutional status. 102nd Amendment also gave Parliament (not states) power to identify OBCs.
Q.157. Goods and Services Tax (GST) was implemented from: Ans: July 1, 2017
Explanation: GST replaced 17 central and state taxes (excise, VAT, service tax, etc.) with one unified tax. "One Nation, One Tax, One Market." 5 slabs: 0%, 5%, 12%, 18%, 28%. Petroleum, alcohol, electricity kept outside GST.
Trick: "GST: July 1, 2017 = midnight launch." 101st Amendment (2016) enabled it. GST Council (Art.279A) decides rates. Petroleum/alcohol NOT under GST (states didn't want to lose revenue from these). IGST=inter-state, CGST+SGST=intra-state.
Q.158. Article 35A (now abrogated) dealt with: Ans: Special privileges to permanent residents of J&K (property rights, government jobs, scholarships)
Explanation: Added by Presidential Order in 1954 (not by Parliament amendment). Gave J&K legislature power to define "permanent residents" and give them exclusive rights. Non-residents couldn't buy property or get govt jobs in J&K. Abrogated along with Art.370 on Aug 5, 2019.
Trick: "35A = J&K residents' special rights = GONE (2019)." It was never debated in Parliament (added by Presidential Order). This was one reason for its controversy. After abrogation, anyone can buy property in J&K.
Q.159. Jammu & Kashmir was reorganized into UTs by: Ans: J&K Reorganisation Act, 2019 (effective from October 31, 2019)
Explanation: J&K state split into: (1) UT of J&K (with legislature, like Delhi) and (2) UT of Ladakh (without legislature). Art.370 abrogated simultaneously. Oct 31 chosen as it's Sardar Patel's birth anniversary (he integrated princely states).
Trick: "Oct 31, 2019 = J&K reorganized." J&K UT has elected Assembly (like Delhi/Puducherry). Ladakh UT has no Assembly (like Chandigarh/Lakshadweep). India went from 29 states to 28 states + 9 UTs (now 8 UTs after Dadra merger).
Q.160. The National Judicial Appointments Commission (NJAC) was struck down in: Ans: 2015 (99th Amendment declared unconstitutional by SC)
Explanation: NJAC was meant to replace Collegium system for appointing judges. It included CJI + 2 senior judges + Law Minister + 2 eminent persons. SC struck it down 4:1 saying it violated judicial independence (basic structure). Collegium system continues.
Trick: "NJAC = 99th Amendment = struck down 2015." SC said: "Judges must appoint judges — executive involvement threatens independence." This is rare — SC declared a constitutional AMENDMENT unconstitutional! Shows power of Basic Structure doctrine.

1.15 Important Articles at a Glance

Q.161. Article 1 states: Ans: "India, that is Bharat, shall be a Union of States"
Explanation: Two key points: (1) India has two names — India AND Bharat (both official). (2) It's a "Union" not "Federation" — meaning states cannot secede. The word "Union" was deliberately chosen to emphasize indestructibility.
Trick: "Art.1 = India = Bharat = Union of States." Why "Union" not "Federation"? Because states have NO right to separate. India's unity is non-negotiable. Ambedkar explained: "The Union is not the result of an agreement by states to join."
Q.162. Article 3 deals with: Ans: Formation of new states and alteration of boundaries
Explanation: Parliament can: create new states, merge states, change boundaries, change names — by SIMPLE majority. President refers the bill to affected state legislature for opinion, but Parliament is NOT bound by that opinion. States cannot veto their own reorganization!
Trick: "Art.3 = Parliament can redraw India's map." States have NO veto! This is how Telangana was created (2014), J&K reorganized (2019). Only Parliament decides. State's opinion is sought but not binding. Shows Centre's dominance.
Q.163. Article 112 deals with: Ans: Annual Financial Statement (Union Budget)
Explanation: The President causes the Budget to be laid before Parliament every year. It shows estimated receipts and expenditure. Budget has two parts: Consolidated Fund (needs Parliament approval) and Contingency Fund (President's discretion).
Trick: "Art.112 = Union Budget." Budget is presented on Feb 1 (since 2017, earlier it was last day of February). Finance Minister presents it. It's a statement of government's income and spending plan for the next year.
Q.164. Article 143 deals with: Ans: Advisory jurisdiction of Supreme Court
Explanation: President can ask SC's opinion on any question of law or fact of public importance. SC's advice is not binding on President. SC can also refuse to answer. Used rarely — examples: Delhi Laws Act case, Cauvery water dispute, 2G spectrum.
Trick: "Art.143 = President asks SC for advice." It's like asking a lawyer for opinion — you don't have to follow it. SC's advisory opinions are not "law declared" under Art.141 (not binding on other courts).
Q.165. Article 200 deals with: Ans: Assent to Bills by Governor
Explanation: When state legislature passes a bill, Governor can: (1) Give assent (becomes law). (2) Withhold assent (bill dies). (3) Return for reconsideration (not Money Bills). (4) Reserve for President's consideration. Governor has more discretion than President in this matter.
Trick: "Art.200 = Governor's assent to state bills." "Art.111 = President's assent to central bills." Governor can reserve bills for President — this is a unique power that President doesn't have (no one above President to reserve for!).
Q.166. Article 213 deals with: Ans: Power of Governor to promulgate Ordinances
Explanation: When state legislature is not in session, Governor can issue Ordinances (temporary laws) on state subjects. Must be laid before legislature within 6 weeks of reassembly. Ceases to operate after 6 weeks if not approved. Needs President's instruction for certain matters.
Trick: "Art.213 = Governor's Ordinance." "Art.123 = President's Ordinance." Same concept at different levels. Ordinance = temporary law when legislature not in session. Valid for 6 weeks after legislature reassembles. Can be re-promulgated (but SC frowns on repeated re-promulgation).
Q.167. Article 243 deals with: Ans: Panchayati Raj (Part IX — Articles 243 to 243O)
Explanation: Part IX (added by 73rd Amendment) contains all provisions about Panchayats: definitions, composition, reservation, elections, powers, finance, etc. Art.243 to 243O cover Panchayats. Art.243P to 243ZG cover Municipalities (Part IXA).
Trick: "Art.243 = Panchayats start here." The entire Panchayat framework is in Art.243 series (243A, 243B, 243C... up to 243O). Similarly Municipalities = 243P onwards. Think of 243 as the "local government article number."
Q.168. Article 280 deals with: Ans: Finance Commission
Q.169. Article 300A states: Ans: No person shall be deprived of property save by authority of law (Legal Right)
Q.170. Article 311 deals with: Ans: Safeguards for civil servants
Q.171. Article 320 deals with: Ans: Functions of Public Service Commissions
Q.172. Article 323A deals with: Ans: Administrative Tribunals
Q.173. Article 330 deals with: Ans: Reservation of seats for SCs/STs in Lok Sabha
Q.174. Article 343 deals with: Ans: Official Language of the Union
Q.175. Article 352 deals with: Ans: Proclamation of National Emergency
Q.176. Article 356 deals with: Ans: President's Rule in States
Q.177. Article 360 deals with: Ans: Financial Emergency
Q.178. Article 368 deals with: Ans: Power of Parliament to amend the Constitution
Q.179. Article 395 is: Ans: Last Article (Repeals) of the original Constitution
Q.180. Which Part of the Constitution deals with Union Territories? Ans: Part VIII (Articles 239-241)

1.16 Landmark Supreme Court Cases

Q.181. Golaknath case (1967) held that: Ans: Parliament cannot amend Fundamental Rights
Explanation: SC (6:5 majority) said FRs are "transcendental" and Parliament cannot take them away. This was later OVERRULED by Kesavananda Bharati (1973) which said Parliament CAN amend FRs but can't destroy basic structure.
Trick: "Golaknath (1967) = FRs can't be amended." "Kesavananda (1973) = CAN amend but can't destroy basic structure." Golaknath was too restrictive; Kesavananda found the middle ground. Timeline: Shankari Prasad(1951)→Golaknath(1967)→Kesavananda(1973).
Q.182. Kesavananda Bharati case (1973) established: Ans: Basic Structure doctrine — Parliament can amend Constitution but cannot destroy its basic structure
Explanation: 13-judge bench (largest ever), 7:6 verdict. Basic structure includes: supremacy of Constitution, republican form, secularism, separation of powers, federalism, judicial review, rule of law, democracy. This is India's most important constitutional case.
Trick: "Kesavananda = Basic Structure = 1973 = 13 judges = 7:6." It's the FOUNDATION of Indian constitutional law. Every amendment since is tested against basic structure. Without this case, Parliament could have made India a dictatorship legally!
Q.183. Minerva Mills case (1980) held that: Ans: Judicial review is part of basic structure; there must be harmony between FRs and DPSPs
Explanation: Struck down parts of 42nd Amendment that tried to give DPSPs supremacy over FRs and remove judicial review. SC said: FRs and DPSPs are complementary, not contradictory. Neither can destroy the other. Balance is essential.
Trick: "Minerva Mills = balance between FR and DPSP." 42nd Amendment tried to make DPSPs supreme over FRs — SC said NO. Both are important. Think of FRs as "individual rights" and DPSPs as "social goals" — society needs both.
Q.184. Maneka Gandhi case (1978) expanded: Ans: Scope of Article 21 — Right to Life includes right to live with dignity, fair procedure
Explanation: Before this case, Art.21 was narrow (just physical life). After Maneka Gandhi, SC said Art.21 includes: right to livelihood, travel abroad, privacy, dignity, clean environment, speedy trial, legal aid, shelter, health, education. Also introduced "due process" concept.
Trick: "Maneka Gandhi (1978) = Art.21 expanded massively." Before: Art.21 = just "don't kill me." After: Art.21 = right to live a DIGNIFIED life with all necessities. This single case transformed Indian human rights jurisprudence.
Q.185. S.R. Bommai case (1994) dealt with: Ans: Misuse of Article 356 (President's Rule) — made it subject to judicial review
Explanation: SC laid down guidelines: (1) President's Rule is subject to judicial review. (2) Floor test is the only way to determine majority (not Governor's subjective opinion). (3) State Assembly should not be dissolved until Parliament approves. Reduced misuse of Art.356 significantly.
Trick: "S.R. Bommai (1994) = Art.356 can be reviewed by courts." Before this, Centre could dismiss any state government at will. After Bommai, courts can check if President's Rule was justified. Dramatically reduced its misuse.
Q.186. Vishaka case (1997) dealt with: Ans: Sexual harassment at workplace — SC laid down guidelines (Vishaka Guidelines)
Explanation: In absence of legislation, SC created guidelines to prevent sexual harassment at work. Defined sexual harassment, mandated complaints committees in every workplace. These guidelines were law until Sexual Harassment of Women at Workplace Act, 2013 replaced them.
Trick: "Vishaka (1997) = workplace sexual harassment guidelines." Named after an NGO from Rajasthan. Led to POSH Act (2013) = Prevention of Sexual Harassment Act. SC acted as legislature because Parliament hadn't made a law yet.
Q.187. Indra Sawhney case (1992) dealt with: Ans: Mandal Commission — upheld 27% OBC reservation; set 50% ceiling on total reservations
Explanation: SC upheld Mandal Commission's 27% OBC reservation but set conditions: (1) Total reservation cannot exceed 50%. (2) "Creamy layer" among OBCs excluded. (3) No reservation in promotions for OBCs. This is the most important reservation case.
Trick: "Indra Sawhney (1992) = Mandal = 50% cap = creamy layer." The 50% rule was later challenged by EWS (103rd Amendment takes total to 59.5%). Creamy layer = economically well-off OBCs who don't need reservation.
Q.188. Shankari Prasad case (1951) held that: Ans: Parliament CAN amend Fundamental Rights under Article 368
Explanation: First case on amendment power. SC said Art.368 gives Parliament power to amend ANY part of Constitution including FRs. "Amendment" is not "law" under Art.13, so FRs don't restrict amendment power. Later partially overruled by Golaknath.
Trick: Timeline of amendment power cases: Shankari Prasad(1951)=CAN amend → Golaknath(1967)=CANNOT amend → Kesavananda(1973)=CAN amend but can't destroy basic structure. The law evolved through these three cases.
Q.189. Berubari Union case (1960) held that: Ans: Preamble is NOT a part of the Constitution (later overruled by Kesavananda, 1973)
Explanation: SC said Preamble is just an introduction — not enforceable, not part of Constitution. This was OVERRULED in Kesavananda (1973) which said Preamble IS part of Constitution (but still non-justiciable). Preamble can be amended (done once by 42nd Amendment).
Trick: "Berubari = Preamble NOT part (1960)." "Kesavananda = Preamble IS part (1973)." Current position: Preamble is part of Constitution, can be amended under Art.368, but is non-justiciable (can't be enforced in court).
Q.190. Waman Rao case (1981) held that: Ans: Amendments made before Kesavananda case (April 24, 1973) are valid and cannot be challenged; basic structure test applies only to amendments made AFTER that date
Explanation: This gave a "cut-off date" for basic structure doctrine. All amendments before April 24, 1973 are immune from basic structure challenge. Only future amendments can be tested. This provided certainty and stability.
Trick: "Waman Rao = April 24, 1973 is the cut-off." Before this date = safe from basic structure challenge. After this date = can be struck down if violates basic structure. This date is from Kesavananda judgment day.

1.17 Anti-Defection & Electoral Reforms

Q.191. Anti-defection law was added by: Ans: 52nd Amendment (1985) — 10th Schedule
Explanation: Prevents elected representatives from switching parties after election. If you defect, you lose your seat. Added after political instability of 1960s-80s when MLAs/MPs were "bought" by rival parties (horse-trading).
Trick: "52nd Amendment = Anti-defection = 10th Schedule = 1985." Rajiv Gandhi's government passed it with massive majority. Dinesh Goswami Committee (1990) and Law Commission recommended reforms to it.
Q.192. Who decides disqualification under anti-defection law? Ans: Speaker/Chairman of the House (subject to judicial review after Kihoto Hollohan case, 1992)
Explanation: Speaker decides if a member has defected. This decision is final BUT can be challenged in court (judicial review). Problem: Speakers often delay decisions for political reasons. No time limit for Speaker to decide!
Trick: "Speaker decides defection." Criticism: Speaker is usually from ruling party — may be biased. Kihoto Hollohan case (1992) said Speaker's decision is subject to judicial review. Many suggest giving this power to Election Commission instead.
Q.193. 91st Amendment (2003) modified anti-defection law by: Ans: Removing provision for 1/3rd split; only merger of 2/3rd of party members allowed
Explanation: Earlier, if 1/3rd of a party's legislators split, it was legal (not defection). This was misused. 91st Amendment removed this — now only MERGER of 2/3rd of party with another party is allowed. Also barred defectors from becoming ministers.
Trick: "91st Amendment = tightened anti-defection." Before: 1/3rd split = legal. After: only 2/3rd merger = legal. This made it harder to break parties. Also: total ministers capped at 15% of House strength (to prevent "ministry of all" governments).
Q.194. EVM (Electronic Voting Machine) was first used in: Ans: 1982 (Kerala — Paravur Assembly constituency, on experimental basis)
Explanation: First experimental use in 1982 (Kerala). First state-wide use: 1998 (select constituencies). All constituencies: 2004 general elections onwards. EVMs replaced paper ballots to reduce booth capturing, invalid votes, and counting time.
Trick: "EVM first = 1982 Kerala." Full nationwide use from 2004. EVMs are made by BEL (Bharat Electronics) and ECIL (Electronics Corporation of India). VVPAT added later (2013) for verification.
Q.195. NOTA option was introduced in: Ans: 2013 (based on PUCL vs Union of India case, SC directed EC to add NOTA)
Explanation: NOTA = None Of The Above. Allows voters to reject all candidates. SC said it's part of right to expression. But NOTA votes don't affect results — even if NOTA gets most votes, the candidate with most votes still wins.
Trick: "NOTA = 2013 = PUCL case." NOTA is symbolic — doesn't lead to re-election even if it wins. Symbol: ballot paper with cross mark. First used in 2013 state elections. Criticism: it's toothless since it doesn't change the outcome.
Q.196. VVPAT (Voter Verifiable Paper Audit Trail) was first used in: Ans: 2013 (Nagaland by-election — Noksen constituency)
Explanation: VVPAT prints a paper slip showing which candidate you voted for — visible for 7 seconds through a window. Provides physical verification that EVM recorded your vote correctly. Mandatory in all elections since 2019.
Trick: "VVPAT = 2013 Nagaland = paper trail for EVM." It's the answer to "EVMs can be hacked" concerns. SC ordered VVPAT matching of 5 random machines per constituency (2019). Adds transparency to electronic voting.
Q.197. Representation of People Act was enacted in: Ans: 1950 (qualifications for voters/candidates) and 1951 (conduct of elections, corrupt practices, disputes)
Explanation: Two Acts: RPA 1950 deals with preparation of electoral rolls and allocation of seats. RPA 1951 deals with actual conduct of elections, election offenses, corrupt practices, and election petitions.
Trick: "RPA 1950 = who can vote (rolls/seats)." "RPA 1951 = how elections are conducted (rules/offenses)." Together they form the legal framework for Indian elections. Most election-related court cases cite RPA 1951.
Q.198. Model Code of Conduct comes into force from: Ans: Date of announcement of elections (not date of voting)
Explanation: MCC is a set of guidelines for parties/candidates during elections. No new schemes, no government ads, no misuse of official machinery. It's NOT a law — it's a voluntary code enforced by EC's moral authority. Violators face EC's displeasure/censure.
Trick: "MCC starts from announcement, ends at results." It's NOT legally enforceable (not a law) — but EC's authority makes parties follow it. Key rules: no freebies announcement, no religious appeals, no government vehicle misuse, no new projects.
Q.199. The first General Elections in India were held in: Ans: 1951-52 (October 1951 to February 1952)
Explanation: India's first elections were the world's largest democratic exercise at that time — 17.3 crore voters, 53% turnout. Congress won 364/489 seats. Nehru became PM. Sukumar Sen was the first Chief Election Commissioner who organized them.
Trick: "First elections = 1951-52." Took 4 months to complete (Oct 1951-Feb 1952) because of logistics. Sukumar Sen = first CEC = hero of Indian democracy (organized elections in a newly independent, largely illiterate nation).
Q.200. Universal Adult Suffrage means: Ans: Every citizen above 18 years has the right to vote regardless of caste, religion, gender, education, or property
Explanation: Originally voting age was 21 (Art.326). Reduced to 18 by 61st Amendment (1988, Rajiv Gandhi's government). India adopted universal suffrage from Day 1 (1950) — unlike UK/USA where women/poor got voting rights much later.
Trick: "61st Amendment (1988) = voting age 21→18." India was progressive — gave ALL adults voting rights in 1950 itself. UK gave women full voting rights only in 1928. USA's 15th Amendment (race) was 1870, 19th (women) was 1920. India did it all at once!

Section 2: Indian History (150 Questions)

Topics: Ancient India, Medieval India, Modern India - Freedom Movement, Important Personalities, Social Reform Movements

2.1 Ancient India

Q.201. The Indus Valley Civilization belongs to which age? Ans: Bronze Age (approximately 3300-1300 BCE, mature phase 2600-1900 BCE)
Explanation: Called "Bronze Age" because they used bronze (copper+tin alloy) for tools and weapons. They did NOT know iron. It's also called Harappan Civilization (after first discovered site). It's one of the world's oldest urban civilizations alongside Mesopotamia and Egypt.
Trick: "IVC = Bronze Age = NO iron." Three phases: Early (3300-2600 BCE), Mature (2600-1900 BCE), Late (1900-1300 BCE). Exam usually asks about Mature phase. Contemporary to: Egyptian pyramids and Mesopotamian cities.
Q.202. The most important sites of Indus Valley Civilization are: Ans: Harappa (Punjab, Pakistan), Mohenjo-daro (Sindh, Pakistan), Lothal (Gujarat), Kalibangan (Rajasthan), Dholavira (Gujarat), Rakhigarhi (Haryana)
Explanation: Harappa = first discovered (1921, Daya Ram Sahni). Mohenjo-daro = largest city ("Mound of Dead"). Lothal = dockyard/port. Kalibangan = ploughed field, fire altars. Dholavira = water management, signboard. Rakhigarhi = largest site in India.
Trick: "HMLDKR" = Harappa, Mohenjo-daro, Lothal, Dholavira, Kalibangan, Rakhigarhi. Remember each site's specialty: Harappa=granary, Mohenjo-daro=Great Bath, Lothal=dock, Kalibangan=ploughed field, Dholavira=water reservoir, Rakhigarhi=largest Indian site.
Q.203. The Great Bath was found at: Ans: Mohenjo-daro (in present-day Sindh, Pakistan)
Explanation: The Great Bath is a large public bathing pool (12m × 7m × 2.4m deep). Made of baked bricks with bitumen (waterproofing). Likely used for ritual bathing/purification. Shows advanced engineering and possibly religious practices.
Trick: "Mohenjo-daro = Great Bath + Dancing Girl + Priest King statue." It's the most excavated IVC site. Name means "Mound of the Dead" in Sindhi. Discovered by R.D. Banerjee (1922).
Q.204. The dockyard of Indus Valley Civilization was found at: Ans: Lothal (Gujarat, India)
Explanation: Lothal had the world's earliest known dockyard (37m × 22m) — proving IVC had maritime trade. They traded with Mesopotamia (modern Iraq). Lothal also had a bead-making factory and a rice husk (earliest evidence of rice cultivation).
Trick: "Lothal = Dock + Trade + Rice." Located in Gujarat near Gulf of Khambhat. "Lothal" means "Mound of the Dead" in Gujarati (similar to Mohenjo-daro!). Discovered by S.R. Rao (1954). Key: proves IVC had sea trade.
Q.205. The script of Indus Valley Civilization is: Ans: Pictographic (not yet deciphered), written from right to left
Explanation: IVC script has about 400-600 symbols. Written right to left (boustrophedon — alternating directions in some cases). Despite 100+ years of attempts, NO ONE has decoded it. We don't know what language they spoke. This is one of archaeology's greatest mysteries.
Trick: "IVC script = UNDECIPHERED = right to left." Because it's undeciphered, we know IVC only through archaeology (buildings, artifacts), not through their own writings. If decoded, it would revolutionize our understanding of ancient India.
Q.206. The Vedas are: Ans: Rig Veda, Yajur Veda, Sama Veda, Atharva Veda
Explanation: Vedas = "knowledge" in Sanskrit. They are the oldest Hindu scriptures (1500-500 BCE). Rig = hymns/prayers. Yajur = rituals/procedures. Sama = melodies/music. Atharva = magic/medicine/daily life. Each Veda has 4 parts: Samhita, Brahmana, Aranyaka, Upanishad.
Trick: "RYSA" = Rig, Yajur, Sama, Atharva. Remember: "Rig = Recitation (hymns), Yajur = Yagna (rituals), Sama = Songs (music), Atharva = Atharvans (priests/magic)." Rig is oldest and most important. Sama is shortest. Atharva is most different (non-ritualistic).
Q.207. The oldest Veda is: Ans: Rig Veda (composed approximately 1500-1200 BCE)
Explanation: Rig Veda has 1028 hymns (suktas) in 10 books (mandalas). It mentions rivers (especially Saraswati), gods (Indra most mentioned — 250 hymns), and early Aryan society. The famous Gayatri Mantra is from Rig Veda (Mandala 3). It's the oldest religious text in the world still in use.
Trick: "Rig Veda = oldest = 1028 hymns = 10 mandalas." Most important god = Indra (war god). Gayatri Mantra = Rig Veda. Mandala 2-7 = oldest (family books). Mandala 1 and 10 = added later. Mandala 10 has Purusha Sukta (origin of varna system).
Q.208. Gayatri Mantra is found in: Ans: Rig Veda (composed by sage Vishwamitra, in Mandala 3)
Explanation: The Gayatri Mantra is a prayer to Savitri (Sun god) for enlightenment of intellect. It's the most sacred mantra in Hinduism, recited daily by millions. "Om Bhur Bhuva Swaha, Tat Savitur Varenyam..." It's in Rig Veda, Mandala 3, Sukta 62, Verse 10.
Trick: "Gayatri = Rig Veda = Vishwamitra = Mandala 3." It's dedicated to Sun (Savitri). Upanayana ceremony (sacred thread) involves teaching this mantra. It's considered the "mother of all Vedas."
Q.209. The founder of Jainism is: Ans: Rishabhadeva (1st Tirthankara); Mahavira (24th and last Tirthankara) is the reformer/propagator
Explanation: Jainism has 24 Tirthankaras (ford-makers/teachers). Rishabhadeva (Adinath) = 1st. Parshvanath = 23rd (historical figure, 250 years before Mahavira). Mahavira (Vardhamana) = 24th, born 540 BCE in Vaishali, contemporary of Buddha.
Trick: "24 Tirthankaras: 1st=Rishabhadeva, 23rd=Parshvanath, 24th=Mahavira." Mahavira's 5 vows: Ahimsa (non-violence), Satya (truth), Asteya (non-stealing), Aparigraha (non-possession), Brahmacharya (celibacy — added by Mahavira, Parshvanath had only 4).
Q.210. Gautama Buddha was born at: Ans: Lumbini (in present-day Nepal), approximately 563 BCE
Explanation: Born as Prince Siddhartha in Shakya clan. Father: Suddhodana (king). Mother: Mayadevi (died 7 days after birth). Raised by stepmother Mahaprajapati Gautami. Left home at 29 (Great Renunciation/Mahabhinishkramana) after seeing old age, disease, death, and a monk.
Trick: Buddha's life events at 4 places (all in exam): Born=Lumbini, Enlightenment=Bodh Gaya, First Sermon=Sarnath, Death=Kushinagar. Remember: "LBSK" = Lumbini, Bodh Gaya, Sarnath, Kushinagar (chronological order of his life).
Q.211. Buddha attained enlightenment at: Ans: Bodh Gaya (under a Peepal/Bodhi tree, on the banks of river Niranjana/Falgu)
Explanation: After 6 years of extreme penance, Siddhartha sat under a Peepal tree and meditated. On the full moon night of Vaishakha (May), he attained Nirvana/Enlightenment at age 35. The tree became "Bodhi Tree" and the place "Bodh Gaya." He became "Buddha" (the awakened one).
Trick: "Bodh Gaya = Enlightenment = Bihar." The Mahabodhi Temple at Bodh Gaya is a UNESCO World Heritage Site. Buddha spent 49 days there after enlightenment before going to Sarnath to teach. Bodhi tree still exists (descendant of original).
Q.212. Buddha gave his first sermon at: Ans: Sarnath (Deer Park, near Varanasi) — called Dharmachakra Pravartana ("Turning the Wheel of Law")
Explanation: After enlightenment, Buddha walked to Sarnath and taught 5 ascetics (his former companions). This first sermon is called "Dhammacakkappavattana Sutta." He taught the Four Noble Truths and Eightfold Path. This event is called "Dharmachakra Pravartana."
Trick: "Sarnath = First Sermon = Deer Park = Dharmachakra Pravartana." India's national emblem (Ashoka Pillar with 4 lions) was found at Sarnath! The wheel (chakra) in Indian flag represents this Dharmachakra. Sarnath is near Varanasi, UP.
Q.213. The Mauryan Empire was founded by: Ans: Chandragupta Maurya (321 BCE) with the guidance of Chanakya/Kautilya
Explanation: Chandragupta overthrew the Nanda dynasty with Chanakya's strategy. Built India's first large empire (from Afghanistan to Bengal). Defeated Seleucus Nicator (Greek general). Capital: Pataliputra (modern Patna). Abdicated throne and became Jain monk; died by Sallekhana (fasting) at Shravanabelagola.
Trick: "Chandragupta + Chanakya = Maurya Empire (321 BCE)." Three great Mauryan rulers: Chandragupta (founder) → Bindusara (expanded) → Ashoka (greatest, turned Buddhist). Megasthenes (Greek ambassador) wrote "Indica" about Chandragupta's court.
Q.214. Arthashastra was written by: Ans: Kautilya/Chanakya (a treatise on statecraft, economics, military strategy, and governance)
Explanation: Arthashastra = "Science of Wealth/Statecraft." Written in Sanskrit, ~15 books. Covers: taxation, espionage, diplomacy, war, law, administration. It's like an ancient "how to run a kingdom" manual. Chanakya was a professor at Takshashila (Taxila) university.
Trick: "Arthashastra = Chanakya = Political Science." Chanakya is also called "Indian Machiavelli" (but he came 1800 years before Machiavelli!). Other names: Kautilya, Vishnugupta. The book was lost for centuries and rediscovered in 1905 by R. Shamasastry.
Q.215. Ashoka embraced Buddhism after the: Ans: Kalinga War (261 BCE) — the bloodshed horrified him and he turned to non-violence
Explanation: Kalinga (modern Odisha) war killed ~100,000 people and displaced 150,000. Ashoka was so disturbed by the carnage that he renounced violence and embraced Buddhism. He then spread Buddhism through missionaries (sent his son Mahendra and daughter Sanghamitra to Sri Lanka).
Trick: "Kalinga War = Ashoka's transformation = 261 BCE." Before Kalinga: Ashoka was "Chandashoka" (cruel). After: "Dharmashoka" (righteous). His edicts (rock/pillar inscriptions) spread across India are our main source about him. Kalinga = Odisha.
Q.216. The Gupta period is known as: Ans: Golden Age of India (4th-6th century CE, approximately 320-550 CE)
Explanation: Called "Golden Age" because of extraordinary achievements in: science (Aryabhatta), mathematics (zero, decimal system), literature (Kalidasa), art (Ajanta caves), medicine (Sushruta), astronomy, and metallurgy (Iron Pillar). Peace and prosperity allowed arts and sciences to flourish.
Trick: "Gupta = Golden Age = 320-550 CE." Key figures: Aryabhatta (math/astronomy), Kalidasa (literature — Shakuntala, Meghaduta), Varahamihira (astronomy), Sushruta (surgery), Fa-Hien (Chinese traveler). Chandragupta I → Samudragupta → Chandragupta II (Vikramaditya) = greatest rulers.
Q.217. Aryabhatta belonged to which period? Ans: Gupta period (476-550 CE, wrote Aryabhatiya in 499 CE)
Explanation: Aryabhatta's contributions: (1) Earth rotates on its axis (revolutionary idea!). (2) Calculated pi (π) to 4 decimal places. (3) Solar/lunar eclipses explained scientifically. (4) Place value system. (5) Algebra foundations. He worked at Nalanda University.
Trick: "Aryabhatta = Gupta period = astronomy + math." India's first satellite (1975) named after him. He said Earth is round and rotates — 1000 years before Copernicus! His book Aryabhatiya covers arithmetic, algebra, trigonometry, and astronomy in 121 verses.
Q.218. Nalanda University was established during: Ans: Gupta period (5th century CE) by Kumaragupta I
Explanation: Nalanda (Bihar) was the world's first residential university. Had 10,000+ students from across Asia. Subjects: Buddhism, logic, grammar, medicine, astronomy. Destroyed by Bakhtiyar Khilji (1193 CE). Library burned for 3 months! Ruins are UNESCO World Heritage Site.
Trick: "Nalanda = Kumaragupta I = Gupta period = world's first university." Hiuen Tsang (Chinese traveler, 7th century) studied here for 5 years and described it in detail. Destroyed by Khilji in 1193. New Nalanda University established in 2014 nearby.
Q.219. The Iron Pillar at Delhi belongs to: Ans: Gupta period (4th century CE, erected by Chandragupta II)
Explanation: The Iron Pillar at Mehrauli (Delhi) is 7.2m tall, weighs 6 tonnes, and has NOT rusted in 1600+ years! This shows Gupta-era metallurgical expertise. The pillar has 99.72% pure iron — a feat modern technology struggles to replicate.
Trick: "Iron Pillar = Gupta = rust-free for 1600 years." It's a testament to ancient Indian metallurgy. Located in Qutub Minar complex. The inscription says it was erected by "Chandra" (identified as Chandragupta II Vikramaditya).
Q.220. Harshavardhana's court poet was: Ans: Banabhatta (wrote Harshacharita — biography of Harsha, and Kadambari — a novel)
Explanation: Harsha ruled North India (606-647 CE) from Kannauj. His court had many scholars. Banabhatta wrote Harshacharita (first historical biography in Sanskrit). Hiuen Tsang visited his court. Harsha himself wrote 3 plays: Ratnavali, Priyadarshika, Nagananda.
Trick: "Harsha = Banabhatta = Hiuen Tsang." Harsha was the last great Hindu emperor of North India before Islamic invasions. After his death (647 CE), North India fragmented into small kingdoms. Hiuen Tsang's account is our main source about Harsha's India.

2.2 Medieval India

Q.221. The Delhi Sultanate was established by: Ans: Qutub-ud-din Aibak (1206 CE) — founded the Slave/Mamluk Dynasty
Explanation: Aibak was a slave-general of Muhammad Ghori. After Ghori's death (1206), Aibak declared independence and became Sultan of Delhi. He started building Qutub Minar (completed by Iltutmish). Ruled only 4 years (died playing polo).
Trick: "1206 = Delhi Sultanate begins = Aibak = Slave Dynasty." Aibak was generous — called "Lakh Baksh" (giver of lakhs). He started Qutub Minar but Iltutmish (his son-in-law and successor) completed it.
Q.222. The five dynasties of Delhi Sultanate are: Ans: Slave (1206-1290), Khilji (1290-1320), Tughlaq (1320-1414), Sayyid (1414-1451), Lodi (1451-1526)
Explanation: 320 years of Muslim rule before Mughals. Slave dynasty had Iltutmish, Razia Sultan (first female ruler), Balban. Khilji had Alauddin (market reforms). Tughlaq had Muhammad (experiments). Sayyid were weak. Lodi were Afghan — last was Ibrahim Lodi (defeated by Babur).
Trick: "SKTSL" = Slave, Khilji, Tughlaq, Sayyid, Lodi. Remember: "Some Kings Try Silly Luck." Or by years: 1206-1290-1320-1414-1451-1526 (each dynasty roughly 30-100 years).
Q.223. Who introduced the token currency of copper coins? Ans: Muhammad bin Tughlaq (to solve shortage of silver; experiment failed as people made fake coins at home)
Explanation: Muhammad bin Tughlaq introduced copper/brass coins with the same value as silver coins (like modern paper currency concept). But people counterfeited them easily at home. Treasury was flooded with fake coins. He had to withdraw the scheme at huge loss.
Trick: "Muhammad bin Tughlaq = experiments that failed." His 5 famous experiments: (1) Token currency (2) Transfer of capital to Daulatabad (3) Taxation in Doab (4) Khorasan expedition (5) Qarachil expedition. All failed! He's called "a mixture of opposites" — brilliant but impractical.
Q.224. Who shifted the capital from Delhi to Daulatabad? Ans: Muhammad bin Tughlaq (1327 CE, shifted entire population from Delhi to Daulatabad in Maharashtra — later reversed)
Explanation: He wanted capital in center of his empire (Daulatabad/Devagiri in Maharashtra). Forced entire Delhi population to march 1500 km. Many died on the way. The plan failed — Daulatabad lacked water. He shifted back to Delhi. Called "the maddest king."
Trick: "Tughlaq = Daulatabad disaster." He was actually strategic (central location, safe from Mongol attacks) but execution was terrible. Ibn Battuta (Moroccan traveler) was in his court and described these events. Daulatabad = Devagiri (Yadava capital).
Q.225. The Vijayanagara Empire was founded by: Ans: Harihara I and Bukka I (1336 CE, with guidance of sage Vidyaranya)
Explanation: Founded on the banks of Tungabhadra river (Hampi, Karnataka). Lasted 1336-1646. Greatest ruler: Krishnadevaraya (1509-1529). It was a Hindu empire that resisted Muslim expansion in South India. Defeated at Battle of Talikota (1565).
Trick: "Vijayanagara = 1336 = Harihara & Bukka = Hampi." Krishnadevaraya = greatest king (patron of Telugu literature — Amuktamalyada). Hampi ruins are UNESCO World Heritage Site. Empire fell after Battle of Talikota/Rakshasa-Tangadi (1565) against Deccan Sultanates alliance.
Q.226. The Battle of Panipat (1526) was fought between: Ans: Babur (Mughal) and Ibrahim Lodi (last Delhi Sultan) — Babur won, established Mughal Empire
Explanation: First Battle of Panipat. Babur had only 12,000 soldiers vs Lodi's 100,000 + elephants. Babur won using gunpowder, cannons (first use in India), and Tulughma (flanking) tactics. This ended Delhi Sultanate and started Mughal Empire (1526-1857).
Trick: "3 Battles of Panipat: 1526, 1556, 1761." 1st (1526): Babur vs Ibrahim Lodi = Mughals begin. 2nd (1556): Akbar vs Hemu = Mughals consolidated. 3rd (1761): Afghans vs Marathas = Maratha power declined. Panipat (Haryana) = India's most decisive battlefield.
Q.227. Akbar's revenue system was called: Ans: Todar Mal's Bandobast / Zabti system (also called Dahsala system)
Explanation: Raja Todar Mal (Akbar's finance minister) created a scientific land revenue system: measured land, classified soil quality, fixed revenue based on average of last 10 years' production (Dahsala = 10 years). Revenue was 1/3rd of produce. Most efficient pre-modern tax system in India.
Trick: "Todar Mal = Zabti = Dahsala = 10-year average." Akbar's revenue was fair — based on actual productivity, not arbitrary. Other Mughal revenue systems: Nasaq (estimate), Kankut (crop cutting), Batai (crop sharing). Zabti was most scientific.
Q.228. Din-i-Ilahi was founded by: Ans: Akbar (1582) — a syncretic religion combining elements of Hinduism, Islam, Christianity, Zoroastrianism, and Jainism
Explanation: Din-i-Ilahi = "Religion of God." Akbar tried to create a universal religion promoting tolerance. It had no priests, no scriptures, no temples. Only 18 people joined (including Birbal). It died with Akbar — never became popular. Shows Akbar's liberal thinking.
Trick: "Din-i-Ilahi = Akbar = 1582 = failed experiment." Only notable convert: Birbal (Hindu). It wasn't forced on anyone. Akbar also held "Ibadat Khana" (House of Worship) debates where scholars of all religions discussed. He abolished Jizya tax on Hindus.
Q.229. Taj Mahal was built by: Ans: Shah Jahan (built 1632-1653, in memory of his wife Mumtaz Mahal, at Agra on banks of Yamuna)
Explanation: Took 22 years, 20,000 workers. Made of white Makrana marble. Architect: Ustad Ahmad Lahauri. Cost: ~32 million rupees (then). It's a UNESCO World Heritage Site and one of the New Seven Wonders of the World. Mumtaz died during birth of 14th child.
Trick: "Taj Mahal = Shah Jahan = Mumtaz = Agra = 1632-1653." Shah Jahan was the greatest Mughal builder (also built Red Fort Delhi, Jama Masjid Delhi, Peacock Throne). He was later imprisoned by his son Aurangzeb in Agra Fort (could see Taj from his prison window).
Q.230. The last Mughal Emperor was: Ans: Bahadur Shah Zafar II (ruled 1837-1857, deposed by British after 1857 revolt, exiled to Rangoon/Myanmar where he died in 1862)
Explanation: By his time, Mughal Empire was just Delhi city. He was a puppet of the British. During 1857 revolt, rebels declared him their leader (symbolic). After revolt failed, British exiled him to Rangoon. He was also a famous Urdu poet. His exile ended 331 years of Mughal rule.
Trick: "Bahadur Shah Zafar = last Mughal = 1857 = exiled to Rangoon." He wrote: "Kitna hai badnaseeb Zafar dafn ke liye, do gaz zameen bhi na mili koo-e-yaar mein" (How unfortunate is Zafar, couldn't get even 2 yards of land in his beloved city for burial). Died in exile, buried in Myanmar.

2.3 Modern India - Freedom Movement

Q.231. The Battle of Plassey (1757) was fought between: Ans: British East India Company (Robert Clive) vs Siraj-ud-Daulah (Nawab of Bengal)
Explanation: Clive bribed Siraj's general Mir Jafar, who betrayed Siraj during battle. British won easily. Mir Jafar became puppet Nawab. This battle gave British control over Bengal's wealth — considered the beginning of British political rule in India. No real fighting — it was a conspiracy.
Trick: "Plassey 1757 = British rule begins = betrayal by Mir Jafar." Plassey (Palashi) is in West Bengal. After this: Battle of Buxar (1764) was the real military victory that confirmed British supremacy. Plassey = conspiracy, Buxar = actual battle.
Q.232. The Revolt of 1857 started from: Ans: Meerut (May 10, 1857) — Mangal Pandey triggered it at Barrackpore (March 29, 1857)
Explanation: Immediate cause: greased cartridges (cow/pig fat — offended both Hindus and Muslims). Mangal Pandey fired first shot at Barrackpore but the actual revolt started at Meerut when sepoys marched to Delhi. They declared Bahadur Shah Zafar as Emperor. Spread across North/Central India.
Trick: "1857: Mangal Pandey = spark (Barrackpore, March). Meerut = fire (May 10)." Key leaders: Rani Lakshmibai (Jhansi), Tantia Tope, Nana Sahib (Kanpur), Kunwar Singh (Bihar), Bahadur Shah Zafar (Delhi). Called: Sepoy Mutiny (British), First War of Independence (Indians).
Q.233. Indian National Congress was founded in: Ans: 1885 by Allan Octavian Hume (retired British ICS officer). First session at Bombay (Gokuldas Tejpal Sanskrit College), presided by W.C. Bonnerjee
Explanation: Hume founded INC as a "safety valve" to channel Indian discontent peacefully. 72 delegates attended first session. Early Congress was moderate — petitions, prayers, constitutional methods. Later split into Moderates (Gokhale) and Extremists (Tilak).
Trick: "INC = 1885 = Hume = Bombay = Bonnerjee." First 20 years = Moderate phase (prayer, petition, protest). 1905 onwards = Extremist phase (Tilak, Lajpat Rai, Bipin Chandra Pal — "Lal-Bal-Pal"). Surat Split (1907) divided Congress.
Q.234. The Partition of Bengal was done in: Ans: 1905 by Lord Curzon (Viceroy) — annulled in 1911 by Lord Hardinge
Explanation: Curzon divided Bengal into East Bengal (Muslim majority, capital Dhaka) and West Bengal (Hindu majority). Official reason: administrative efficiency. Real reason: divide Hindu-Muslim unity. Triggered massive Swadeshi and Boycott movements. Annulled in 1911 due to protests.
Trick: "1905 = Partition of Bengal = Curzon = Swadeshi Movement born." It backfired on British — united Indians against them. Vande Mataram became national song during this movement. Bengal was reunited in 1911 but capital shifted from Calcutta to Delhi.
Q.235. Swadeshi Movement started in: Ans: 1905 (as protest against Partition of Bengal)
Explanation: "Swadeshi" = own country's goods. People boycotted British goods (burned foreign cloth) and promoted Indian products. First mass movement in India. Led to growth of Indian industries. Also promoted national education (National Council of Education, 1906).
Trick: "Swadeshi = 1905 = anti-Bengal partition = boycott British goods." This was India's first economic nationalism. Leaders: Tilak, Aurobindo, Bipin Chandra Pal. Methods: boycott, national education, self-reliance. It inspired later movements (Non-Cooperation, Quit India).
Q.236. Muslim League was founded in: Ans: 1906 at Dhaka (by Aga Khan, Nawab Salimullah of Dhaka)
Explanation: Founded to protect Muslim political interests. Initially supported British (got separate electorate in 1909). Later demanded Pakistan (1940 Lahore Resolution). Jinnah became leader in 1913. Two-Nation Theory led to partition of India in 1947.
Trick: "Muslim League = 1906 = Dhaka." Timeline: 1906 (founded) → 1916 (Lucknow Pact with Congress) → 1940 (Pakistan Resolution) → 1947 (Pakistan created). Jinnah was initially in Congress, joined League in 1913, became its permanent president.
Q.237. Morley-Minto Reforms (1909) introduced: Ans: Separate electorate for Muslims (Indian Councils Act, 1909)
Explanation: Muslims could now vote only for Muslim candidates in reserved constituencies. This "divide and rule" policy sowed seeds of communalism. Lord Minto (Viceroy) and John Morley (Secretary of State) introduced it. Congress opposed it; Muslim League supported it.
Trick: "Morley-Minto 1909 = Separate Electorate = communal divide." This was the British strategy: keep Hindus and Muslims fighting each other. It eventually led to partition. Separate electorate continued until independence (Communal Award 1932, Poona Pact 1932).
Q.238. Home Rule Movement was started by: Ans: Bal Gangadhar Tilak (April 1916, Pune) and Annie Besant (September 1916, Madras)
Explanation: Demanded self-governance (Home Rule) within British Empire — like Ireland's Home Rule movement. Two separate leagues: Tilak's (Maharashtra, Karnataka, Central Provinces) and Besant's (rest of India). United Indians across regions. Besant was arrested — made her more popular.
Trick: "Home Rule = 1916 = Tilak + Annie Besant." Two leagues, same goal. Tilak: "Swaraj is my birthright and I shall have it!" Besant: Irish-born theosophist who loved India. Movement ended when Montagu-Chelmsford reforms were announced (1918).
Q.239. Jallianwala Bagh Massacre occurred on: Ans: April 13, 1919 (Baisakhi day) — General Dyer ordered firing on unarmed crowd at Amritsar, Punjab
Explanation: People gathered peacefully to protest Rowlatt Act (allowed detention without trial). General Dyer blocked the only exit and fired for 10 minutes. ~1000+ killed (official: 379), 1200+ wounded. Rabindranath Tagore returned his knighthood in protest. Dyer was never punished criminally.
Trick: "Jallianwala Bagh = April 13, 1919 = Dyer = Amritsar." Consequences: Tagore returned knighthood, Gandhi started Non-Cooperation Movement, Hunter Committee investigated (called it wrong but Dyer wasn't punished). Udham Singh assassinated Michael O'Dwyer (Punjab Lt. Governor) in London in 1940 as revenge.
Q.240. Non-Cooperation Movement was launched in: Ans: 1920 by Mahatma Gandhi (withdrawn in February 1922 after Chauri Chaura incident)
Explanation: First mass movement led by Gandhi. People: returned titles, boycotted courts/schools/elections, burned foreign cloth, resigned from government jobs. Chauri Chaura (UP): mob burned police station killing 22 policemen. Gandhi immediately withdrew movement saying people weren't ready for non-violence.
Trick: "Non-Cooperation = 1920-1922 = Gandhi's first big movement." Reasons: Jallianwala Bagh + Khilafat issue (Muslim support). Chauri Chaura (Feb 5, 1922) = violent incident that ended it. Gandhi said: "I'd rather be called a coward than lead a violent movement."
Q.241. Simon Commission visited India in: Ans: 1928 (all-white British commission to review India's constitutional progress — boycotted with slogan 'Simon Go Back')
Explanation: No Indian member in the commission — seen as insult. Massive protests across India. Lala Lajpat Rai was injured in lathi charge during protest in Lahore (died later — "Sher-e-Punjab"). Bhagat Singh avenged his death by killing British officer Saunders.
Trick: "Simon Commission = 1928 = no Indian member = Simon Go Back." Lajpat Rai's death → Bhagat Singh killed Saunders (1928) → Bhagat Singh threw bomb in Assembly (1929) → arrested → hanged (March 23, 1931). Chain of events from Simon Commission.
Q.242. Dandi March (Salt Satyagraha) was in: Ans: March 12 to April 6, 1930 (Gandhi walked 388 km from Sabarmati Ashram to Dandi, Gujarat)
Explanation: Gandhi chose salt tax as the issue — it affected every Indian (rich and poor). He walked 24 days with 78 followers. On April 6, he picked up natural salt from the seashore, breaking the salt law. This sparked Civil Disobedience Movement across India. Thousands were arrested.
Trick: "Dandi March = March 12, 1930 = 388 km = 24 days = salt." Why salt? Everyone uses it, tax was unjust, easy to understand. Gandhi's genius: chose a simple issue that united all Indians. 78 marchers initially, millions joined later. It got worldwide media attention.
Q.243. Civil Disobedience Movement was launched in: Ans: 1930 (started with Dandi March, suspended after Gandhi-Irwin Pact 1931, resumed 1932, ended 1934)
Explanation: People broke unjust laws openly and accepted punishment. Salt laws broken everywhere. Forest laws violated. No-tax campaigns. Women participated massively for first time. Gandhi-Irwin Pact (1931): Gandhi agreed to attend Round Table Conference; government released prisoners.
Trick: "CDM = 1930-1934." Different from Non-Cooperation (1920-22): NCM = don't cooperate (passive). CDM = actively break laws (aggressive). Gandhi went to 2nd Round Table Conference (London, 1931) but it failed. CDM resumed and finally withdrawn in 1934.
Q.244. Quit India Movement was launched on: Ans: August 8, 1942 — Gandhi gave the call "Do or Die" (Karo ya Maro) at Bombay's Gowalia Tank Maidan
Explanation: Most intense movement. Demanded immediate British withdrawal. All top leaders arrested within hours. Leaderless masses continued: destroyed railways, telegraph lines, government buildings. British used extreme force (aerial bombing of protesters!). Lasted till 1944.
Trick: "Quit India = August 8, 1942 = Do or Die = Gowalia Tank." Also called "August Kranti" (August Revolution). Aruna Asaf Ali hoisted flag at Gowalia Tank. Underground leaders: Jayaprakash Narayan, Ram Manohar Lohia. Parallel governments formed in Satara, Ballia, Midnapore.
Q.245. INA (Indian National Army) was founded by: Ans: Captain Mohan Singh (1942, in Singapore); reorganized by Subhas Chandra Bose (1943)
Explanation: INA was formed from Indian POWs captured by Japan in Southeast Asia. Bose took over in 1943, gave calls "Delhi Chalo" and "Jai Hind." INA fought alongside Japan against British in Imphal/Kohima. Failed militarily but inspired Indian soldiers in British army to question loyalty.
Trick: "INA = Mohan Singh (founded) + Bose (made famous)." Bose's slogans: "Give me blood, I'll give you freedom," "Delhi Chalo," "Jai Hind." INA trial (Red Fort, 1945) of Shah Nawaz Khan, Dhillon, Sahgal united India. Even British Indian soldiers sympathized — hastened independence.
Q.246. Cabinet Mission came to India in: Ans: 1946 (proposed plan for transfer of power, formation of Constituent Assembly, interim government)
Explanation: Three British ministers (Pethick-Lawrence, Cripps, Alexander) came to negotiate independence. Rejected Pakistan demand but proposed a loose federation with grouped provinces. Congress and League both initially accepted, then disagreed on interpretation. Led to Direct Action Day (Aug 16, 1946) and communal riots.
Trick: "Cabinet Mission = 1946 = 3 ministers = Constituent Assembly plan." It rejected Pakistan but proposed grouping of provinces (Group A, B, C). Failure of this plan made partition inevitable. Constituent Assembly was formed based on Cabinet Mission's framework.
Q.247. India got independence on: Ans: August 15, 1947 (under Indian Independence Act, 1947 passed by British Parliament on July 18, 1947)
Explanation: Lord Mountbatten (last Viceroy) announced partition plan on June 3, 1947. India and Pakistan became independent dominions. Nehru's "Tryst with Destiny" speech at midnight. Mountbatten became first Governor-General of independent India. Jinnah became Pakistan's Governor-General.
Trick: "Aug 15, 1947 = Independence." Key dates: June 3 (Mountbatten Plan), July 18 (Independence Act passed), Aug 14 (Pakistan independent), Aug 15 (India independent). Radcliffe Line divided India-Pakistan (drawn in 5 weeks by someone who'd never been to India!).
Q.248. Mountbatten Plan was announced on: Ans: June 3, 1947 (plan for partition of India into India and Pakistan)
Explanation: Also called "June 3rd Plan" or "Dickie Bird Plan." Proposed: (1) India divided into India and Pakistan. (2) Bengal and Punjab divided. (3) Princely states free to join either. (4) Boundary commission (Radcliffe) to draw borders. Both Congress and League accepted.
Trick: "June 3, 1947 = Mountbatten Plan = partition confirmed." Mountbatten advanced the date from June 1948 to August 1947 (10 months early!) — many believe this haste caused more violence during partition. 10-15 million displaced, 1-2 million killed.
Q.249. Who gave the slogan 'Swaraj is my birthright'? Ans: Bal Gangadhar Tilak
Explanation: Full quote: "Swaraj is my birthright and I shall have it!" Tilak was the first leader to demand complete self-rule (not just reforms). He was called "Lokmanya" (accepted by people) and "Father of Indian Unrest" (by British). He started Ganesh Chaturthi and Shivaji festivals to unite people.
Trick: "Tilak = Swaraj is my birthright = Lokmanya = Extremist leader." Other famous slogans: "Inquilab Zindabad" = Bhagat Singh. "Jai Hind" = Bose. "Do or Die" = Gandhi. "Vande Mataram" = Bankim Chandra (from Anandamath novel). "Jai Jawan Jai Kisan" = Lal Bahadur Shastri.
Q.250. Who gave the slogan 'Jai Hind'? Ans: Subhas Chandra Bose
Explanation: "Jai Hind" = "Victory to India." Bose used it as INA's greeting/war cry. He also gave: "Give me blood, I'll give you freedom" and "Delhi Chalo" (Onward to Delhi). Bose was called "Netaji" (respected leader). He escaped British India, went to Germany and Japan to seek help for Indian independence.
Trick: Bose's slogans: "Jai Hind," "Delhi Chalo," "Give me blood..." He formed Azad Hind Government (Free India Government) in Singapore (1943). Died mysteriously in a plane crash (Aug 18, 1945, Taiwan) — still debated. His legacy: proved Indians could fight for freedom militarily.

2.4 Important Acts & Reforms

Q.251. Regulating Act was passed in: Ans: 1773 — first step by British Parliament to regulate East India Company
Explanation: After Company's corruption became scandalous, Parliament intervened. Key provisions: (1) Governor of Bengal became Governor-General (Warren Hastings = first). (2) Supreme Court established at Calcutta. (3) Company's political activities came under Parliament's oversight.
Trick: "1773 = Regulating Act = first British control over Company." It's the BEGINNING of constitutional history of India. Before this, Company was purely commercial. After this, it became political. Warren Hastings = first Governor-General of Bengal.
Q.252. Pitt's India Act was passed in: Ans: 1784 — established dual government (Board of Control + Court of Directors)
Explanation: Created "double government": Board of Control (British government, handled political affairs) + Court of Directors (Company, handled commercial affairs). This gave British government direct control over Company's Indian policies while Company kept trade profits.
Trick: "Pitt's Act 1784 = Dual Government." Named after PM William Pitt. Think: "Pitt = Politics + Trade split." Board of Control = government's eyes on Company. This system lasted until 1858 (when Company was abolished after 1857 revolt).
Q.253. Charter Act of 1833 made: Ans: Governor-General of Bengal into Governor-General of INDIA (first was Lord William Bentinck)
Explanation: Centralized British administration. Governor-General now controlled all of British India (not just Bengal). Also: ended Company's commercial activities (became purely administrative), opened civil services to Indians (in theory). Lord Bentinck = first GG of India.
Trick: "1833 = GG of Bengal → GG of India = Bentinck." Also: Company lost trade monopoly (became only administrator). Key: 1833 is when British India became ONE administrative unit under one head.
Q.254. Indian Councils Act 1861 introduced: Ans: Portfolio system, Indian representation in Viceroy's council, and decentralization
Explanation: After 1857 revolt, British realized they needed Indian cooperation. This Act: (1) Added Indians to legislative councils (nominated, not elected). (2) Introduced portfolio system (each member handles a department). (3) Gave legislative powers to Bombay and Madras presidencies.
Trick: "1861 = Indians in councils (first time!) = post-1857 reform." It's the beginning of Indian participation in governance (even if just advisory). Three Indians nominated to Viceroy's council. Baby step toward representative government.
Q.255. Government of India Act 1919 (Montagu-Chelmsford Reforms) introduced: Ans: Dyarchy in provinces (dual government — some subjects to Indian ministers, some to British Governor)
Explanation: "Dyarchy" = two rulers. Provincial subjects divided into: Transferred (education, health — Indian ministers responsible) and Reserved (finance, police — British Governor controlled). Also introduced direct elections and expanded franchise. Failed because Indian ministers had no real power.
Trick: "1919 = Dyarchy = Montagu-Chelmsford." Transferred subjects = less important (education, health). Reserved = important (money, police). Indian ministers were responsible but powerless — Governor could overrule them. Congress called it "inadequate and disappointing."
Q.256. Government of India Act 1935 introduced: Ans: Provincial autonomy, Federal Court, All India Federation (federation part never implemented), bicameral legislatures in some provinces
Explanation: Most detailed Act (321 sections!). Abolished dyarchy in provinces — gave full autonomy. Introduced dyarchy at Centre (never implemented). Created Federal Court (predecessor of Supreme Court). RBI established under this Act. Formed basis of India's Constitution.
Trick: "1935 = Provincial Autonomy = basis of our Constitution." 75% of Indian Constitution is derived from this Act! Key: Federation never came into being because princely states refused to join. Provincial part implemented in 1937 elections (Congress won 8 of 11 provinces).
Q.257. Rowlatt Act (1919) was also known as: Ans: "Black Act" — allowed detention without trial, no appeal, no lawyer
Explanation: Passed despite unanimous Indian opposition in council. Gave government power to arrest anyone without warrant, detain without trial, and try without jury. Gandhi called it "unjust, subversive of principles of liberty." Led to Jallianwala Bagh massacre (protest against this Act).
Trick: "Rowlatt Act = Black Act = no vakeel, no daleel, no appeal" (no lawyer, no argument, no appeal). This phrase captures its essence. Gandhi's first all-India protest (hartal on April 6, 1919) was against this Act. It was never actually used and was repealed in 1922.
Q.258. Communal Award (1932) was given by: Ans: British PM Ramsay MacDonald — gave separate electorates to depressed classes (Dalits), Muslims, Sikhs, Christians
Explanation: Extended separate electorate (which Muslims already had) to Dalits. Gandhi opposed this fiercely — said it would permanently divide Hindu society. He went on fast unto death in Yerwada Jail. This forced Ambedkar to negotiate, leading to Poona Pact.
Trick: "Communal Award 1932 = MacDonald = separate electorate for Dalits." Gandhi's fast forced Ambedkar to accept Poona Pact (reserved seats within joint electorate instead of separate electorate). This is a crucial Gandhi-Ambedkar episode for exams.
Q.259. Poona Pact (1932) was between: Ans: Gandhi and Ambedkar — replaced separate electorates with reserved seats for depressed classes within joint Hindu electorate
Explanation: Ambedkar wanted separate electorates (Dalits vote only for Dalit candidates). Gandhi said this would divide Hindus permanently. Gandhi fasted unto death. Ambedkar agreed to reserved seats (Dalits can vote for all + have reserved constituencies). Reserved seats increased from 71 to 148.
Trick: "Poona Pact = Gandhi vs Ambedkar = reserved seats (not separate electorate)." This is the foundation of SC/ST reservation in legislatures today. Ambedkar later said he regretted signing it under pressure of Gandhi's fast. The debate continues.
Q.260. Cripps Mission (1942) proposed: Ans: Dominion Status after World War II ended (rejected by both Congress and Muslim League)
Explanation: Sir Stafford Cripps came during WWII to get Indian support for war effort. Offered: Dominion Status after war, Constituent Assembly, provinces could opt out. Congress rejected (wanted immediate self-rule). League rejected (didn't guarantee Pakistan). Gandhi called it "a post-dated cheque on a crashing bank."
Trick: "Cripps 1942 = post-dated cheque = rejected by all." It failed because: (1) No immediate transfer of power. (2) Defence remained with British. (3) Provinces could secede (Congress opposed). After Cripps' failure, Gandhi launched Quit India Movement (Aug 1942).

2.5 Social Reform Movements

Q.261. Brahmo Samaj was founded by: Ans: Raja Ram Mohan Roy (1828) in Calcutta
Explanation: Brahmo Samaj = "Society of God." Opposed idol worship, caste system, sati, child marriage. Promoted monotheism (one God), women's education, widow remarriage. Ram Mohan Roy is called "Father of Indian Renaissance" and "Father of Modern India."
Trick: "Brahmo Samaj = Ram Mohan Roy = 1828 = Calcutta = reform Hinduism." He fought against sati (abolished 1829), promoted English education, started newspapers (Sambad Kaumudi in Bengali, Mirat-ul-Akhbar in Persian). He's the FIRST modern Indian reformer.
Q.262. Arya Samaj was founded by: Ans: Swami Dayananda Saraswati (1875, Bombay) — motto: "Back to the Vedas"
Explanation: Unlike Brahmo Samaj (which was liberal/Western), Arya Samaj was revivalist — wanted to return to Vedic Hinduism. Opposed idol worship, caste by birth (supported caste by merit), child marriage. Promoted Shuddhi (reconversion) and Hindi. Founded DAV schools/colleges.
Trick: "Arya Samaj = Dayananda = 1875 = Back to Vedas." Key difference from Brahmo Samaj: Brahmo = reform through Western ideas. Arya = reform through ancient Vedic ideas. Dayananda wrote "Satyarth Prakash" (Light of Truth). DAV = Dayanand Anglo-Vedic schools.
Q.263. Ramakrishna Mission was founded by: Ans: Swami Vivekananda (1897, after returning from Chicago World Parliament of Religions, 1893)
Explanation: Named after his guru Ramakrishna Paramahamsa. Combines spiritual training with social service (education, healthcare, disaster relief). Vivekananda's Chicago speech ("Sisters and Brothers of America") made Hinduism known worldwide. Headquarters: Belur Math, Kolkata.
Trick: "Ramakrishna Mission = Vivekananda = 1897 = service + spirituality." Vivekananda said: "Arise, awake, and stop not till the goal is reached." He introduced Hinduism to the West. Died young at 39 (1902). His birthday (Jan 12) = National Youth Day.
Q.264. Sati was abolished by: Ans: Lord William Bentinck (1829, Regulation XVII) — due to efforts of Raja Ram Mohan Roy
Explanation: Sati = widow burning herself on husband's funeral pyre. Ram Mohan Roy campaigned against it for years, showing it wasn't in Vedas. Bentinck (Governor-General) made it illegal. First major social reform by British in India. Ram Mohan Roy used both Hindu scriptures and Western rationalism to argue against it.
Trick: "Sati abolished = 1829 = Bentinck + Ram Mohan Roy." Ram Mohan Roy's own sister-in-law was burned — this motivated him. He proved from Vedas/Upanishads that sati was NOT a religious requirement. British were initially reluctant (feared religious backlash) but Roy gave them confidence.
Q.265. Widow Remarriage Act was passed in: Ans: 1856 — due to efforts of Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar
Explanation: Hindu widows were forbidden from remarrying — condemned to a life of suffering. Vidyasagar proved from Hindu scriptures that remarriage was allowed. He personally organized widow remarriages and faced social boycott. His own son married a widow.
Trick: "Widow Remarriage = 1856 = Vidyasagar." He was a Bengali scholar ("Vidyasagar" = ocean of knowledge). Also promoted women's education and opposed child marriage. He's one of Bengal's greatest reformers alongside Ram Mohan Roy.
Q.266. Theosophical Society in India was led by: Ans: Annie Besant (headquarters at Adyar, Chennai)
Explanation: Theosophical Society (founded 1875 by Blavatsky and Olcott in USA) promoted universal brotherhood and study of ancient religions. Annie Besant (Irish) came to India in 1893, revived Hindu pride, started Home Rule Movement (1916), became INC President (1917).
Trick: "Theosophy = Annie Besant = Adyar (Chennai)." She was unique: Irish woman who became Indian freedom fighter. Founded Central Hindu College (later became BHU). Started "New India" newspaper. First woman INC President (1917).
Q.267. Aligarh Movement was started by: Ans: Sir Syed Ahmed Khan
Explanation: After 1857 revolt, Muslims were worst affected (British blamed them most). Sir Syed worked to modernize Muslim education through Western learning. Founded MAO College (1875) which became Aligarh Muslim University (1920). He opposed Congress and promoted Muslim loyalty to British.
Trick: "Aligarh Movement = Sir Syed = Muslim modernization." He said: "Muslims should get Western education first, politics later." Founded Scientific Society, wrote "Causes of Indian Revolt." Controversial: opposed Congress, promoted two-nation theory seeds. AMU is his lasting legacy.
Q.268. Servants of India Society was founded by: Ans: Gopal Krishna Gokhale (1905, Pune)
Explanation: A secular organization dedicated to serving India through education, sanitation, and social reform. Members took vows of poverty and service. Gandhi considered Gokhale his "political guru." Gokhale was a Moderate leader who believed in constitutional methods.
Trick: "Servants of India = Gokhale = 1905." Gokhale = Moderate, constitutional methods, mentor of Gandhi. Tilak = Extremist, aggressive methods. Both were from Pune but had opposite approaches. Gandhi took the best of both.
Q.269. Who is called the 'Father of Indian Renaissance'? Ans: Raja Ram Mohan Roy
Explanation: "Renaissance" = rebirth/awakening. Ram Mohan Roy awakened India from social evils through reason and reform. He fought sati, promoted women's education, English education, press freedom, and monotheism. He bridged Eastern and Western thought.
Trick: Ram Mohan Roy's titles: "Father of Indian Renaissance," "Father of Modern India," "Herald of New Age." He founded Brahmo Samaj (1828), Atmiya Sabha (1815). First Indian to visit England (died in Bristol, 1833). Started first Bengali newspaper.
Q.270. Satyashodhak Samaj was founded by: Ans: Jyotirao Phule (1873, Pune) — for upliftment of lower castes and women
Explanation: "Satyashodhak" = truth-seekers. Phule fought against Brahmin dominance and caste discrimination. He and his wife Savitribai opened India's first school for girls (1848) and for untouchables. He coined the term "Dalit." Ambedkar considered him a guru.
Trick: "Phule = Satyashodhak Samaj = 1873 = anti-caste." Savitribai Phule = India's first female teacher. Jyotirao wrote "Gulamgiri" (Slavery, 1873). He's the pioneer of social justice movement in India. Maharashtra celebrates him as a great reformer.

2.6 Telangana in History

Q.271. The Satavahana dynasty ruled from: Ans: Pratishthana (Paithan, Maharashtra) and later Amaravati (Andhra Pradesh), 2nd century BCE to 3rd century CE
Explanation: Satavahanas were the first major dynasty of Deccan/South India after Mauryas. They controlled trade routes between North and South. Known for: Amaravati Stupa (Buddhist art), lead coins, bilingual inscriptions (Prakrit + Telugu). Gautamiputra Satakarni was greatest ruler.
Trick: "Satavahanas = Deccan's first empire = Amaravati." They're important for Telangana/AP history. Gautamiputra Satakarni defeated Shakas. They promoted Buddhism and trade with Romans. Amaravati stupa = finest Buddhist sculpture in India.
Q.272. The Kakatiya dynasty capital was: Ans: Warangal (originally called Orugallu = "one stone" in Telugu)
Explanation: Kakatiyas ruled Telangana region (1163-1323 CE). They built the famous Warangal Fort (with 4 ornamental gateways — Kakatiya Thoranam), Thousand Pillar Temple (Hanamkonda), Ramappa Temple (UNESCO World Heritage Site). They promoted Telugu language and culture.
Trick: "Kakatiyas = Warangal = Telangana's golden age." Key monuments: Warangal Fort, Thousand Pillar Temple, Ramappa Temple (UNESCO 2021). Kakatiya Thoranam (gateway) is Telangana's state emblem! They built many tanks/lakes for irrigation (Pakala, Ramappa, Laknavaram).
Q.273. The most famous Kakatiya ruler was: Ans: Prataparudra II (also notable: Ganapati Deva and Rudrama Devi)
Explanation: Ganapati Deva (1199-1262) expanded the kingdom to its greatest extent. Rudrama Devi (1262-1289) was one of India's few women rulers. Prataparudra II (1289-1323) was the last ruler — defeated by Delhi Sultanate's Malik Kafur and later Ulugh Khan.
Trick: "Kakatiya rulers: Ganapati → Rudrama Devi → Prataparudra II." Ganapati = expansion. Rudrama Devi = woman warrior queen. Prataparudra = last king (defeated by Tughlaq forces, 1323). Marco Polo mentioned Rudrama Devi in his travels!
Q.274. Rudrama Devi was: Ans: One of the few women rulers in Indian history (Kakatiya dynasty, ruled 1262-1289 CE)
Explanation: Ganapati Deva had no sons, so he raised his daughter Rudrama as a boy and made her queen. She ruled as "Rudradeva Maharaja" (male title). She fought wars, suppressed rebellions, and maintained the kingdom. Marco Polo called her a wise ruler. Died fighting a rebellion.
Trick: "Rudrama Devi = Kakatiya woman ruler = 1262-1289." Other famous women rulers in Indian history: Razia Sultan (Delhi Sultanate, 1236-1240), Rani Durgavati (Gondwana), Ahilyabai Holkar (Malwa), Rani Lakshmibai (Jhansi). Rudrama Devi is Telangana's pride.
Q.275. The Qutb Shahi dynasty ruled from: Ans: Golconda/Hyderabad (1518-1687 CE)
Explanation: Founded by Sultan Quli Qutb Shah (a Turkmen governor who declared independence from Bahmani Sultanate). Built Golconda Fort, Charminar, Mecca Masjid. Known for diamond trade (Kohinoor came from Golconda mines). Defeated by Mughal Emperor Aurangzeb in 1687.
Trick: "Qutb Shahis = Golconda = 1518-1687 = diamonds + Charminar." 7 rulers in 169 years. Muhammad Quli Qutb Shah (5th ruler) founded Hyderabad city (1591) and built Charminar. Golconda was famous worldwide for diamonds (Hope Diamond, Kohinoor originated here).
Q.276. Hyderabad city was founded by: Ans: Muhammad Quli Qutb Shah in 1591 CE
Explanation: He moved capital from crowded Golconda Fort to a new planned city on the banks of Musi river. Named it "Bhagyanagar" (after his Hindu beloved Bhagmati, later renamed Hyderabad). Built Charminar as the city's centerpiece. The city was planned with wide roads and gardens.
Trick: "Hyderabad = 1591 = Muhammad Quli Qutb Shah." Original name: Bhagyanagar (city of fortune/Bhagmati). Charminar built same year (1591) to commemorate end of plague. Musi river divides old city (south) from new city (north).
Q.277. Charminar was built by: Ans: Muhammad Quli Qutb Shah (1591) — to commemorate the end of a deadly plague epidemic
Explanation: "Char" = four, "Minar" = towers/minarets. It has 4 grand arches facing 4 directions (representing 4 pillars of Islam, or 4 Khalifas). A mosque is on the top floor. It's Hyderabad's most iconic monument and symbol of the city.
Trick: "Charminar = 4 minarets = 1591 = plague ended = Hyderabad's symbol." Each minaret is 48.7m tall. There's a legend that Quli Qutb Shah prayed at this spot during the plague and vowed to build a mosque if it ended. It did, and he built Charminar.
Q.278. The Asaf Jahi dynasty (Nizams) was founded by: Ans: Mir Qamar-ud-din (titled Nizam-ul-Mulk Asaf Jah) in 1724 CE
Explanation: He was a Mughal governor of Deccan who declared independence as Mughal Empire weakened. The Nizam dynasty ruled Hyderabad State for 224 years (1724-1948). They were among the richest rulers in the world. 7 Nizams ruled in total.
Trick: "Asaf Jahi/Nizams = 1724-1948 = 7 Nizams = 224 years." They were technically Mughal vassals but practically independent. Hyderabad State was the largest princely state in India (area of 82,698 sq miles). Last Nizam was the richest man in the world at one point.
Q.279. Hyderabad State was merged with Indian Union through: Ans: Operation Polo (Police Action) on September 17, 1948
Explanation: After independence, Nizam wanted to remain independent or join Pakistan. India sent army (Operation Polo, led by Major General J.N. Chaudhuri). Nizam surrendered in 5 days. September 17 is celebrated as "Telangana Liberation Day" / "Hyderabad Merger Day."
Trick: "Operation Polo = Sep 17, 1948 = Hyderabad merged." Why "Polo"? Hyderabad had the most polo grounds in India! Sardar Patel ordered the action. It ended the Razakar (Nizam's militia) atrocities. Sep 17 = Telangana Liberation Day (state holiday).
Q.280. The last Nizam of Hyderabad was: Ans: Mir Osman Ali Khan (7th and last Nizam, ruled 1911-1948)
Explanation: He was once the richest man in the world (featured on TIME magazine cover, 1937). Despite immense wealth, he was famously miserly (wore the same fez cap for 35 years!). He donated generously to institutions (Osmania University, hospitals). After merger, he became Rajpramukh (ceremonial head) of Hyderabad State.
Trick: "Osman Ali Khan = 7th Nizam = richest man = last Nizam." He founded Osmania University (1918), built Osman Sagar and Himayat Sagar dams. His wealth: Jacob Diamond (185 carats) used as paperweight! After 1948, he cooperated with India and was given privy purse.

2.7 Important Personalities & Contributions

Q.281. Who is known as 'Grand Old Man of India'? Ans: Dadabhai Naoroji
Explanation: Dadabhai Naoroji (1825-1917) was one of the earliest Indian political leaders. He was the first Indian to be elected to British Parliament (1892, Liberal Party, Finsbury Central). He exposed British economic exploitation through his "Drain Theory." Three-time INC President.
Trick: "Dadabhai = Grand Old Man = Drain Theory = first Indian in British Parliament." He proved that Britain was draining India's wealth (estimated £200-300 million annually). His book: "Poverty and Un-British Rule in India." He lived to 92 — hence "Grand Old Man."
Q.282. Who propounded the 'Drain Theory'? Ans: Dadabhai Naoroji (in his book 'Poverty and Un-British Rule in India', 1901)
Explanation: Drain Theory = British were systematically transferring India's wealth to Britain through: (1) salaries of British officials, (2) home charges, (3) profits of British companies, (4) interest on debt. India got nothing in return. This "drain" caused India's poverty.
Trick: "Drain Theory = Naoroji = economic nationalism." Other economic critics: R.C. Dutt ("Economic History of India"), M.G. Ranade. They proved India was rich BEFORE British and became poor BECAUSE of British policies. This economic critique united Indians against colonial rule.
Q.283. Who is known as 'Frontier Gandhi'? Ans: Khan Abdul Ghaffar Khan (also called "Badshah Khan")
Explanation: A Pashtun leader from NWFP (now Pakistan) who followed Gandhi's non-violence despite being from a warrior community. Founded "Khudai Khidmatgar" (Servants of God) — a non-violent army of 100,000 Pashtuns! Opposed partition. Spent more years in jail than any other freedom fighter.
Trick: "Frontier Gandhi = Ghaffar Khan = Pashtun non-violence." He proved non-violence works even among warriors. Opposed Pakistan's creation but was trapped there after partition. Awarded Bharat Ratna (1987) — first non-Indian citizen to receive it. Died in Peshawar (1988).
Q.284. Who founded the Forward Bloc? Ans: Subhas Chandra Bose (1939, after resigning as INC President)
Explanation: Bose won INC presidency (1938, 1939) against Gandhi's candidate. Gandhi opposed him, so Bose resigned and formed Forward Bloc — a left-wing party within Congress. He wanted armed revolution, not just non-violence. Later escaped India (1941) to seek foreign help for independence.
Trick: "Forward Bloc = Bose = 1939 = left-wing." Bose vs Gandhi: Bose wanted aggressive action + foreign help. Gandhi wanted non-violence + self-reliance. Both wanted independence but disagreed on methods. Forward Bloc still exists as a political party (allied with Left Front).
Q.285. Who gave the slogan 'Inquilab Zindabad'? Ans: Bhagat Singh popularized it (originally coined by Maulana Hasrat Mohani in 1921)
Explanation: "Inquilab Zindabad" = "Long Live the Revolution!" Bhagat Singh shouted it while throwing bombs in Central Legislative Assembly (April 8, 1929). He wanted to "make the deaf hear" — the bombs were harmless (smoke bombs). He was arrested, tried, and hanged (March 23, 1931, age 23).
