Trick: "Inquilab Zindabad = Bhagat Singh (popularized) = Hasrat Mohani (coined)." Bhagat Singh also said: "Revolution is an inalienable right of mankind." He was an atheist, socialist, and intellectual — not just a bomb-thrower. Read his jail diary and "Why I Am an Atheist."
Q.286. Who is known as 'Iron Man of India'? Ans: Sardar Vallabhbhai Patel
Explanation: Patel integrated 562 princely states into India after independence — a monumental task done through diplomacy and (rarely) force (Hyderabad, Junagadh). Without him, India would have been fragmented into hundreds of pieces. He was India's first Deputy PM and Home Minister.
Trick: "Patel = Iron Man = integrated princely states = Statue of Unity." Statue of Unity (Gujarat, 182m) is world's tallest statue — dedicated to Patel. His birthday (Oct 31) = National Unity Day (Rashtriya Ekta Diwas). He's called "Bismarck of India" (like Germany's unifier).
Q.287. Who is known as 'Nightingale of India'? Ans: Sarojini Naidu
Explanation: A poet and freedom fighter. Called "Nightingale" for her beautiful poetry in English ("The Golden Threshold," "The Bird of Time"). First Indian woman INC President (1925). First woman Governor of a state (UP, 1947). Active in Salt Satyagraha — led raid on Dharasana Salt Works.
Trick: "Sarojini Naidu = Nightingale = poet + politician." Firsts: First Indian woman INC President (1925), First woman Governor (UP, 1947). She was witty — once told Gandhi: "Do you know how much it costs to keep you in poverty?" (referring to his simple lifestyle's logistics).
Q.288. Who wrote 'Hind Swaraj'? Ans: Mahatma Gandhi (1909, written on a ship from London to South Africa)
Explanation: "Hind Swaraj" = "Indian Self-Rule." Gandhi's manifesto criticizing Western civilization, modern machinery, railways, lawyers, doctors. He argued true freedom is self-discipline, not just political independence. Written in Gujarati in just 10 days on the ship.
Trick: "Hind Swaraj = Gandhi = 1909 = critique of Western civilization." It's Gandhi's most controversial book — he rejected modernity itself. He said: "India's salvation lies in unlearning what it has learned in the last 50 years." Many disagreed but it defined his philosophy.
Q.289. Who wrote 'Discovery of India'? Ans: Jawaharlal Nehru (written in Ahmednagar Fort jail, 1944)
Explanation: Nehru wrote it during his imprisonment in Quit India Movement. It traces India's history from Indus Valley to independence movement. Shows Nehru's love for Indian culture and his vision of a modern, scientific India. Also wrote: "Glimpses of World History" and "An Autobiography."
Trick: Nehru's books (all written in jail!): "Discovery of India" (1944), "Glimpses of World History" (1934), "An Autobiography/Toward Freedom" (1936). "Letters from a Father to His Daughter" (1929) — written to Indira Gandhi. Nehru spent ~9 years total in British jails.
Q.290. Who wrote 'Annihilation of Caste'? Ans: Dr. B.R. Ambedkar (1936)
Explanation: Originally written as a speech for a Hindu reform conference (Jat-Pat Todak Mandal, Lahore) — but they cancelled his invitation after reading it! So Ambedkar published it himself. It's a devastating critique of the caste system and Hindu social order. Gandhi responded with "A Vindication of Caste" — Ambedkar demolished his arguments.
Trick: "Annihilation of Caste = Ambedkar = 1936 = anti-caste masterpiece." Other Ambedkar works: "Who Were the Shudras?" "The Buddha and His Dhamma." He converted to Buddhism (Oct 14, 1956) with 600,000 followers — rejecting Hinduism's caste system. Died Dec 6, 1956.
Q.291. The first Indian to become member of British Parliament was: Ans: Dadabhai Naoroji (1892, elected from Finsbury Central, London, Liberal Party)
Explanation: Won by just 5 votes! He used his position to raise India's issues in British Parliament. He was 67 years old when elected. Served 1892-1895. This showed Indians could compete in Western democratic systems.
Trick: "Naoroji = first Indian in British Parliament = 1892." He won by 5 votes — closest margin! PM Salisbury had said "a black man" can't win in England — Naoroji proved him wrong. Also: first Indian to demand "Swaraj" (self-rule) in INC session (1906, Calcutta).
Q.292. Who founded the Ghadar Party? Ans: Lala Har Dayal (1913, San Francisco, USA)
Explanation: "Ghadar" = mutiny/revolution. Founded by Indian immigrants in USA/Canada who wanted armed revolution against British. Published "Ghadar" newspaper in Urdu, Punjabi, Hindi. Planned uprising in India during WWI (1915) but it was crushed. Members were mostly Punjabi Sikhs.
Trick: "Ghadar Party = 1913 = San Francisco = Har Dayal = armed revolution from abroad." They tried to send arms and revolutionaries to India during WWI. Komagata Maru incident (1914) — ship of Indians denied entry to Canada — fueled Ghadar anger. Many members were hanged/imprisoned.
Q.293. Champaran Satyagraha (1917) was Gandhi's first: Ans: Civil disobedience movement in India (against indigo planters in Bihar who exploited farmers)
Explanation: Farmers in Champaran (Bihar) were forced to grow indigo on 3/20th of their land (Tinkathia system) for British planters. Gandhi went there, investigated, and used Satyagraha. British appointed an inquiry committee — Gandhi was a member. Tinkathia system was abolished.
Trick: "Champaran 1917 = Gandhi's first Satyagraha in India = indigo = Bihar." Gandhi's India Satyagrahas in order: Champaran (1917, Bihar) → Kheda (1918, Gujarat, crop failure) → Ahmedabad Mill Strike (1918, workers' wages). These three established Gandhi as India's leader before national movements.
Q.294. Khilafat Movement (1919-1924) was led by: Ans: Ali Brothers — Mohammad Ali and Shaukat Ali
Explanation: After WWI, British dismembered Ottoman Empire (Turkey). Indian Muslims protested because Ottoman Sultan was Caliph (Khalifa) of Islam. Gandhi supported Khilafat to unite Hindus and Muslims. It merged with Non-Cooperation Movement (1920). Ended when Turkey itself abolished Caliphate (1924).
Trick: "Khilafat = Ali Brothers = 1919-1924 = Hindu-Muslim unity." Gandhi's masterstroke: by supporting Muslim cause, he got Muslim support for Non-Cooperation. But unity was temporary — it collapsed after Khilafat ended. Moplah Rebellion (1921, Kerala) was a dark side of this movement.
Q.295. Who gave the title 'Mahatma' to Gandhi? Ans: Rabindranath Tagore
Explanation: "Mahatma" = "Great Soul." Tagore used this title for Gandhi in 1915 when Gandhi returned from South Africa. Some scholars debate this — some say Nautamlal Bhagwanji Mehta first used it. But Tagore popularized it. Gandhi himself disliked the title — said it was a burden.
Trick: "Tagore gave 'Mahatma' to Gandhi. Gandhi gave 'Gurudev' to Tagore." Mutual respect between two giants. Tagore also gave title "Deshbandhu" to C.R. Das. Gandhi called Gokhale his "political guru."
Q.296. Who gave the title 'Gurudev' to Tagore? Ans: Mahatma Gandhi
Explanation: "Gurudev" = "Divine Teacher." Gandhi respected Tagore as India's greatest intellectual and poet. Despite disagreements (Tagore criticized Non-Cooperation as narrow nationalism; Gandhi criticized Tagore as too detached), they deeply respected each other.
Trick: "Gandhi ↔ Tagore: exchanged titles." They disagreed on many things: nationalism, spinning wheel, non-cooperation. But both wanted India's freedom and cultural renaissance. Their debates enriched Indian thought. Tagore = Nobel Prize (1913), Gandhi = never got Nobel (nominated 5 times).
Q.297. First woman President of Indian National Congress was: Ans: Annie Besant (1917, Calcutta session)
Explanation: Annie Besant was Irish-born but dedicated her life to India. She led Home Rule Movement, founded Central Hindu College (later BHU), and was a theosophist. She became INC President during WWI when Congress was demanding self-rule.
Trick: "First woman INC President = Annie Besant (1917)." "First INDIAN woman INC President = Sarojini Naidu (1925)." Don't confuse! Besant was British/Irish. Naidu was Indian. Both are important "firsts."
Q.298. First Indian woman President of INC was: Ans: Sarojini Naidu (1925, Kanpur session)
Explanation: Naidu was already famous as a poet ("Nightingale of India") and freedom fighter. She presided over the Kanpur session at age 46. She was also the first woman Governor of independent India (UP, 1947-1949).
Trick: "Sarojini Naidu = first INDIAN woman INC President = 1925 = Kanpur." Multiple firsts: first Indian woman INC President, first woman Governor. She was multilingual (English, Urdu, Telugu, Bengali) and a powerful orator.
Q.299. Vande Mataram was composed by: Ans: Bankim Chandra Chattopadhyay (from his novel "Anandamath," 1882)
Explanation: "Vande Mataram" = "I bow to thee, Mother (India)." Written in Sanskrit-Bengali mix. It became the anthem of Swadeshi Movement (1905). First sung at INC session in 1896 by Tagore. Only first 2 stanzas adopted as National Song (1950) — rest has Hindu religious imagery.
Trick: "Vande Mataram = Bankim Chandra = Anandamath = 1882." It's the NATIONAL SONG (not anthem). National Anthem = Jana Gana Mana (Tagore). National Song = Vande Mataram (Bankim). Both have equal status. Only first 2 stanzas are official (to keep it secular).
Q.300. Jana Gana Mana was composed by: Ans: Rabindranath Tagore (first sung on December 27, 1911 at INC Calcutta session)
Explanation: Written in highly Sanskritized Bengali. Adopted as National Anthem on January 24, 1950. Playing time: 52 seconds (full version, 5 stanzas). Short version (first and last lines): 20 seconds. It mentions India's diverse geography and people.
Trick: "Jana Gana Mana = Tagore = Dec 27, 1911 = National Anthem." Controversy: some say it was written for King George V's visit (1911). Tagore denied this — said it's addressed to "Bharat Bhagya Vidhata" (Dispenser of India's destiny = God, not King). 52 seconds = full, 20 seconds = short version.

2.8 Post-Independence India

Q.301. The first Five Year Plan was launched in: Ans: 1951 (based on Harrod-Domar model, focused on agriculture and irrigation)
Explanation: India adopted Soviet-style planned economy. First Plan (1951-56) prioritized agriculture (dams like Bhakra Nangal, Hirakud). Planning Commission (headed by PM) made these plans. 12 Five Year Plans total (1951-2017). NITI Aayog replaced Planning Commission in 2015.
Trick: "1st Plan = 1951 = agriculture/dams." Key plans: 1st=agriculture, 2nd=industry (Mahalanobis model), 4th=growth with stability, 8th=liberalization era. Plans ended in 2017 — now NITI Aayog makes 15-year vision documents instead.
Q.302. States Reorganisation Act was passed in: Ans: 1956 (reorganized states on linguistic basis, based on Fazl Ali Commission/States Reorganisation Commission)
Explanation: Created 14 states and 6 UTs based on language. Before this, states had arbitrary boundaries from British era. Demand started with Potti Sriramulu's death (1952, fasted for Andhra state). First linguistic state: Andhra Pradesh (1953, from Madras).
Trick: "1956 = linguistic states = Fazl Ali Commission." Potti Sriramulu's sacrifice (died fasting, Dec 1952) forced government to create Andhra. Then floodgates opened — everyone wanted linguistic states. 7th Amendment (1956) implemented the reorganization.
Q.303. Goa was liberated from Portuguese rule in: Ans: 1961 (Operation Vijay, December 19)
Explanation: Portugal refused to leave Goa even after India's independence (1947). After 14 years of diplomacy failed, India sent military (Operation Vijay). Portuguese surrendered in 36 hours. Goa became a UT (1961), then a full state (1987). Last European colony in India to be freed.
Trick: "Goa = 1961 = Operation Vijay = Portuguese." India was independent in 1947 but Goa remained Portuguese for 14 more years! French left Pondicherry in 1954 (peacefully). Portuguese had to be forced out militarily. Goa became 25th state in 1987.
Q.304. Green Revolution in India was introduced by: Ans: M.S. Swaminathan (1960s — high-yielding variety seeds, especially wheat and rice)
Explanation: India faced severe food shortages (1960s famines). Green Revolution used HYV seeds (from Norman Borlaug, Mexico), fertilizers, irrigation, and pesticides to dramatically increase food production. Punjab and Haryana led the revolution. India became food self-sufficient by 1970s.
Trick: "Green Revolution = Swaminathan = 1960s = wheat/rice = Punjab/Haryana." Norman Borlaug (Nobel Peace Prize 1970) = father of global Green Revolution. Swaminathan = father of Indian Green Revolution. Downside: soil degradation, water depletion, inequality (only benefited irrigated areas).
Q.305. White Revolution (Operation Flood) was led by: Ans: Dr. Verghese Kurien (milk production — made India world's largest milk producer)
Explanation: Operation Flood (1970-1996) created a nationwide milk grid connecting producers to consumers. Based on Amul cooperative model (Gujarat). India went from milk-deficient to world's #1 milk producer. Kurien is called "Milkman of India."
Trick: "White Revolution = Kurien = Amul = milk." Kurien founded NDDB (National Dairy Development Board) and Amul. India produces ~220 million tonnes of milk/year (world's highest). Other revolutions: Blue=fish, Yellow=oilseeds, Golden=fruits/honey, Silver=eggs, Pink=prawns/onions.
Q.306. India conducted its first nuclear test (Smiling Buddha) in: Ans: May 18, 1974 at Pokhran, Rajasthan (under PM Indira Gandhi)
Explanation: Code-named "Smiling Buddha" — India called it a "peaceful nuclear explosion." Made India the 6th country to test nuclear weapons. Led to international sanctions and creation of Nuclear Suppliers Group (to prevent proliferation). Scientist: Raja Ramanna.
Trick: "1974 = Smiling Buddha = Pokhran-I = Indira Gandhi." "1998 = Operation Shakti = Pokhran-II = Vajpayee." First test was "peaceful" (no weapons declared). Second test (1998) was openly military — India declared itself a nuclear weapons state.
Q.307. India's second nuclear test (Pokhran-II/Operation Shakti) was in: Ans: May 11 and 13, 1998 (under PM Atal Bihari Vajpayee)
Explanation: 5 nuclear tests in 2 days (3 on May 11, 2 on May 13). India declared itself a nuclear weapons state. Led to international sanctions (lifted later). Pakistan responded with its own tests (May 28, 1998). Scientist: APJ Abdul Kalam. May 11 = National Technology Day.
Trick: "Pokhran-II = 1998 = Vajpayee = APJ Abdul Kalam = 5 tests." May 11 = National Technology Day (celebrates this). India's nuclear doctrine: "No First Use" (NFU) — India won't use nukes first but will retaliate massively if attacked.
Q.308. Emergency was declared in India from: Ans: June 25, 1975 to March 21, 1977 (21 months, under PM Indira Gandhi)
Explanation: Declared under Art.352 on grounds of "internal disturbance." Triggered by Allahabad HC invalidating Indira's election. Press censored, opposition leaders arrested, fundamental rights suspended. Elections held in 1977 — Congress lost badly. Led to 44th Amendment reforms.
Trick: "Emergency = June 25, 1975 = 21 months = Indira." Darkest period of Indian democracy. Key events during Emergency: forced sterilization, slum demolition, press censorship, MISA (Maintenance of Internal Security Act) used to jail thousands. Janata Party won 1977 elections — first non-Congress government.
Q.309. Economic Liberalization (LPG reforms) was introduced in: Ans: 1991 (by PM P.V. Narasimha Rao and Finance Minister Dr. Manmohan Singh)
Explanation: India faced balance of payments crisis (foreign reserves = only 2 weeks of imports!). LPG = Liberalization (reduce government control), Privatization (sell public companies), Globalization (open to foreign trade/investment). Transformed India from closed socialist economy to open market economy.
Trick: "1991 = LPG = Rao + Manmohan = economic crisis → reforms." India pledged gold to IMF to get emergency loan. Then opened economy: abolished License Raj, reduced import duties, allowed FDI, devalued rupee. Result: India's GDP growth jumped from 3.5% ("Hindu rate") to 6-8%.
Q.310. India became a member of United Nations on: Ans: October 30, 1945 (founding member — even before independence!)
Explanation: India was a founding member of UN (signed charter in 1945) even though it was still under British rule! This was because British India had separate international representation. After independence (1947), India continued as a member. India has been non-permanent UNSC member 8 times.
Trick: "India = UN founding member = 1945 (before independence!)." India wants permanent UNSC seat (currently 5 permanent: USA, UK, France, Russia, China). India is the largest contributor of troops to UN peacekeeping missions.

2.9 World History Highlights

Q.311. French Revolution occurred in: Ans: 1789
Explanation: Overthrew monarchy (King Louis XVI executed). Established republic based on "Liberty, Equality, Fraternity." Inspired democratic movements worldwide including India's freedom movement. India's Preamble borrows these ideals from France.
Trick: "1789 = French Revolution = Liberty, Equality, Fraternity." These 3 words are in India's Preamble! Bastille Day (July 14) = France's Independence Day. Napoleon rose to power after the revolution (1799).
Q.312. American War of Independence was in: Ans: 1776 (Declaration of Independence, July 4)
Explanation: 13 American colonies declared independence from Britain. "No taxation without representation" was the slogan. Thomas Jefferson wrote the Declaration. George Washington led the army and became first President. Inspired French Revolution and later Indian freedom movement.
Trick: "1776 = American Independence = July 4." India borrowed from US Constitution: Preamble, Fundamental Rights, Judicial Review, Federal structure, Impeachment. US = world's oldest democracy still functioning under same constitution.
Q.313. Russian Revolution occurred in: Ans: 1917 (October Revolution — Bolsheviks under Lenin overthrew Tsar)
Explanation: Ended 300-year Romanov dynasty. Established world's first communist state (USSR). Two revolutions: February (Tsar abdicated) and October (Lenin's Bolsheviks seized power). Led to Cold War (1947-1991) between USA and USSR.
Trick: "1917 = Russian Revolution = Lenin = Communism." USSR lasted 1922-1991 (69 years). India borrowed Emergency provisions from Germany's Weimar Republic, but was also influenced by USSR's planning (Five Year Plans, DPSP ideas).
Q.314. World War I was fought during: Ans: 1914-1918
Explanation: Allies (Britain, France, Russia, USA) vs Central Powers (Germany, Austria-Hungary, Ottoman Empire). Trigger: assassination of Archduke Franz Ferdinand. India sent 1.3 million soldiers for Britain. After WWI: League of Nations formed, Ottoman Empire collapsed (Khilafat issue).
Trick: "WWI = 1914-1918 = 4 years." India's role: 1.3 million soldiers, 74,000 died. British promised reforms in return → Montagu-Chelmsford (1919) was disappointing → led to Non-Cooperation. Treaty of Versailles (1919) humiliated Germany → led to WWII.
Q.315. World War II was fought during: Ans: 1939-1945
Explanation: Allies (Britain, USA, USSR, France) vs Axis (Germany, Italy, Japan). Hitler's invasion of Poland triggered it. India was dragged in without consent (Viceroy declared war without consulting Indians → Congress resigned from provinces). Ended with atomic bombs on Japan (Hiroshima, Nagasaki).
Trick: "WWII = 1939-1945 = 6 years." India's connection: Quit India (1942), INA (1943-45), Bengal Famine (1943, 3 million died). After WWII, Britain was too weak to hold India → independence (1947). UN formed (1945) to prevent future world wars.
Q.316. United Nations was established in: Ans: October 24, 1945 (headquarters in New York, USA)
Explanation: Replaced failed League of Nations. 51 founding members (India included). Main organs: General Assembly, Security Council (5 permanent + 10 non-permanent), ICJ, Secretariat. Current members: 193 countries. Secretary-General: António Guterres (since 2017).
Trick: "UN = Oct 24, 1945 = New York." Oct 24 = UN Day. 5 permanent UNSC members (P5): USA, UK, France, Russia, China (all have veto power). India wants to be 6th permanent member. UN agencies: WHO, UNESCO, UNICEF, ILO, FAO, IMF, World Bank.
Q.317. Universal Declaration of Human Rights was adopted in: Ans: December 10, 1948 (by UN General Assembly in Paris)
Explanation: 30 articles defining fundamental human rights for all people. Not legally binding but morally powerful. Inspired by WWII atrocities (Holocaust). Dec 10 = Human Rights Day. India's Fundamental Rights are influenced by UDHR.
Trick: "UDHR = Dec 10, 1948 = 30 articles." Dec 10 = Human Rights Day worldwide. Drafted by committee chaired by Eleanor Roosevelt (US). India's Hansa Mehta was a key contributor (she changed "All men" to "All human beings" in Article 1!).
Q.318. The Renaissance began in: Ans: Italy (14th-17th century, starting in Florence)
Explanation: "Renaissance" = rebirth. Revival of art, science, and learning after the "Dark Ages" in Europe. Key figures: Leonardo da Vinci, Michelangelo, Galileo, Copernicus. Spread from Italy to rest of Europe. Led to Scientific Revolution and Enlightenment.
Trick: "Renaissance = Italy = 14th century = rebirth of learning." It ended medieval superstition and started modern science. India had its own "Renaissance" in 19th century (Ram Mohan Roy, Vivekananda) — inspired by European Renaissance ideas.
Q.319. Industrial Revolution started in: Ans: England (18th century, approximately 1760s onwards)
Explanation: Shift from hand production to machine manufacturing. Started with textile industry (spinning jenny, power loom). Steam engine (James Watt) revolutionized transport and factories. Led to urbanization, capitalism, colonialism (need for raw materials and markets — why Britain colonized India).
Trick: "Industrial Revolution = England = 18th century = machines replace hands." It's WHY Britain colonized India: needed raw cotton (India) → made cloth in Manchester → sold back to India (destroying Indian weavers). This economic exploitation is what Drain Theory describes.
Q.320. Berlin Wall fell in: Ans: November 9, 1989
Explanation: The Wall divided Berlin (and Germany) into West (capitalist, democratic) and East (communist, Soviet-controlled) from 1961-1989. Its fall symbolized the end of Cold War and communism in Europe. Germany reunified in 1990. USSR dissolved in 1991.
Trick: "Berlin Wall = 1961 (built) to 1989 (fell) = 28 years." Its fall = end of Cold War. Timeline: Wall falls (1989) → Germany reunites (1990) → USSR dissolves (1991) → Cold War officially ends. This reshaped world politics — USA became sole superpower.

2.10 Cultural Heritage

Q.321. Ajanta Caves are famous for: Ans: Buddhist paintings and sculptures (2nd century BCE to 6th century CE, Maharashtra)
Explanation: 30 rock-cut caves near Aurangabad. Famous for murals (wall paintings) depicting Buddha's life and Jataka tales. Paintings survived 2000 years in dark caves! UNESCO World Heritage Site. Rediscovered by a British officer (John Smith, 1819) during a tiger hunt.
Trick: "Ajanta = paintings (Buddhist only)." "Ellora = sculptures (Hindu+Buddhist+Jain)." Ajanta = older, paintings. Ellora = newer, sculptures. Both in Maharashtra near Aurangabad. Ajanta's paintings are India's finest ancient art.
Q.322. Ellora Caves contain: Ans: Hindu, Buddhist, AND Jain temples (6th-11th century CE, Maharashtra) — 34 caves total
Explanation: 12 Buddhist + 17 Hindu + 5 Jain caves. The Kailasa Temple (Cave 16) is the world's largest monolithic rock-cut structure — carved TOP-DOWN from a single rock! UNESCO World Heritage Site.
Trick: "Ellora = all 3 religions = Kailasa Temple = carved from ONE rock top to bottom." 200,000 tonnes of rock removed. Built by Rashtrakuta king Krishna I (8th century).
Q.323. Konark Sun Temple was built by: Ans: Narasimhadeva I of Eastern Ganga dynasty (13th century, Odisha)
Explanation: Designed as a giant chariot of Sun God with 24 wheels (=24 hours) and 7 horses (=7 days). The wheels are actual sundials! Called "Black Pagoda" by European sailors. UNESCO World Heritage Site.
Trick: "Konark = Sun Temple = chariot = 24 wheels = 7 horses = Odisha." Oriented east (towards sunrise). "Kona" (corner) + "Arka" (sun) = Konark.
Q.324. Sanchi Stupa was built by: Ans: Emperor Ashoka (3rd century BCE, Madhya Pradesh)
Explanation: Buddhist monument containing relics of Buddha. Hemispherical dome with ornamental gateways (toranas) added later by Satavahanas. UNESCO World Heritage Site.
Trick: "Sanchi = Ashoka = Buddhist stupa = MP." Note: Lion Capital (national emblem) is from Sarnath, NOT Sanchi. Buddha shown by symbols (footprints, tree) in early art — not human form.
Q.325. Qutub Minar was started by: Ans: Qutub-ud-din Aibak (1193, completed by Iltutmish)
Explanation: 72.5m tall, India's tallest brick minaret. 5 storeys of red sandstone and marble. Built to celebrate Muslim victory. UNESCO World Heritage Site. Iron Pillar (Gupta, rust-free 1600 years) stands in same complex.
Trick: "Qutub Minar: Aibak started, Iltutmish completed, Firoz Shah repaired." 5 storeys. Named after Sufi saint Qutbuddin Bakhtiar Kaki (or Aibak himself — debated).
Q.326. The Thousand Pillar Temple in Warangal was built by: Ans: Rudra Deva (Kakatiya dynasty, 1163 CE, at Hanamkonda)
Explanation: Dedicated to Shiva, Vishnu, and Surya (Trikutalayam = 3 shrines). 1000 intricately carved pillars. Star-shaped platform. Nandi carved from single black basalt rock. Showcases Kakatiya architectural excellence.
Trick: "Thousand Pillar Temple = Rudra Deva = 1163 = Hanamkonda = Trikutalayam." Kakatiya architecture: star-shaped plans, ornate pillars, bracket figures. Telangana's pride.
Q.327. Ramappa Temple (UNESCO World Heritage Site) was built by: Ans: Recharla Rudra, general of Kakatiya king Ganapati Deva (1213 CE, Palampet, Mulugu district)
Explanation: Named after its sculptor Ramappa (rare!). Famous for floating bricks (so light they float on water!), bracket figures (madanikas), intricate carvings. UNESCO World Heritage Site since 2021 — Telangana's first.
Trick: "Ramappa = 1213 = Kakatiya = UNESCO 2021 = floating bricks." Marco Polo reportedly called it "the brightest star in the galaxy of temples." Only temple named after its sculptor, not deity or king.
Q.328. Golconda Fort was originally built by: Ans: Kakatiya rulers (12th-13th century, mud fort); later expanded by Qutb Shahi dynasty (16th-17th century, granite)
Explanation: 4 forts within forts, 8 gates, famous acoustics (clap at entrance heard 1 km away at top!). Famous for diamond trade (Kohinoor, Hope Diamond). Fell to Aurangzeb after 8-month siege (1687).
Trick: "Golconda = Kakatiyas (original) + Qutb Shahis (expanded)." "Golla Konda" = Shepherd's Hill (Telugu). Famous for: acoustics, diamonds, 87 bastions. Fateh Darwaza = Victory Gate (where Aurangzeb's army finally broke through).
Q.329. The first Indian to win Nobel Prize was: Ans: Rabindranath Tagore (Literature, 1913, for "Gitanjali")
Explanation: First non-European to win Nobel in Literature. Composed national anthems of TWO countries: India and Bangladesh. Founded Visva-Bharati University (Shantiniketan). Returned knighthood after Jallianwala Bagh (1919).
Trick: Indian Nobel winners: Tagore(Lit,1913), Raman(Physics,1930), Mother Teresa(Peace,1979), Amartya Sen(Econ,1998), Kailash Satyarthi(Peace,2014). Indian-origin: Khorana, Chandrasekhar, Ramakrishnan, Banerjee.
Q.330. The first Indian to win Nobel Prize in Science was: Ans: C.V. Raman (Physics, 1930, for "Raman Effect" — inelastic scattering of light)
Explanation: Discovered Feb 28, 1928 — celebrated as National Science Day. When light passes through transparent material, some changes wavelength. Used to identify chemical compounds. Worked at IISc Bangalore.
Trick: "C.V. Raman = Physics = 1930 = Feb 28 = National Science Day." His nephew S. Chandrasekhar also won Nobel (Physics, 1983). Raman was first Asian to win science Nobel.
Q.331. Sangam literature belongs to: Ans: Tamil Nadu (3rd century BCE to 3rd century CE)
Explanation: "Sangam" = assembly of poets at Madurai. Covers love (Akam), war (Puram), ethics. Tirukkural by Thiruvalluvar is the most famous work. Gives detailed picture of ancient Tamil trade with Romans, Pandya/Chola/Chera kingdoms.
Trick: "Sangam = Tamil = Madurai = 3rd BCE-3rd CE." Key works: Tirukkural ("Tamil Veda"), Silappadikaram, Manimekalai. Mentions Roman trade, pepper export, Muziris port.
Q.332. Megasthenes was the ambassador of: Ans: Seleucus Nicator (Greek) to Chandragupta Maurya's court — wrote "Indica"
Explanation: Lived in Pataliputra for years. Described Indian society, caste system, Mauryan administration. Original book lost — known through quotes by other Greek writers.
Trick: Foreign travelers sequence: Megasthenes(Maurya) → Fa-Hien(Gupta) → Hiuen Tsang(Harsha) → Al-Biruni(Ghazni) → Ibn Battuta(Tughlaq) → Marco Polo(Kakatiya). Each = one dynasty!
Q.333. Fa-Hien visited India during the reign of: Ans: Chandragupta II / Vikramaditya (Gupta period, ~399-414 CE)
Explanation: Chinese Buddhist monk collecting manuscripts. Described India as peaceful and prosperous (Golden Age). Said people were honest, roads safe. Didn't mention the king by name (focused on Buddhism, not politics).
Trick: "Fa-Hien = Gupta = peaceful India = Buddhist pilgrim." Compare: Fa-Hien barely mentions politics. Hiuen Tsang gives detailed political info. Both were Chinese Buddhist monks but different eras.
Q.334. Hiuen Tsang visited India during the reign of: Ans: Harshavardhana (7th century CE, stayed ~629-645 CE)
Explanation: Spent 16 years in India, studied at Nalanda for 5 years. His "Si-Yu-Ki" is our most detailed source about Harsha's India. Carried 657 Buddhist texts back to China on 20 horses.
Trick: "Hiuen Tsang = Harsha = Nalanda = 'Prince of Pilgrims' = Si-Yu-Ki." Most important foreign traveler for Indian history exams. Described Nalanda as having 10,000 students.
Q.335. Ibn Battuta visited India during: Ans: Muhammad bin Tughlaq's reign (stayed 1333-1347 CE)
Explanation: Moroccan traveler, served as Qazi (judge) for 8 years. His book "Rihla" describes Tughlaq's experiments, Delhi's grandeur. Traveled 75,000 miles — history's greatest medieval traveler.
Trick: "Ibn Battuta = Tughlaq = Rihla = Moroccan = 14th century." Witnessed capital transfer to Daulatabad, token currency. Confirms Tughlaq's "mad genius" reputation from Indian sources.
Q.336. Marco Polo visited: Ans: South India (Kakatiya and Pandya kingdoms) in 13th century (1292-1294 CE)
Explanation: Italian merchant. Mentioned Rudrama Devi (Kakatiya queen) as wise ruler. Described diamond mines, spice trade, wealthy ports. His book introduced India to Europe.
Trick: "Marco Polo = South India = Kakatiyas = 13th century = Italian." Important for Telangana — provides external evidence of Kakatiya prosperity and Rudrama Devi's fame.
Q.337. The Chola dynasty is famous for: Ans: Naval power (conquered SE Asia), Brihadeeswarar Temple (Thanjavur), excellent village self-government
Explanation: Cholas (9th-13th century, Tamil Nadu) had India's most powerful navy. Rajendra Chola I conquered Sri Lanka, Maldives, parts of SE Asia. Village administration (Sabha, Ur) was remarkably democratic. Brihadeeswarar = UNESCO site.
Trick: "Cholas = Navy + Temple + Village admin." Rajaraja I (temple builder) and Rajendra I (naval conqueror). Chola bronzes (Nataraja) = world-famous. Uttaramerur inscriptions show ancient village democracy.
Q.338. Pallava dynasty is famous for: Ans: Shore Temple at Mahabalipuram, rock-cut architecture, Kanchipuram temples (3rd-9th century CE, Tamil Nadu)
Explanation: Pioneered Dravidian temple architecture. Mahabalipuram's Shore Temple and Five Rathas = UNESCO sites. Developed Grantha script (ancestor of many SE Asian scripts). Narasimhavarman I = greatest ruler.
Trick: "Pallavas = Mahabalipuram = rock-cut = Kanchipuram." Narasimhavarman I called "Mamalla" — Mahabalipuram named after him. Pallava architecture influenced Angkor Wat (Cambodia)!
Q.339. Chalukya dynasty capital was: Ans: Badami/Vatapi (Western Chalukyas, 6th-8th century); Kalyani (Later Chalukyas, 10th-12th century)
Explanation: Three branches: Badami, Eastern (Vengi, AP), Kalyani. Built Pattadakal temples (UNESCO) and Aihole temples ("cradle of Indian architecture"). Pulakeshin II defeated Harsha — only king to do so!
Trick: "Chalukyas = Badami + Aihole + Pattadakal (Karnataka)." Pulakeshin II = greatest (defeated Harsha at Narmada). Aihole = "cradle of temple architecture" — earliest experiments in temple building.
Q.340. The Battle of Talikota (1565) resulted in: Ans: Defeat and destruction of Vijayanagara Empire by combined Deccan Sultanates
Explanation: Also called Battle of Rakshasa-Tangadi. Five Sultanates (Bijapur, Golconda, Ahmednagar, Bidar, Berar) united against Vijayanagara. King Aliya Rama Raya killed. Hampi looted for 6 months. Ended 229 years of Vijayanagara glory.
Trick: "Talikota 1565 = Vijayanagara destroyed = 5 Sultanates united." Most important battle in South Indian history. After this, no major Hindu empire in South until Marathas. Hampi's ruins today show the scale of destruction.
Q.341. Permanent Settlement (1793) was introduced by: Ans: Lord Cornwallis (in Bengal, Bihar, Orissa)
Explanation: Fixed land revenue permanently. Zamindars collected tax from farmers, paid fixed amount to British. Zamindars became owners; farmers became tenants with no rights. Revenue fixed forever — bad for British long-term (inflation eroded value).
Trick: "Permanent Settlement = Cornwallis = 1793 = Zamindari = Bengal." Three systems: Zamindari (Bengal, landlord collects), Ryotwari (South, farmer pays directly), Mahalwari (North, village pays collectively). VERY common exam topic — know all three!
Q.342. Ryotwari System was introduced in: Ans: Madras and Bombay (by Thomas Munro and Alexander Read)
Explanation: "Ryot" = farmer. Direct settlement between British and individual farmer. No zamindar middleman. Farmer owns land but pays 50% revenue (very high!). Covered most of South/West India including present-day Telangana/AP.
Trick: "Ryotwari = Ryot = farmer direct = South = Munro." 50% revenue was exploitative. If crop failed, farmer still owed → debt trap. This system covered AP, Telangana, TN, Karnataka, Maharashtra — relevant for TSPSC!
Q.343. Mahalwari System was introduced in: Ans: North-Western Provinces, Punjab (by Holt Mackenzie, 1822)
Explanation: "Mahal" = village. Revenue collected from entire village collectively. Village headman responsible. Revenue revised periodically (not permanent). Middle ground between Zamindari and Ryotwari.
Trick: "Mahalwari = village collectively = North = Mackenzie." Comparison: Zamindari(landlord, Bengal), Ryotwari(individual farmer, South), Mahalwari(village, North). All three exploited farmers differently.
Q.344. Doctrine of Lapse was introduced by: Ans: Lord Dalhousie (Governor-General, 1848-1856)
Explanation: If ruler died without natural male heir, kingdom annexed by British. Adopted sons not recognized. States annexed: Satara, Jhansi, Nagpur, Jaitpur, Sambhalpur. Major cause of 1857 revolt — Rani Lakshmibai lost Jhansi this way.
Trick: "Doctrine of Lapse = Dalhousie = no heir = British take." Dalhousie annexed more territory than any other GG. Rani Lakshmibai's adopted son wasn't recognized → she revolted in 1857. "Meri Jhansi nahi doongi!" (I won't give up my Jhansi!).
Q.345. English education was introduced in India by: Ans: Lord Macaulay (Macaulay's Minute, 1835)
Explanation: Macaulay wanted to create "Indians in blood but English in taste" — intermediaries for British rule. Oriental learning defunded. English became medium of higher education. Controversial but created the educated class that later led freedom movement!
Trick: "Macaulay's Minute = 1835 = English education." Irony: Macaulay wanted loyal subjects, but English-educated Indians read about liberty/democracy and demanded freedom! The tool of colonialism became the weapon against it.
Q.346. Railways were first introduced in India in: Ans: 1853 (Bombay to Thane, 34 km, April 16, under Lord Dalhousie)
Explanation: Built to transport raw materials to ports and move troops. 14 carriages, 400 passengers. By 1947: 54,000 km of railways. Built for exploitation but accidentally united India and helped freedom movement (people could travel, ideas could spread).
Trick: "First train = 1853 = Bombay-Thane = Dalhousie." Railways united India physically. Irony: built for British profit but became tool of Indian unity. Today Indian Railways = world's 4th largest network, largest employer.
Q.347. Telegraph was introduced in India by: Ans: Lord Dalhousie (1853, first line: Calcutta to Agra)
Explanation: Helped British control vast empire quickly. By 1857: 4000 miles of lines. Rebels in 1857 cut telegraph wires (understood its strategic importance). India's telegraph service lasted 160 years until 2013!
Trick: "Dalhousie = Railways + Telegraph + Postal (all 1853-54)." He modernized India's infrastructure for British benefit. Telegraph was crucial for military communication — that's why 1857 rebels targeted it.
Q.348. Indian Penal Code (IPC) was drafted by: Ans: Lord Macaulay (drafted 1837, enacted 1860, replaced by Bharatiya Nyaya Sanhita 2023)
Explanation: India's criminal law for 163 years. Covered all crimes. Section 124A (sedition) used against freedom fighters. Section 377 (homosexuality) struck down 2018. Replaced by BNS, BNSS, BSA in 2023 (new criminal laws).
Trick: "IPC = Macaulay = 1860 = replaced by BNS (2023)." Macaulay shaped both education AND law in India. New laws (2023): BNS (replaces IPC), BNSS (replaces CrPC), BSA (replaces Evidence Act).
Q.349. Vernacular Press Act (1878) was passed by: Ans: Lord Lytton (to suppress Indian language newspapers critical of British)
Explanation: Indian language papers criticizing British during Afghan War and famine. Government could confiscate presses and ban publications. English papers exempt (double standards!). Repealed by Lord Ripon (1882). Called "gagging act."
Trick: "Vernacular Press Act = Lytton = 1878 = suppress Indian press." "Ripon repealed = 1882." Lytton was unpopular (lavish Durbar during famine). This Act increased nationalist anger — opposite of intended effect!
Q.350. Ilbert Bill controversy (1883) was during: Ans: Lord Ripon's tenure — proposed Indian judges trying European offenders
Explanation: Europeans protested violently (racist opposition) against being tried by Indian judges. Bill watered down. But it showed Indians that Europeans would never accept equality voluntarily — boosted nationalism. Led directly to INC founding (1885).
Trick: "Ilbert Bill = Ripon = 1883 = racist backlash → INC founded 1885." The controversy proved Indians needed political organization. Ripon was the most popular Viceroy among Indians (also introduced local self-government, repealed Vernacular Press Act).

Section 3: Telangana Movement & State (150 Questions)

Topics: Telangana Armed Struggle, Separate Statehood Movement, Formation of Telangana State, Telangana Culture, Welfare Schemes, Government Policies

3.1 Telangana Armed Struggle (1946-1951)

Q.351. The Telangana Armed Struggle (1946-1951) was against: Ans: Nizam's feudal rule and the Razakar atrocities
Explanation: The largest peasant uprising in Indian history. Farmers revolted against: (1) Nizam's autocratic rule, (2) Razakar militia's violence, (3) Feudal landlords (Deshmukhs/Jagirdars) who exploited peasants through forced labor (Vetti), illegal taxes, and land grabbing. About 4000 villages were liberated by peasants.
Trick: "Telangana Armed Struggle = 1946-51 = anti-Nizam + anti-feudal + anti-Razakar." It was BOTH a freedom struggle (against Nizam's rule) AND a class struggle (against landlords). CPI led it. 4000 villages liberated, 10 lakh acres of land distributed to poor farmers.
Q.352. The Telangana Armed Struggle was led by: Ans: Communist Party of India (CPI)
Explanation: CPI organized peasants into armed guerrilla squads ("dalams"). Key leaders: Ravi Narayan Reddy, Baddam Yella Reddy, Makhdoom Mohiuddin (poet). They established "gram rajyams" (village republics) with people's courts, land redistribution, and abolition of forced labor.
Trick: "CPI led Telangana struggle." Key leaders: Ravi Narayan Reddy (first elected communist MLA in India), Makhdoom Mohiuddin (revolutionary Urdu poet — "Ye jung hai jung-e-azadi"). The struggle was called off in 1951 after Indian Army entered and elections were announced.
Q.353. The Razakars were led by: Ans: Qasim Razvi (head of Ittehad-ul-Muslimeen paramilitary force)
Explanation: Razakars = "volunteers." They were the Nizam's private militia (150,000-200,000 strong) who terrorized Hindus and anyone supporting India's integration. They committed murders, rapes, forced conversions, and looting. Their atrocities were a major reason for Operation Polo.
Trick: "Razakars = Qasim Razvi = Ittehad-ul-Muslimeen = Nizam's militia." They wanted Hyderabad to remain independent or join Pakistan. Their violence against civilians forced India's hand — Sardar Patel ordered Operation Polo. After merger, Razvi was arrested and later released (went to Pakistan).
Q.354. The Telangana Armed Struggle started from which village? Ans: Kadivendi village, Jangaon district (July 4, 1946 — Doddi Komarayya was killed by landlord's men)
Explanation: Doddi Komarayya, a Dalit farmer, was killed by the landlord's goondas for supporting the peasant movement. His death sparked the armed uprising. Farmers took up arms, formed guerrilla squads, and began attacking landlords and Razakars. July 4 is remembered as the start.
Trick: "July 4, 1946 = Kadivendi = Doddi Komarayya killed = struggle begins." His death was the trigger — like Jallianwala Bagh was for Non-Cooperation. The struggle then spread across Nalgonda, Warangal, Khammam, and Karimnagar districts.
Q.355. Chakali Ailamma is famous for: Ans: Resisting the landlord Visnur Ramachandra Reddy in Palakurthy village — symbol of Telangana women's resistance
Explanation: Ailamma (a washerwoman — "Chakali" caste) refused to give up her land to the landlord. Despite threats, beatings, and her house being burned, she didn't surrender. She became the icon of women's participation in the Telangana struggle. Thousands of women joined after her example.
Trick: "Chakali Ailamma = Palakurthy = woman resistance symbol." She proved that even the poorest, lowest-caste woman could stand up to powerful landlords. Women played a huge role in the struggle — as fighters, spies, food suppliers, and shelter providers for guerrillas.
Q.356. Operation Polo (Police Action) was conducted on: Ans: September 13-17, 1948 (Indian Army entered Hyderabad State; Nizam surrendered in 5 days)
Explanation: Led by Major General J.N. Chaudhuri. Indian Army entered from multiple directions. Nizam's forces (including Razakars) collapsed quickly. Nizam surrendered on Sep 17. Minimal military casualties but Razakar violence against civilians continued briefly during the operation.
Trick: "Operation Polo = Sep 13-17, 1948 = 5 days = J.N. Chaudhuri." Why "Polo"? Hyderabad had most polo grounds in India! Sardar Patel ordered it after all diplomatic efforts failed. It ended 224 years of Nizam rule and integrated Hyderabad into India.
Q.357. Hyderabad State was merged into Indian Union on: Ans: September 17, 1948 (celebrated as Telangana Liberation Day / Vimochana Dinotsavam / Hyderabad Merger Day)
Explanation: The Nizam signed the Instrument of Accession on Sep 17. This ended: (1) Nizam's autocratic rule, (2) Razakar terror, (3) Feudal exploitation. September 17 is a state holiday in Telangana. Different groups call it different names — Liberation Day, Merger Day, or Integration Day.
Trick: "Sep 17, 1948 = Telangana Liberation Day." It's on Sardar Patel's birth anniversary month (Oct 31). The date is politically significant — Telangana government celebrates it as "Liberation Day" (from Nizam's oppression). It's a state government holiday.
Q.358. The Vande Mataram movement in Hyderabad State was in: Ans: 1938-39 (against Nizam's ban on singing Vande Mataram and hoisting Indian flag)
Explanation: Nizam banned Vande Mataram and Indian national flag in Hyderabad State. People defied the ban — thousands were arrested. This was Hyderabad's version of the national freedom movement. Leaders: Swami Ramananda Tirtha, Burgula Ramakrishna Rao.
Trick: "Vande Mataram movement = 1938-39 = Hyderabad = anti-Nizam." It showed that people of Hyderabad State wanted to be part of India, not remain under Nizam. Swami Ramananda Tirtha = leader of Hyderabad State Congress (different from Indian National Congress).
Q.359. Komaram Bheem fought against: Ans: Nizam's rule for tribal rights in Adilabad (martyred at Jodeghat, 1940)
Explanation: A Gond tribal leader who fought for tribal land rights and against exploitation by Nizam's officials and moneylenders. His slogan: "Jal, Jungle, Zameen" (Water, Forest, Land — for tribals). Killed in an encounter at Jodeghat (Adilabad) in 1940. He's Telangana's tribal hero.
Trick: "Komaram Bheem = Adilabad = tribal rights = Jal Jungle Zameen = 1940." He's like Birsa Munda of Telangana. Fought for tribal self-rule in Gondu areas. His sacrifice inspired tribal movements. Asifabad district renamed as "Komaram Bheem Asifabad" in his honor.
Q.360. The Andhra Mahasabha was founded in: Ans: 1930 (to promote Telugu language and culture in Nizam's dominion where Urdu was official language)
Explanation: Initially a cultural organization demanding Telugu medium education and recognition. Later became political — split into moderates (who joined Congress) and radicals (who joined CPI and led armed struggle). It was the voice of Telugu people in Nizam's Hyderabad.
Trick: "Andhra Mahasabha = 1930 = Telugu rights in Nizam's state." It evolved: cultural (1930s) → political (1940s) → revolutionary (1946-51). The CPI faction of Andhra Mahasabha led the Telangana Armed Struggle. It's the precursor to Telangana's political consciousness.

3.2 States Reorganisation & Visalandhra

Q.361. Andhra State (separate from Madras) was formed on: Ans: October 1, 1953 (after Potti Sriramulu's sacrifice, capital: Kurnool)
Explanation: First state formed on linguistic basis. Carved out of Madras Presidency's Telugu-speaking districts. Capital was Kurnool (1953-1956). This was ONLY the Andhra region (Rayalaseema + Coastal Andhra) — Telangana was NOT part of it (still in Hyderabad State).
Trick: "Andhra State = Oct 1, 1953 = first linguistic state = Kurnool capital." Don't confuse with Andhra Pradesh (1956, which included Telangana). Andhra State (1953) was only coastal+Rayalaseema. Telangana merged with it in 1956 to form AP.
Q.362. Potti Sriramulu died on: Ans: December 15, 1952 (after 58-day fast demanding separate Andhra State from Madras)
Explanation: A Gandhian who fasted unto death for a Telugu-speaking state. Nehru initially ignored him. After his death, massive riots erupted across Telugu areas. Nehru was forced to announce Andhra State within 2 days. His sacrifice triggered linguistic reorganization of ALL Indian states.
Trick: "Potti Sriramulu = Dec 15, 1952 = 58 days fast = Andhra State." His death changed India's map forever. Without him, linguistic states might not have happened (or happened much later). He's called "Amarajeevi" (immortal). Oct 1 = Andhra Pradesh Formation Day.
Q.363. States Reorganisation Commission (SRC) was headed by: Ans: Justice Fazal Ali (members: K.M. Panikkar, H.N. Kunzru) — appointed 1953, reported 1955
Explanation: After Potti Sriramulu's death, government appointed SRC to study linguistic reorganization of ALL states. It recommended 16 states and 3 UTs. For Telangana, it recommended keeping it SEPARATE (not merging with Andhra) — but this was overruled by politicians.
Trick: "SRC = Fazal Ali = 1953-55 = recommended Telangana stay separate." This is CRUCIAL for Telangana questions. SRC clearly said Telangana should NOT be merged with Andhra. But Nehru and leaders overruled this with Gentlemen's Agreement (1956). SRC's wisdom was proven right 58 years later (2014 bifurcation).
Q.364. SRC recommended regarding Telangana: Ans: Telangana should remain separate; merger with Andhra only after 1961 general elections if people of Telangana desire it
Explanation: SRC said: "It is in the interest of Telangana as well as Andhra that for the present the Telangana area should constitute into a separate state." It feared Telangana (smaller, less developed) would be dominated by Andhra (larger, more developed). History proved SRC right.
Trick: "SRC said: keep Telangana separate, merge only if Telangana people want it after 1961." This recommendation was IGNORED. Politicians forced merger in 1956 with Gentlemen's Agreement as "safeguard." Those safeguards were never implemented — leading to 1969, 1972, and 2001-2014 movements.
Q.365. Andhra Pradesh was formed by merging Telangana with Andhra on: Ans: November 1, 1956
Explanation: Despite SRC's recommendation against merger, Telangana was merged with Andhra State to form Andhra Pradesh. Capital: Hyderabad. Gentlemen's Agreement was signed as a "safeguard" for Telangana's interests. This merger was the root cause of all subsequent Telangana movements.
Trick: "Nov 1, 1956 = AP formed = Telangana + Andhra merged." This date is the beginning of Telangana's grievances. SRC said don't merge → politicians merged anyway → safeguards violated → 1969 movement → 2001-2014 movement → finally separated in 2014. Full circle in 58 years.
Q.366. The Gentlemen's Agreement (1956) was between: Ans: Leaders of Telangana and Andhra regions (to protect Telangana's interests in the merged state)
Explanation: Signed before merger to assure Telangana people. Key signatories: B. Ramakrishna Rao (Telangana), Bezawada Gopala Reddy (Andhra). It promised safeguards in jobs, education, budget, and political representation for Telangana. Almost all provisions were violated within years.
Trick: "Gentlemen's Agreement = 1956 = promises to Telangana = ALL BROKEN." It was called "gentlemen's" because it wasn't legally enforceable — just a moral commitment. When Andhra leaders violated it, Telangana had no legal remedy. This betrayal is the foundation of the separate state demand.
Q.367. Key provisions of Gentlemen's Agreement included: Ans: Safeguards for Telangana in education, employment (Mulki Rules), budget allocation, and CM rotation
Explanation: Promises: (1) Telangana's revenue spent in Telangana. (2) Mulki Rules for jobs (locals get preference). (3) Separate Regional Committee for Telangana. (4) CM from Telangana for some years. (5) Telangana's education budget protected. Almost none were honored.
Trick: "Gentlemen's Agreement promises: Jobs, Budget, Education, CM rotation — ALL VIOLATED." Telangana's revenue was diverted to Andhra. Mulki Rules were diluted. Regional Committee was powerless. CM rotation never happened properly. This systematic violation fueled decades of resentment.
Q.368. The Mulki Rules were meant to: Ans: Protect employment of local Telangana people in government jobs (locals get preference in their region)
Explanation: "Mulki" = local/native. Rules said government jobs in Telangana should go to Telangana residents (who lived there for 15+ years). These existed since Nizam's time. After merger, Andhra people flooded Telangana for jobs, violating these rules. This was a major grievance.
Trick: "Mulki Rules = local jobs for locals = Telangana's protection." Violation of Mulki Rules was the MAIN trigger for 1969 movement. Supreme Court upheld Mulki Rules (1972) but then government passed a law to override them (leading to Jai Andhra movement). It's the core jobs issue.
Q.369. The first Chief Minister of united Andhra Pradesh was: Ans: Neelam Sanjiva Reddy (1956-1960)
Explanation: He was from Andhra region (Anantapur). Despite Gentlemen's Agreement promising Telangana representation, the first CM was from Andhra. He later became President of India (1977-1982). This set the pattern of Andhra dominance in AP politics.
Trick: "Sanjiva Reddy = first CM of AP = later President of India." He was from Andhra region, not Telangana — showing that Gentlemen's Agreement was ignored from Day 1. Telangana leaders felt cheated immediately after merger.
Q.370. Burgula Ramakrishna Rao was: Ans: First Chief Minister of Hyderabad State (1952-1956, before merger with Andhra)
Explanation: After Operation Polo (1948), Hyderabad State had military governor, then civilian government. Burgula was elected CM in 1952 (first elections in Hyderabad State). He served until merger (1956). He was a Telangana leader who signed the Gentlemen's Agreement.
Trick: "Burgula = first CM of Hyderabad State = 1952-56." He's different from first CM of AP (Sanjiva Reddy). Hyderabad State existed as a separate entity from 1948-1956 before being merged into AP. Burgula represented Telangana's interests during merger negotiations.

3.3 Separate Telangana Movement

Q.371. The first major Telangana movement (Jai Telangana) was in: Ans: 1969
Explanation: Massive agitation demanding separate Telangana state. Triggered by violation of Mulki Rules and Gentlemen's Agreement. Students led the movement. About 369 people died (mostly in police firing). Government promised reforms but didn't deliver. Movement subsided but grievances remained.
Trick: "1969 = first Jai Telangana movement = 369 deaths = students led." It was the FIRST organized demand for separate Telangana after merger. Government's response: promises, committees, but no real action. This pattern (agitation → promises → betrayal) repeated for 45 years until 2014.
Q.372. The 1969 movement was triggered by: Ans: Violation of Mulki Rules and Gentlemen's Agreement; non-implementation of safeguards for Telangana
Explanation: Specific triggers: (1) Andhra people getting Telangana government jobs (violating Mulki Rules). (2) Telangana's revenue being spent in Andhra region. (3) Telangana students not getting seats in Osmania University. (4) No CM rotation as promised. Accumulated grievances exploded.
Trick: "1969 trigger = Mulki Rules violated + budget diverted + jobs stolen." The core issue was always ECONOMIC: Telangana's resources being used for Andhra's development while Telangana remained backward. This economic argument remained central through 2014.
Q.373. How many people died in the 1969 Telangana movement? Ans: About 369 people (mostly students, in police firing and self-immolations)
Explanation: Students from Osmania University and Kakatiya University were at the forefront. Police fired on protesters multiple times. Several students self-immolated. Despite the sacrifice, the movement was suppressed. Government formed committees but took no real action.
Trick: "369 martyrs in 1969." The sacrifice was enormous but the movement didn't achieve its goal. It took 45 more years (until 2014) for Telangana to become a state. These martyrs are honored every year in Telangana.
Q.374. The Jai Andhra movement was in: Ans: 1972 (by Andhra region people AGAINST Mulki Rules — they wanted Mulki Rules abolished)
Explanation: After Supreme Court upheld Mulki Rules (1972), Andhra people protested — they wanted equal access to Hyderabad jobs. Demanded either abolish Mulki Rules or separate Andhra from Telangana! Ironic: both regions wanted separation at different times.
Trick: "Jai Andhra = 1972 = Andhra people against Mulki Rules." Irony: 1969 = Telangana wanted separation. 1972 = Andhra wanted separation! Both movements showed the merger was a failure. Government's solution: Six-Point Formula (1973) — another compromise that satisfied nobody.
Q.375. The Six-Point Formula (1973) was: Ans: Agreement between Telangana and Andhra leaders to resolve regional disputes (replaced Mulki Rules with zonal system)
Explanation: Replaced Mulki Rules with a "zonal system" for jobs (6 zones in AP, locals get preference in their zone). Also promised: (1) Separate development boards. (2) Proportional budget allocation. (3) Education safeguards. Like previous agreements, it was poorly implemented.
Trick: "Six-Point Formula = 1973 = replaced Mulki Rules = zonal system." Pattern: Gentlemen's Agreement (1956) → violated → 1969 movement → promises → Six-Point Formula (1973) → violated → 2001 movement → promises → finally separation (2014). Each "solution" was just a temporary patch.
Q.376. Telangana Praja Samithi (TPS) was founded by: Ans: M. Chenna Reddy (1969, during the first Telangana movement)
Explanation: TPS was the first political party dedicated to separate Telangana. Won 11 Lok Sabha seats in 1971 elections (showing massive public support). But Chenna Reddy later merged TPS with Congress (1971) after being promised CM post. This "betrayal" disillusioned Telangana people.
Trick: "TPS = Chenna Reddy = 1969 = first Telangana party." He won big but then merged with Congress for personal power. This pattern of leaders "selling out" the movement repeated until KCR (who stayed committed). Chenna Reddy did become CM later (1989) but didn't push for Telangana.
Q.377. The second phase of Telangana movement intensified in: Ans: 1997 onwards (with formation of various organizations and political parties demanding statehood)
Explanation: After decades of neglect, Telangana's backwardness became undeniable. Multiple organizations formed: Telangana Jagruti, various student unions, intellectuals' forums. The demand gained academic and intellectual backing with data showing Telangana's systematic underdevelopment.
Trick: "1997 onwards = second phase = intellectual + political movement." This phase was different from 1969: it was more organized, data-driven, and sustained. It culminated in TRS formation (2001) and eventually statehood (2014). 17 years of continuous agitation.
Q.378. Telangana Rashtra Samithi (TRS) was founded by: Ans: K. Chandrashekar Rao (KCR) on April 27, 2001
Explanation: KCR left TDP to form TRS with single agenda: separate Telangana state. The party became the vehicle for the statehood movement. Won seats in 2004 elections, joined UPA government, later withdrew. KCR's hunger strike (2009) was the turning point. TRS renamed to BRS (Bharat Rashtra Samithi) in 2022.
Trick: "TRS = KCR = April 27, 2001 = single-point agenda: Telangana state." KCR sacrificed his political career in TDP to fight for Telangana. His persistence for 13 years (2001-2014) finally achieved statehood. TRS became BRS in 2022 (national ambitions).
Q.379. KCR's hunger strike for Telangana was in: Ans: November 29 - December 9, 2009 (11 days, ended after government announced Telangana formation)
Explanation: KCR went on indefinite fast. His health deteriorated rapidly. Massive protests erupted across Telangana — bandhs, rail rokos, self-immolations. On Dec 9, Home Minister P. Chidambaram announced "process of forming Telangana state will be initiated." KCR broke fast.
Trick: "KCR fast = Nov-Dec 2009 = Dec 9 announcement." But the announcement was later put "on hold" (Jan 2010) after Andhra leaders protested. This betrayal intensified the movement further. Sakala Janula Samme (all-people strike) followed. Final achievement came only in 2014.
Q.380. The UPA government announced the formation of Telangana on: Ans: December 9, 2009 (later put on hold in January 2010 after backlash from Andhra leaders)
Explanation: Home Minister Chidambaram's midnight announcement created euphoria in Telangana but fury in Andhra. Andhra MLAs/MPs threatened to resign. Government backtracked within weeks — appointed Srikrishna Committee to "study" the issue. This flip-flop angered Telangana people immensely.
Trick: "Dec 9, 2009 = announced → Jan 2010 = put on hold." This was the biggest betrayal — giving hope and snatching it away. It led to the most intense phase of the movement (2010-2014): Million March, Sakala Janula Samme, student suicides, and finally Parliament passing the bill in 2014.
Q.381. Srikrishna Committee was appointed in: Ans: February 2010 (Justice B.N. Srikrishna; submitted report December 30, 2010)
Explanation: Appointed after government put Telangana announcement "on hold." Studied all aspects: historical, economic, social, political. Gave 6 options. Preferred option: keep AP united with empowered Telangana Regional Council. Telangana people rejected this — wanted full statehood, not a "council."
Trick: "Srikrishna Committee = Feb 2010 = 6 options = preferred united AP." Telangana rejected the report because it didn't recommend separate state. The committee acknowledged Telangana's genuine grievances but chose a "middle path" that satisfied nobody.
Q.382. Srikrishna Committee recommended: Ans: 6 options; preferred Option 5: keeping united AP with constitutionally empowered Telangana Regional Council
Explanation: 6 options ranged from: (1) Status quo, (2) Bifurcation, (3) Separate Telangana with Hyderabad as UT, (4) Separate Telangana with Hyderabad as capital, (5) United AP with empowered council (preferred), (6) Bifurcation with Hyderabad as shared capital for 10 years.
Trick: "6 options, preferred #5 (united AP + council)." But government ultimately chose something close to Option 6 (bifurcation with Hyderabad as joint capital for 10 years). The committee's work was thorough but its preferred option was politically unviable — Telangana people would never accept anything less than full statehood.
Q.383. The All-Party Meeting on Telangana was held on: Ans: July 30, 2013 (Congress Working Committee approved bifurcation of AP to create Telangana)
Explanation: After years of agitation, UPA government finally decided to bifurcate AP. CWC passed resolution on July 30, 2013. This was the definitive political decision. AP Reorganisation Bill was then drafted and introduced in Parliament.
Trick: "July 30, 2013 = CWC approves Telangana." This was the point of no return. After this, it was just a matter of parliamentary process. The decision came after: KCR's fast (2009), Srikrishna Committee (2010), Million March (2011), Sakala Janula Samme (2011), and continuous agitation.
Q.384. AP Reorganisation Act was passed by Parliament on: Ans: February 18, 2014 (Lok Sabha) and March 1, 2014 (Rajya Sabha); President's assent: March 1, 2014
Explanation: Passed amid chaos — Andhra MPs protested, pepper spray was used in Parliament! The Act created Telangana as 29th state with 10 districts (now 33). Hyderabad = joint capital for max 10 years. Special provisions for Andhra (new capital, institutions, Polavaram project).
Trick: "AP Reorganisation Act = Feb 18, 2014 (LS) = March 1, 2014 (RS + President)." Passed in extraordinary circumstances — pepper spray in Parliament! Shows how contentious it was. But democracy prevailed — the bill was passed by majority vote.
Q.385. Telangana State was officially formed on: Ans: June 2, 2014 (India's 29th state)
Explanation: KCR sworn in as first CM at Raj Bhavan. Capital: Hyderabad (joint capital with AP for 10 years). Initially 10 districts (later reorganized to 33 districts in 2016). State symbols: Palapitta (Indian Roller) = state bird, Jammi Chettu (Prosopis cineraria) = state tree.
Trick: "June 2, 2014 = Telangana born = 29th state = KCR first CM." After 58 years of merger (1956-2014) and decades of struggle, Telangana finally became a separate state. June 2 = Telangana Formation Day (state holiday). The dream of millions was realized.
Q.386. The first Chief Minister of Telangana State was: Ans: K. Chandrashekar Rao (KCR) — served 2014-2023
Explanation: KCR led the movement for 13 years (2001-2014) and became the natural choice for first CM. He won 2014 and 2018 elections. Focused on irrigation (Kaleshwaram, Mission Bhagiratha), welfare (Rythu Bandhu, KCR Kit), and development. Lost 2023 elections to Congress (Revanth Reddy became CM).
Trick: "KCR = first CM = 2014-2023 = TRS/BRS." Key schemes: Kaleshwaram (irrigation), Mission Bhagiratha (drinking water), Rythu Bandhu (farmer investment support), Dalit Bandhu, KCR Kit (pregnant women). He reorganized 10 districts into 33 districts (2016).
Q.387. The first Governor of Telangana was: Ans: E.S.L. Narasimhan (served as Governor of both AP and Telangana during transition)
Explanation: He was already Governor of united AP. After bifurcation, he served as Governor of both states simultaneously during the transition period. Later, separate Governors were appointed. He administered oath to KCR as first CM on June 2, 2014.
Trick: "ESL Narasimhan = first Governor of Telangana = also last Governor of united AP." He's a former IB (Intelligence Bureau) chief. Served as Governor from 2014 to 2019. Current Governor: check latest appointment.
Q.388. Hyderabad serves as joint capital of AP and Telangana for: Ans: Maximum 10 years (till 2024 as per AP Reorganisation Act, 2014)
Explanation: Since AP didn't have a ready capital, Hyderabad was shared. AP was supposed to build a new capital (Amaravati was planned but not fully built). After 10 years (2024), Hyderabad becomes exclusively Telangana's capital. AP's capital situation remains unresolved.
Trick: "Joint capital = 10 years = till 2024." AP planned Amaravati as new capital but it's incomplete. The 10-year period has ended (June 2024). Hyderabad is now exclusively Telangana's. AP uses Amaravati/Visakhapatnam.
Q.389. How many districts did Telangana have at formation? Ans: 10 districts (Adilabad, Karimnagar, Warangal, Khammam, Nalgonda, Mahabubnagar, Rangareddy, Hyderabad, Medak, Nizamabad)
Explanation: These were the original 10 districts from united AP that became Telangana. In 2016, KCR reorganized them into 33 districts for better administration (smaller districts = closer governance). Each old district was split into 2-4 new districts.
Trick: "10 original → 33 new (2016)." Original 10: "AKWKNMRHM N" — Adilabad, Karimnagar, Warangal, Khammam, Nalgonda, Mahabubnagar, Rangareddy, Hyderabad, Medak, Nizamabad. Reorganization was for administrative efficiency.
Q.390. Telangana currently has how many districts? Ans: 33 districts (reorganized from 10 in October 2016)
Explanation: New districts created by splitting old ones. Examples: Warangal → Warangal Urban + Warangal Rural + Jangaon + Mahabubabad. Karimnagar → Karimnagar + Rajanna Sircilla + Jagtial + Peddapalli. Goal: bring administration closer to people.
Trick: "33 districts since 2016." Key new districts: Yadadri Bhuvanagiri (temple district), Siddipet, Kamareddy, Mancherial, Wanaparthy, Nagarkurnool, Suryapet, Jayashankar Bhupalpally, Jogulamba Gadwal, Medchal-Malkajgiri (most urban after Hyderabad).

3.4 Telangana State - Key Facts

Q.391. Area of Telangana State is: Ans: 1,12,077 sq km (12th largest state by area in India)
Explanation: Telangana is larger than many countries (bigger than South Korea, Portugal, Hungary). It's on the Deccan Plateau at an average elevation of 400-600m. Mostly semi-arid climate with hot summers and moderate rainfall.
Trick: "Telangana area = 1.12 lakh sq km = 12th largest." For comparison: Rajasthan is largest (3.42 lakh), Goa smallest (3,702). Telangana is about 3.4% of India's total area. Population: ~3.5 crore (2011 census).
Q.392. Telangana shares borders with: Ans: Maharashtra (North), Chhattisgarh (North-East), Andhra Pradesh (South & East), Karnataka (West)
Explanation: 4 neighboring states. Longest border with AP (south and east). Maharashtra border in north (Adilabad, Nirmal, Kumuram Bheem districts). Chhattisgarh touches only a small part in northeast (Bhadradri Kothagudem). Karnataka in west (Jogulamba Gadwal, Narayanpet).
Trick: "Telangana borders: MACK" = Maharashtra, AP, Chhattisgarh, Karnataka. Clockwise from North: Maharashtra → Chhattisgarh → AP → Karnataka. No coast (landlocked state). No international border.
Q.393. The State Animal of Telangana is: Ans: Deer (Jinka — specifically the Spotted Deer/Chital)
Explanation: The spotted deer is found in Telangana's forests, especially in Amrabad Tiger Reserve and Eturnagaram Wildlife Sanctuary. It represents the state's wildlife heritage. Deer are also culturally significant — associated with forests and nature in Telugu literature.
Trick: "State Animal = Deer (Jinka)." Other state symbols: Bird=Palapitta (Indian Roller), Tree=Jammi Chettu, Flower=Tangedu, Fish=Korameenu (Murrel). Memorize all state symbols — frequently asked in TSPSC exams!
Q.394. The State Bird of Telangana is: Ans: Palapitta (Indian Roller / Blue Jay — Coracias benghalensis)
Explanation: A beautiful blue bird commonly seen in Telangana's countryside. It's considered auspicious — seeing it during Dasara is believed to bring good luck. The bird is associated with Bathukamma festival. It's also called "Neelakantha" (blue-throated, like Lord Shiva).
Trick: "State Bird = Palapitta = Indian Roller = blue bird." It's seen during Dasara — people look for it as a good omen. The bird's blue color is striking. It's different from AP's state bird (Rose-ringed Parakeet/Rama Chiluka).
Q.395. The State Tree of Telangana is: Ans: Jammi Chettu (Prosopis cineraria / Shami tree)
Explanation: A drought-resistant tree found in semi-arid Telangana. Culturally significant — worshipped during Dasara (Pandavas hid weapons in Shami tree). Provides fodder, fuel, and timber in dry regions. Symbolizes resilience (survives in harsh conditions like Telangana's people).
Trick: "State Tree = Jammi Chettu = Shami = Dasara connection." Worshipped on Vijayadashami (Dasara). The tree survives extreme drought — symbolizing Telangana's resilience through decades of struggle. Also called "Kalpavriksha of the desert."
Q.396. The State Flower of Telangana is: Ans: Tangedu Puvvu (Senna auriculata / Tanner's Cassia)
Explanation: A bright yellow flower that blooms during Bathukamma season (September-October). Used extensively in Bathukamma flower arrangements. The flower represents Telangana's cultural identity and is closely tied to its most important festival.
Trick: "State Flower = Tangedu = yellow = Bathukamma flower." Tangedu flowers are the primary flowers used in making Bathukamma (flower stack). The flower blooms in September-October, coinciding with Bathukamma/Dasara season. It's uniquely Telangana.
Q.397. Telangana State Formation Day is celebrated on: Ans: June 2 (the day Telangana officially became India's 29th state in 2014)
Explanation: A state holiday. Celebrated with flag hoisting, cultural programs, and government events. Marks the culmination of decades of struggle for separate statehood. The first Formation Day (June 2, 2015) was celebrated with great enthusiasm across the state.
Trick: "June 2 = Formation Day." "Sep 17 = Liberation Day." Two important Telangana dates. June 2 = birth of new state (2014). Sep 17 = liberation from Nizam (1948). Both are state holidays.
Q.398. Telangana Liberation Day is celebrated on: Ans: September 17 (the day Hyderabad State was merged with India in 1948 through Operation Polo)
Explanation: Marks freedom from Nizam's autocratic rule and Razakar atrocities. Celebrated as a state government holiday since 2014 (earlier it was not officially celebrated by united AP government — a major Telangana grievance). Also called "Vimochana Dinotsavam."
Trick: "Sep 17 = Liberation Day = Operation Polo = 1948." The fact that united AP government never officially celebrated this day was a major emotional grievance for Telangana people. After statehood, it became an official celebration — acknowledging Telangana's unique history.
Q.399. The Telangana Legislative Assembly has how many seats? Ans: 119 seats (+ 1 nominated Anglo-Indian, now discontinued = effectively 119)
Explanation: 119 constituencies across 33 districts. Hyderabad district alone has 15 seats. Elections held every 5 years. First election: 2014 (TRS won 63 seats). Second: 2018 (TRS won 88). Third: 2023 (Congress won 64, formed government).
Trick: "Telangana Assembly = 119 seats." AP Assembly = 175 seats. Telangana Lok Sabha = 17 seats. AP Lok Sabha = 25 seats. Total from erstwhile AP = 119+175=294 Assembly, 17+25=42 LS seats.
Q.400. Telangana has how many Lok Sabha constituencies? Ans: 17
Explanation: 17 parliamentary constituencies: Adilabad, Peddapalli, Karimnagar, Nizamabad, Zahirabad, Medak, Malkajgiri, Secunderabad, Hyderabad, Chevella, Mahbubnagar, Nagarkurnool, Nalgonda, Bhongir, Warangal, Mahabubabad, Khammam.
Trick: "17 LS seats in Telangana." Hyderabad is the most famous (Owaisi's constituency). Malkajgiri is the largest by population. In 2024 elections, results showed diverse political representation across these 17 seats.

3.5 Telangana Government Schemes & Policies

Q.401. Kaleshwaram Lift Irrigation Project is on which river? Ans: Godavari River (world's largest multi-stage lift irrigation project)
Explanation: Lifts Godavari water through multiple stages to irrigate drought-prone areas of Telangana. Has 21 lifts, 20 reservoirs, 1832 km of gravity canals. Designed to irrigate 18.25 lakh acres. Lifts water to a height of ~618m (like lifting water to the top of a 200-story building!).
Trick: "Kaleshwaram = Godavari = world's largest lift irrigation." It's Telangana's flagship project. Named after Kaleshwaram temple (Shiva) at the confluence of Godavari and Pranahita rivers. Controversial due to cost (₹80,000+ crore) but transformative for Telangana's agriculture.
Q.402. Mission Bhagiratha aims to provide: Ans: Safe drinking water to every household through pipeline (100 LPCD in urban, 100 LPCD in rural)
Explanation: LPCD = Liters Per Capita Per Day. Goal: piped treated water to every household (no more borewells or tankers). Sources water from Godavari and Krishna rivers. One of India's largest drinking water projects. Named after King Bhagiratha (who brought Ganga to earth in mythology).
Trick: "Mission Bhagiratha = drinking water to every home = 100 LPCD." Named after mythological king who brought river to earth. Telangana's answer to water scarcity. Covers all 33 districts. Aims to eliminate fluoride/contamination problems in groundwater.
Q.403. Mission Kakatiya is related to: Ans: Restoration of tanks/water bodies in Telangana (restoring ancient irrigation tanks built by Kakatiyas and others)
Explanation: Telangana has ~46,000 tanks (many built by Kakatiyas 800 years ago) that had fallen into disrepair. Mission Kakatiya restores them: desilting, strengthening bunds, repairing sluices. Increases irrigation capacity and groundwater recharge. Named after Kakatiya dynasty (famous tank builders).
Trick: "Mission Kakatiya = tank restoration = 46,000 tanks." Kakatiyas were master tank builders (Ramappa Lake, Pakala Lake, Laknavaram). This mission revives their legacy. Restored tanks increase irrigation + groundwater + fish production. Win-win-win.
Q.404. Rythu Bandhu scheme provides: Ans: Investment support of ₹10,000 per acre per year to farmers (₹5,000 per season × 2 seasons)
Explanation: Direct cash transfer to farmers BEFORE sowing season — for seeds, fertilizers, labor. Given to all farmers regardless of crop or land size. No loan needed. First state to give direct investment support (not loan waiver). Covers ~58 lakh farmers. Praised by NITI Aayog.
Trick: "Rythu Bandhu = ₹10,000/acre/year = ₹5,000 per season." "Rythu" = farmer, "Bandhu" = friend. It's different from PM-KISAN (₹6,000/year to all farmers nationally). Telangana's scheme is per ACRE (so larger farmers get more). Controversial but effective in reducing farmer distress.
Q.405. Rythu Bima scheme provides: Ans: Life insurance of ₹5 lakh to farmers (age 18-59 years) — premium paid by state government
Explanation: If a farmer dies (any cause — natural, accident, suicide), family gets ₹5 lakh. State pays the entire premium (farmer pays nothing). Covers all land-owning farmers enrolled in Rythu Bandhu. One of India's most comprehensive farmer insurance schemes.
Trick: "Rythu Bima = ₹5 lakh life insurance = free for farmer." "Bima" = insurance. Combined with Rythu Bandhu (investment support), it provides complete financial security to farmers. State pays ~₹1,000 crore/year in premiums.
Q.406. KCR Kit scheme is for: Ans: Pregnant women and newborns — provides ₹12,000 cash + kit with baby care items
Explanation: Provides: (1) ₹12,000 cash assistance for institutional delivery. (2) Kit containing baby clothes, diapers, mosquito net, oil, soap, toys, blankets. Encourages hospital deliveries (reduces maternal/infant mortality). Available at all government hospitals.
Trick: "KCR Kit = pregnant women + newborns = ₹12,000 + baby kit." Aims to reduce maternal mortality and encourage institutional deliveries. Similar to Tamil Nadu's "Amma Baby Care Kit." Named after the CM who introduced it.
Q.407. Aasara Pensions scheme provides pensions to: Ans: Old age (₹2,016/month), widows, disabled, beedi workers, weavers, toddy tappers, single women, filaria/AIDS patients
Explanation: One of India's highest state pensions. Covers 8 categories of vulnerable people. Amount: ₹2,016/month (increased from ₹200 in united AP era). Covers ~40 lakh beneficiaries. Directly credited to bank accounts. Named "Aasara" = support/shelter.
Trick: "Aasara = ₹2,016/month = 8 categories." It's significantly higher than most states (many give only ₹500-1000). The amount ₹2,016 was symbolic (year of district reorganization). Covers: old age, widows, disabled, beedi, weavers, toddy, single women, filaria.
Q.408. Telangana Ku Haritha Haram is: Ans: Massive tree plantation program (target: 230 crore saplings to increase forest cover from 24% to 33%)
Explanation: "Haritha Haram" = Green Garland. Aims to increase Telangana's forest/tree cover to 33% (national target). Involves planting along roads, in institutions, on private lands, and in degraded forests. One of India's largest afforestation programs.
Trick: "Haritha Haram = 230 crore trees = green Telangana." Goal: 33% forest cover (currently ~24%). Involves all departments, schools, colleges, and citizens. Saplings distributed free. Survival rate monitoring through apps. Named to evoke "green necklace" around Telangana.
Q.409. T-Hub is: Ans: India's largest technology business incubator (in Hyderabad, supports startups)
Explanation: Located in Hyderabad (IIIT campus initially, now T-Hub 2.0 in Raidurg — world's largest innovation campus at 5.82 lakh sq ft). Supports startups with mentoring, funding access, workspace, and networking. Has incubated 2000+ startups. Partnership with government, academia, and industry.
Trick: "T-Hub = Hyderabad = India's largest incubator = startups." T-Hub 2.0 (opened 2022) is the world's largest innovation campus. Telangana positioned itself as India's startup capital alongside Bangalore. Also: WE-Hub (women entrepreneurs), T-Works (prototyping).
Q.410. TS-iPASS provides: Ans: Single-window industrial clearance within 15 days (automatic approval if no response in 15 days)
Explanation: TS-iPASS = Telangana State Industrial Project Approval and Self-Certification System. Revolutionary: if government doesn't respond within 15 days, approval is AUTOMATIC (deemed approved). Attracted massive industrial investment to Telangana. First state to guarantee time-bound clearance.
Trick: "TS-iPASS = 15 days = auto-approval = industry-friendly." This made Telangana one of India's top investment destinations. "Self-certification" means industries certify compliance themselves (inspected later). Reduced red tape dramatically. Other states copied this model.
Q.411. Bathukamma is: Ans: Floral festival unique to Telangana (celebrated during Navaratri/Dasara by women, 9 days)
Explanation: "Bathukamma" = "Mother Goddess, come alive!" Women make conical flower stacks (using Tangedu, Gunuka, Chamanti flowers), sing folk songs, dance in circles, and immerse Bathukamma in water on the last day (Saddula Bathukamma). It's Telangana's identity festival — declared state festival in 2014.
Trick: "Bathukamma = flowers + women + Navaratri = Telangana's identity." 9 days of celebration ending on Ashtami (day before Dasara). Each day has a different name.
