Q.1747. The Kakori Train Robbery (1925) was organized by: Ans: HRA members including Ram Prasad Bismil, Ashfaqullah Khan, Rajendra Lahiri
Q.1748. Bhagat Singh, Sukhdev, and Rajguru were hanged on: Ans: March 23, 1931 (Lahore Conspiracy Case)
Q.1749. Bhagat Singh threw a bomb in the Central Legislative Assembly on: Ans: April 8, 1929 (to protest against Public Safety Bill and Trade Disputes Bill)
Q.1750. The Hindustan Socialist Republican Association (HSRA) was formed by: Ans: Bhagat Singh, Chandrashekhar Azad, and others in 1928 (renamed from HRA)
Q.1751. Chandrashekhar Azad died at: Ans: Alfred Park, Allahabad on February 27, 1931 (shot himself to avoid capture)
Q.1752. The Chittagong Armoury Raid (1930) was led by: Ans: Surya Sen (Masterda)
Q.1753. Khudiram Bose was executed for: Ans: Muzaffarpur bombing (1908) – one of the youngest revolutionaries to be hanged (age 18)
Q.1754. The Anushilan Samiti and Jugantar were revolutionary organizations in: Ans: Bengal
Q.1755. The Ghadar Party was founded in: Ans: 1913 at San Francisco, USA by Lala Hardayal and Sohan Singh Bhakna

12.9 Social Reform Movements

Q.1756. Raja Ram Mohan Roy founded: Ans: Brahmo Samaj (1828) – worked against Sati, child marriage, and for women's education
Q.1757. Sati was abolished by: Ans: Lord William Bentinck through Regulation XVII of 1829
Q.1758. The Arya Samaj was founded by: Ans: Swami Dayanand Saraswati in 1875 at Bombay
Q.1759. The motto of Arya Samaj is: Ans: "Back to the Vedas" (Krinvanto Vishwam Aryam)
Q.1760. The Ramakrishna Mission was founded by: Ans: Swami Vivekananda in 1897
Q.1761. Swami Vivekananda represented Hinduism at: Ans: World Parliament of Religions, Chicago (1893)
Q.1762. The Theosophical Society in India was led by: Ans: Annie Besant (headquarters at Adyar, Madras)
Q.1763. Jyotirao Phule founded: Ans: Satyashodhak Samaj (1873) for upliftment of lower castes
Q.1764. Dr. B.R. Ambedkar founded which organization for Dalit rights? Ans: Bahishkrit Hitakarini Sabha (1924) and later Independent Labour Party
Q.1765. The Self-Respect Movement in South India was started by: Ans: E.V. Ramasamy Periyar (1925)
Q.1766. Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar worked for: Ans: Widow Remarriage (Hindu Widows' Remarriage Act, 1856)
Q.1767. The Aligarh Movement was led by: Ans: Sir Syed Ahmad Khan (founded MAO College, 1875, later Aligarh Muslim University)
Q.1768. The Prarthana Samaj was founded in: Ans: 1867 at Bombay by Atmaram Pandurang
Q.1769. The Young Bengal Movement was led by: Ans: Henry Louis Vivian Derozio (at Hindu College, Calcutta)
Q.1770. The Widow Remarriage Association was founded by: Ans: M.G. Ranade and R.G. Bhandarkar in 1861

12.10 Press & Education in British India

Q.1771. The first newspaper in India was: Ans: Bengal Gazette (Hicky's Gazette) started by James Augustus Hicky in 1780
Q.1772. The Vernacular Press Act (1878) was passed by: Ans: Lord Lytton (to suppress Indian language newspapers)
Q.1773. The Vernacular Press Act was repealed by: Ans: Lord Ripon in 1882
Q.1774. The Indian Press Act was passed in: Ans: 1910 (during Lord Minto's tenure)
Q.1775. Wood's Despatch (1854) is known as: Ans: "Magna Carta of English Education in India" (recommended universities at Calcutta, Bombay, Madras)
Q.1776. The first three universities in India were established in: Ans: 1857 at Calcutta, Bombay, and Madras
Q.1777. Macaulay's Minute (1835) advocated: Ans: English education in India (English as medium of instruction)
Q.1778. The Hunter Commission (1882) was appointed for: Ans: Review of education system (recommended primary education development)
Q.1779. Lord Curzon's Indian Universities Act (1904) aimed at: Ans: Greater government control over universities
Q.1780. The Sadler Commission (1917) dealt with: Ans: Problems of university education in India

12.11 Important INC Sessions & Events

Q.1781. The INC session where 'Vande Mataram' was first sung: Ans: 1896 Calcutta session (composed by Bankim Chandra Chattopadhyay)
Q.1782. The first woman President of INC was: Ans: Annie Besant (1917, Calcutta session)
Q.1783. The first Indian woman President of INC was: Ans: Sarojini Naidu (1925, Kanpur session)
Q.1784. The Karachi Session (1931) adopted: Ans: Resolution on Fundamental Rights and National Economic Programme
Q.1785. The Tripuri Session (1939) is significant because: Ans: Subhas Chandra Bose defeated Pattabhi Sitaramayya (Gandhi's candidate) for presidency
Q.1786. The August Offer (1940) was made by: Ans: Viceroy Lord Linlithgow (offered Dominion Status after war, expansion of Viceroy's Council)
Q.1787. The Quit India Resolution was moved by: Ans: Jawaharlal Nehru and seconded by Sardar Patel at AICC Bombay session
Q.1788. During Quit India Movement, underground radio was operated by: Ans: Usha Mehta (Congress Radio)
Q.1789. The Simla Conference (1945) was called by: Ans: Lord Wavell
Q.1790. The Attlee's Declaration (February 1947) announced: Ans: British intention to transfer power by June 1948

12.12 Miscellaneous History

Q.1791. The Indian Councils Act, 1892 introduced: Ans: Indirect elections (nomination on recommendation) and power to discuss budget
Q.1792. The Montagu-Chelmsford Reforms (1919) introduced: Ans: Dyarchy in provinces (transferred and reserved subjects)
Q.1793. The Chauri Chaura incident occurred in: Ans: Gorakhpur district, UP on February 5, 1922
Q.1794. The Bardoli Satyagraha (1928) was led by: Ans: Sardar Vallabhbhai Patel (against enhanced land revenue in Gujarat)
Q.1795. The title 'Sardar' was given to Patel by: Ans: Women of Bardoli during Bardoli Satyagraha
Q.1796. The Moplah Rebellion (1921) occurred in: Ans: Malabar region of Kerala (peasant uprising against landlords)
Q.1797. The Tebhaga Movement (1946) was a peasant movement in: Ans: Bengal (demanding 2/3 share of produce for sharecroppers)
Q.1798. The Telangana Peasant Armed Struggle (1946-51) was against: Ans: Nizam's feudal rule and landlordism (led by Communist Party)
Q.1799. The Champaran Satyagraha was against: Ans: Tinkathia system (forced indigo cultivation on 3/20th of land)
Q.1800. The Indian Independence Act, 1947 provided for: Ans: Two independent dominions (India and Pakistan), abolition of suzerainty over princely states, Governor-General for each dominion

Section 13: Telangana History, Culture & Economy (150 Questions)

Topics: Nizam Rule, Razakars, Police Action 1948, Telangana Armed Struggle, Gentlemen's Agreement, States Reorganization, Separate Telangana Agitations (1969, 2001-2014), Formation of State 2014, Bathukamma, Bonalu, Telangana Economy, Irrigation Projects, Districts

13.1 Nizam Rule & Hyderabad State

Q.1801. The Asaf Jahi dynasty (Nizams) was founded by: Ans: Mir Qamar-ud-din (Nizam-ul-Mulk) in 1724
Q.1802. The last Nizam of Hyderabad was: Ans: Mir Osman Ali Khan (Nizam VII, ruled 1911-1948)
Q.1803. Hyderabad State was the largest princely state in India by: Ans: Revenue and population (area-wise it was second after Jammu & Kashmir)
Q.1804. The official language of Hyderabad State under Nizams was: Ans: Urdu
Q.1805. The Nizam's currency was: Ans: Osmania Sicca (Hali Sicca)
Q.1806. Osmania University was established in: Ans: 1918 (first university with an Indian language – Urdu – as medium of instruction)
Q.1807. The Nizam's Guaranteed State Railway was established in: Ans: 1879
Q.1808. The Mulki Rules in Hyderabad State meant: Ans: Preference in government jobs to locals (those domiciled in Hyderabad for 15 years)
Q.1809. The Hyderabad State Congress was formed in: Ans: 1938 (to fight for responsible government under Nizam)
Q.1810. The Andhra Mahasabha was founded in: Ans: 1930 (initially for cultural and linguistic rights of Telugu people in Hyderabad State)

13.2 Razakars & Police Action 1948

Q.1811. The Razakars were the paramilitary force of: Ans: Ittehad-ul-Muslimeen (MIM), led by Qasim Razvi
Q.1812. Operation Polo (Police Action) was launched on: Ans: September 13, 1948
Q.1813. Operation Polo was led by: Ans: Major General J.N. Chaudhuri
Q.1814. The Nizam surrendered on: Ans: September 17, 1948 (celebrated as Telangana Liberation Day / Vimochana Dinotsavam)
Q.1815. After Police Action, who was appointed as Military Governor of Hyderabad? Ans: Major General J.N. Chaudhuri
Q.1816. The first Chief Minister of Hyderabad State after integration was: Ans: M.K. Vellodi (civil servant, served as CM 1950-52)
Q.1817. The first elected Chief Minister of Hyderabad State was: Ans: Burgula Ramakrishna Rao (1952-1956)
Q.1818. The Sunderlal Committee was appointed to: Ans: Investigate atrocities during and after Police Action in Hyderabad (report was suppressed for decades)
Q.1819. September 17 is celebrated in Telangana as: Ans: Telangana National Integration Day / Liberation Day (Praja Palana Dinotsavam)
Q.1820. The Nizam wanted Hyderabad to: Ans: Remain independent or join Pakistan (refused to accede to India)

13.3 Telangana Armed Struggle (1946-1951)

Q.1821. The Telangana Armed Struggle (1946-51) was led by: Ans: Communist Party of India (CPI)
Q.1822. The Telangana Armed Struggle started from: Ans: Nalgonda district (village Kadivendi/Jangaon area, July 4, 1946)
Q.1823. The immediate trigger for the armed struggle was: Ans: Murder of Doddi Komarayya, a village leader, by deshmukh's goondas
Q.1824. The main demands of the Telangana Armed Struggle were: Ans: Abolition of forced labor (vetti), redistribution of land, end of feudal exploitation
Q.1825. Key leaders of the Telangana Armed Struggle include: Ans: Ravi Narayan Reddy, Baddam Yella Reddy, Makhdoom Mohiuddin, Chakali Ailamma
Q.1826. Chakali Ailamma is famous for: Ans: Resisting the landlord Visnur Ramachandra Reddy's attempts to seize her land in Palakurthy village
Q.1827. The armed struggle covered approximately: Ans: 3,000 villages in Nalgonda, Warangal, and Khammam districts
Q.1828. About how much land was redistributed during the struggle? Ans: About 10 lakh acres of land was seized from landlords and distributed to peasants
Q.1829. The CPI withdrew the armed struggle in: Ans: October 1951 (after Indian Army operations and approaching general elections)
Q.1830. The Telangana Armed Struggle is considered one of the largest: Ans: Peasant uprisings in Indian history

13.4 States Reorganization & Gentlemen's Agreement

Q.1831. The States Reorganisation Commission (SRC) was headed by: Ans: Fazal Ali (with H.N. Kunzru and K.M. Panikkar as members)
Q.1832. The SRC submitted its report in: Ans: 1955
Q.1833. The SRC recommended regarding Telangana: Ans: Telangana should remain as a separate state (not merge with Andhra)
Q.1834. Despite SRC recommendation, Telangana was merged with Andhra through: Ans: Gentlemen's Agreement (February 20, 1956)
Q.1835. The Gentlemen's Agreement was signed between leaders of: Ans: Telangana and Andhra regions
Q.1836. Key provisions of Gentlemen's Agreement included: Ans: Safeguards for Telangana in education, employment, budget allocation; Regional Council for Telangana; CM rotation
Q.1837. Andhra Pradesh was formed on: Ans: November 1, 1956 (by merging Telangana with Andhra State)
Q.1838. The first Chief Minister of united Andhra Pradesh was: Ans: Neelam Sanjiva Reddy
Q.1839. The Telangana Regional Committee was established under: Ans: Section 21 of States Reorganisation Act, 1956
Q.1840. The Gentlemen's Agreement was violated primarily in: Ans: Employment (Mulki rules not followed), education, and budget allocation for Telangana

13.5 Separate Telangana Agitations

Q.1841. The 1969 Telangana agitation was triggered by: Ans: Supreme Court ruling against Mulki Rules and non-implementation of safeguards
Q.1842. The 1969 agitation was led by: Ans: Students and employees; key leaders included Dr. Marri Chenna Reddy
Q.1843. How many people died in the 1969 Telangana agitation? Ans: About 369 people (mostly students) in police firing
Q.1844. The Jai Andhra Movement (1972) was a counter-movement demanding: Ans: Separation of Andhra from Telangana (triggered by Mulki Rules implementation)
Q.1845. The Six-Point Formula (1973) was an agreement to: Ans: Resolve Telangana-Andhra disputes (replaced Gentlemen's Agreement safeguards)
Q.1846. The Telangana Rashtra Samithi (TRS) was founded on: Ans: April 27, 2001 by K. Chandrashekar Rao (KCR)
Q.1847. KCR's hunger strike for Telangana statehood began on: Ans: November 29, 2009
Q.1848. The December 9, 2009 announcement by the Central Government was: Ans: Process for formation of Telangana state would be initiated (later put on hold)
Q.1849. The Srikrishna Committee was appointed in: Ans: February 2010 (to study the demand for separate Telangana)
Q.1850. The Srikrishna Committee submitted its report in: Ans: December 2010 (recommended keeping AP united with empowered Telangana Regional Council as preferred option)
Q.1851. The UPA government announced the decision to form Telangana on: Ans: July 30, 2013
Q.1852. The Andhra Pradesh Reorganisation Act was passed by Parliament on: Ans: February 18, 2014 (received Presidential assent on March 1, 2014)
Q.1853. Telangana became the 29th state of India on: Ans: June 2, 2014
Q.1854. The first Chief Minister of Telangana state was: Ans: K. Chandrashekar Rao (KCR)
Q.1855. The first Governor of Telangana was: Ans: E.S.L. Narasimhan
Q.1856. Hyderabad served as common capital for both states for: Ans: 10 years (as per AP Reorganisation Act, 2014)
Q.1857. The 'Million March' for Telangana was held on: Ans: March 10, 2011 (massive rally in Hyderabad)
Q.1858. Sakala Janula Samme (All People's Strike) in Telangana was held in: Ans: September 2011 (42-day strike)
Q.1859. The Telangana movement's popular slogan was: Ans: "Jai Telangana" and "Jaya Jaya He Telangana"
Q.1860. The song "Jaya Jaya He Telangana" was written by: Ans: Ande Sri (Andesri)

13.6 Telangana Culture & Festivals

Q.1861. Bathukamma is a festival celebrated in: Ans: Telangana – a floral festival celebrated by women during Sharad Navaratri (September-October)
Q.1862. Bathukamma literally means: Ans: "Mother Goddess Come Alive" (Bathuku + Amma)
Q.1863. Bathukamma is celebrated for how many days? Ans: 9 days (from Mahalaya Amavasya to Durgashtami)
Q.1864. The flowers used in Bathukamma are primarily: Ans: Tangedu (Cassia auriculata), Gunugu, Banti (Marigold), Chemanti, and other seasonal flowers
Q.1865. Bonalu is a festival dedicated to: Ans: Goddess Mahakali (celebrated in July-August in Telangana)
Q.1866. Bonalu is mainly celebrated in: Ans: Hyderabad, Secunderabad, and other parts of Telangana (Golconda, Ujjaini Mahakali temple)
Q.1867. 'Bonam' in Bonalu refers to: Ans: Food offering (cooked rice with jaggery and curd) to the Goddess in a decorated pot
Q.1868. Sammakka-Saralamma Jatara is held at: Ans: Medaram, Mulugu district (every two years – one of the largest tribal fairs in Asia)
Q.1869. Sammakka-Saralamma Jatara is celebrated by which tribe? Ans: Koya tribe (in honor of tribal goddesses Sammakka and Saralamma)
Q.1870. The Telangana state festival declared by the government is: Ans: Bathukamma (declared as state festival in 2014)
Q.1871. Perini Sivatandavam is: Ans: An ancient dance form of Telangana (warrior dance performed before going to war, revived from Kakatiya era)
Q.1872. Oggu Katha is: Ans: A traditional ballad singing art form of Telangana (narrating stories of Lord Shiva/Mallanna)
Q.1873. Gusadi dance is performed by: Ans: Raj Gond tribals of Adilabad district during Dussehra
Q.1874. Kolatam is: Ans: A folk dance of Telangana performed with sticks (similar to Dandiya)
Q.1875. The Kakatiya Kala Thoranam (arch) is located at: Ans: Warangal (part of the Kakatiya dynasty's Swayambhu temple complex)

13.7 Telangana Economy & Irrigation Projects

Q.1876. The Kaleshwaram Lift Irrigation Project is on which river? Ans: Godavari River (world's largest multi-stage lift irrigation project)
Q.1877. Mission Bhagiratha aims to provide: Ans: Safe drinking water to every household in Telangana through pipeline
Q.1878. The Nagarjuna Sagar Dam is built on: Ans: Krishna River (shared between Telangana and Andhra Pradesh)
Q.1879. Srisailam Dam is on which river? Ans: Krishna River (in Nallamala Hills)
Q.1880. The Jurala Project is on: Ans: Krishna River in Jogulamba Gadwal district
Q.1881. Singur Dam is on which river? Ans: Manjira River (supplies drinking water to Hyderabad)
Q.1882. Nizamsagar Dam is on: Ans: Manjira River in Kamareddy district (built in 1931)
Q.1883. The SRSP (Sriram Sagar Project) is on: Ans: Godavari River at Pochampad, Nizamabad district
Q.1884. The Devadula Lift Irrigation Scheme benefits: Ans: Warangal, Khammam, and Nalgonda districts (lifts Godavari water)
Q.1885. Telangana's GSDP growth rate (approximate) is: Ans: Among the highest in India (around 11-13% at current prices in recent years)
Q.1886. The IT sector in Telangana is concentrated in: Ans: HITEC City, Gachibowli, and Madhapur areas of Hyderabad
Q.1887. Telangana's major crops include: Ans: Rice, cotton, maize, turmeric, red gram, sugarcane
Q.1888. Telangana is the largest producer in India of: Ans: Turmeric (Nizamabad district) and red gram
Q.1889. The Pharma City project in Telangana is located at: Ans: Mucherla (Rangareddy district) – one of the largest pharma clusters
Q.1890. Telangana State Industrial Project Approval and Self-Certification System is called: Ans: TS-iPASS (for single-window industrial clearances within 15 days)

13.8 Telangana Districts & Administration

Q.1891. How many districts does Telangana currently have? Ans: 33 districts (reorganized from 10 in 2016)
Q.1892. The capital of Telangana is: Ans: Hyderabad
Q.1893. The largest district in Telangana by area is: Ans: Bhadradri Kothagudem
Q.1894. The most populous district in Telangana is: Ans: Hyderabad district (most densely populated)
Q.1895. Telangana Legislative Assembly has how many seats? Ans: 119 seats
Q.1896. Telangana Legislative Council has how many seats? Ans: 40 seats
Q.1897. Telangana sends how many members to Lok Sabha? Ans: 17 members
Q.1898. Telangana sends how many members to Rajya Sabha? Ans: 7 members
Q.1899. The Telangana State emblem features: Ans: Kakatiya Kala Thoranam (arch)
Q.1900. The state bird of Telangana is: Ans: Palapitta (Indian Roller / Blue Jay)
Q.1901. The state animal of Telangana is: Ans: Jinka (Spotted Deer / Chital)
Q.1902. The state tree of Telangana is: Ans: Jammi Chettu (Prosopis cineraria / Shami tree)
Q.1903. The state flower of Telangana is: Ans: Tangedu Puvvu (Tanner's Cassia / Senna auriculata)
Q.1904. The Telangana State Song is: Ans: "Jaya Jaya He Telangana, Janani Jayaketanam"
Q.1905. Telangana Formation Day is celebrated on: Ans: June 2 every year

13.9 Telangana Government Schemes

Q.1906. Rythu Bandhu scheme provides: Ans: Rs. 10,000 per acre per year (Rs. 5,000 per season) to farmers for investment support
Q.1907. Rythu Bima scheme provides: Ans: Rs. 5 lakh life insurance to farmers (age 18-59) – premium paid by state government
Q.1908. Kalyana Lakshmi/Shaadi Mubarak scheme provides: Ans: Rs. 1,00,116 for marriage of girls from BPL families
Q.1909. KCR Kit scheme provides: Ans: Kit worth Rs. 15,000 for pregnant women delivering in government hospitals
Q.1910. Aasara Pensions scheme covers: Ans: Old age, widows, disabled, toddy tappers, weavers, single women, filaria patients, AIDS patients
Q.1911. Dalit Bandhu scheme provides: Ans: Rs. 10 lakh grant to each Dalit family for self-employment/business
Q.1912. Mission Kakatiya aims to: Ans: Restore and rejuvenate tanks/water bodies in Telangana for irrigation
Q.1913. Haritha Haram is: Ans: Telangana's massive tree plantation program (target: 230 crore saplings)
Q.1914. T-Hub is: Ans: India's largest technology incubator, located in Hyderabad (for startups)
Q.1915. WE-Hub is: Ans: India's first state-led incubator exclusively for women entrepreneurs (in Hyderabad)

13.10 Telangana Historical Dynasties & Heritage

Q.1916. The Kakatiya dynasty ruled from: Ans: Warangal (12th-14th century CE)
Q.1917. The most famous Kakatiya ruler was: Ans: Ganapati Deva and his daughter Rudrama Devi
Q.1918. Rudrama Devi was one of the few: Ans: Women rulers in Indian history (ruled Kakatiya kingdom 1263-1289 CE)
Q.1919. Prataparudra II was the last ruler of: Ans: Kakatiya dynasty (defeated by Malik Kafur and later Ulugh Khan in 1323)
Q.1920. The Thousand Pillar Temple is located at: Ans: Hanamkonda, Warangal (built by Rudra Deva in 1163 CE)
Q.1921. The Ramappa Temple (UNESCO World Heritage Site) is in: Ans: Palampet, Mulugu district (built by Recharla Rudra, a general of Kakatiya king Ganapati Deva, in 1213 CE)
Q.1922. The Qutb Shahi dynasty ruled from: Ans: Golconda/Hyderabad (1518-1687 CE)
Q.1923. The founder of Qutb Shahi dynasty was: Ans: Sultan Quli Qutb Shah
Q.1924. Charminar was built by: Ans: Muhammad Quli Qutb Shah in 1591 (to commemorate the end of plague)
Q.1925. Golconda Fort was originally built by: Ans: Kakatiya rulers (later expanded by Qutb Shahi and Bahmani sultans)
Q.1926. The Bahmani Sultanate was founded by: Ans: Alauddin Bahman Shah in 1347 (capital at Gulbarga, later Bidar)
Q.1927. The Satavahana dynasty had its capital at: Ans: Pratishthana (Paithan) and later Amaravati; Kotilingala in Telangana was an early capital
Q.1928. The most famous Satavahana ruler was: Ans: Gautamiputra Satakarni
Q.1929. The Ikshvaku dynasty ruled from: Ans: Nagarjunakonda (Vijayapuri) in present-day Telangana/AP
Q.1930. The Chalukyas of Kalyani ruled parts of Telangana during: Ans: 10th-12th century CE

13.11 Telangana Miscellaneous

Q.1931. The Pochampally village is famous for: Ans: Ikat weaving (Pochampally sarees – GI tagged)
Q.1932. Nirmal paintings and toys are from: Ans: Nirmal town, Nirmal district (GI tagged handicraft)
Q.1933. Bidriware is a metal handicraft from: Ans: Bidar (Karnataka) but also practiced in Hyderabad region
Q.1934. Pembarthi brass/metal work is from: Ans: Pembarthi village, Jangaon district (GI tagged)
Q.1935. The Kohinoor diamond was originally mined from: Ans: Kollur Mine in Guntur (some sources say Golconda mines in Telangana region)
Q.1936. Hyderabad is known as: Ans: City of Pearls, City of Nizams, Cyberabad
Q.1937. The Hussain Sagar Lake was built by: Ans: Ibrahim Quli Qutb Shah in 1563 (named after Hussain Shah Wali)
Q.1938. The Musi River flows through: Ans: Hyderabad city
Q.1939. The great Musi flood occurred in: Ans: 1908 (led to construction of Osman Sagar and Himayat Sagar reservoirs)
Q.1940. Osman Sagar and Himayat Sagar were built on: Ans: Musi River and Esi River respectively (for flood control and water supply to Hyderabad)
Q.1941. The Telangana State Road Transport Corporation (TSRTC) was formed in: Ans: 2015 (bifurcated from APSRTC)
Q.1942. Rajiv Gandhi International Airport is located at: Ans: Shamshabad, Hyderabad
Q.1943. The Genome Valley in Hyderabad is: Ans: India's first biotech cluster (in Shamirpet area)
Q.1944. DRDL and DRDO missile development center is located at: Ans: Hyderabad (Defence Research and Development Laboratory)
Q.1945. The National Remote Sensing Centre (NRSC) is located at: Ans: Balanagar, Hyderabad
Q.1946. ICRISAT (International Crops Research Institute for Semi-Arid Tropics) is at: Ans: Patancheru, near Hyderabad
Q.1947. The University of Hyderabad was established in: Ans: 1974 (Central University)
Q.1948. NALSAR University of Law is located at: Ans: Shamirpet, Hyderabad
Q.1949. The Telangana State Public Service Commission (TSPSC) was constituted in: Ans: 2014 (after formation of Telangana state)
Q.1950. The High Court of Telangana was established as a separate entity in: Ans: January 1, 2019 (bifurcated from common High Court of Judicature at Hyderabad)

Section 14: World & Indian Geography Advanced (150 Questions)

Topics: Climatology, Oceanography, Indian Monsoon, Soil Types, Natural Vegetation, Mineral Resources, Indian Rivers and Dams, Population Census, Urbanization, Agriculture, Industries, Transport, Telangana Rivers and Projects

14.1 Climatology & Indian Monsoon

Q.1951. The Indian monsoon is driven by: Ans: Differential heating of land and sea, ITCZ shift, and upper air circulation (jet streams)
Q.1952. The southwest monsoon arrives in India first at: Ans: Kerala coast (around June 1)
Q.1953. The monsoon trough extends from: Ans: Thar Desert to the head of Bay of Bengal (along the Gangetic plain)
Q.1954. The retreating monsoon (northeast monsoon) brings rainfall to: Ans: Tamil Nadu and southern Andhra Pradesh/Telangana (October-December)
Q.1955. El Nino effect on Indian monsoon is: Ans: Generally causes deficit/weak monsoon rainfall in India
Q.1956. La Nina effect on Indian monsoon is: Ans: Generally causes above-normal monsoon rainfall
Q.1957. The Indian Ocean Dipole (IOD) affects: Ans: Indian monsoon – positive IOD brings more rainfall to India
Q.1958. Mango showers occur in: Ans: Kerala and Karnataka during March-May (pre-monsoon showers)
Q.1959. Norwesters (Kal Baisakhi) occur in: Ans: West Bengal and Assam during April-May (thunderstorms)
Q.1960. The Coriolis force causes winds to deflect to the: Ans: Right in Northern Hemisphere, Left in Southern Hemisphere
Q.1961. The driest place in India is: Ans: Leh (Ladakh) – receives about 10 cm annual rainfall
Q.1962. The wettest place in India (and world) is: Ans: Mawsynram, Meghalaya (average 11,871 mm annual rainfall)
Q.1963. Western disturbances bring winter rainfall to: Ans: North India (Punjab, Haryana, J&K) – originating from Mediterranean Sea
Q.1964. The Tropic of Cancer passes through how many Indian states? Ans: 8 states (Gujarat, Rajasthan, MP, Chhattisgarh, Jharkhand, West Bengal, Tripura, Mizoram)
Q.1965. India's climate is classified as: Ans: Tropical Monsoon type (Koppen classification: Am)

14.2 Oceanography

Q.1966. The deepest point in the ocean is: Ans: Mariana Trench (Challenger Deep) – about 11,034 meters in Pacific Ocean
Q.1967. The largest ocean is: Ans: Pacific Ocean (covers about 1/3 of Earth's surface)
Q.1968. Tsunami waves are caused by: Ans: Underwater earthquakes, volcanic eruptions, or submarine landslides
Q.1969. The 2004 Indian Ocean Tsunami was triggered by an earthquake near: Ans: Sumatra, Indonesia (magnitude 9.1)
Q.1970. Ocean currents are caused by: Ans: Wind, temperature differences, salinity differences, Earth's rotation, and shape of coastline
Q.1971. The Gulf Stream is a warm current in: Ans: Atlantic Ocean (flows from Gulf of Mexico towards Europe)
Q.1972. The salinity of ocean water is highest in: Ans: Dead Sea (among water bodies); among oceans, the Atlantic has highest average salinity
Q.1973. Continental shelf extends up to a depth of: Ans: About 200 meters from the coast
Q.1974. India's Exclusive Economic Zone (EEZ) extends to: Ans: 200 nautical miles from the baseline
Q.1975. Coral reefs in India are found at: Ans: Gulf of Kutch, Gulf of Mannar, Andaman & Nicobar Islands, Lakshadweep

14.3 Indian Soils & Natural Vegetation

Q.1976. Black soil (Regur) is best suited for: Ans: Cotton cultivation (found in Deccan Plateau – Maharashtra, MP, Gujarat, Telangana)
Q.1977. Black soil is rich in: Ans: Iron, lime, calcium, magnesium, alumina; deficient in nitrogen, phosphorus, organic matter
Q.1978. Alluvial soil is found in: Ans: Indo-Gangetic plains, river deltas (most fertile and widespread soil in India)
Q.1979. Laterite soil is formed by: Ans: Leaching in areas of heavy rainfall and high temperature (rich in iron and aluminium)
Q.1980. Red soil gets its color from: Ans: Iron oxide content (found in Telangana, Tamil Nadu, Karnataka, Odisha)
Q.1981. The predominant soil type in Telangana is: Ans: Red soil and black soil (red soil in northern parts, black soil in southern parts)
Q.1982. Tropical Evergreen Forests are found in areas with rainfall above: Ans: 200 cm (Western Ghats, Northeast India, Andaman Islands)
Q.1983. Tropical Deciduous Forests are the most widespread forests in India, found in areas with rainfall: Ans: 70-200 cm (also called Monsoon Forests)
Q.1984. Mangrove forests in India are best developed in: Ans: Sundarbans (West Bengal) – largest mangrove forest in the world
Q.1985. Teak and Sal are found in: Ans: Tropical Deciduous Forests (Teak in moist deciduous, Sal in dry deciduous)

14.4 Mineral Resources & Industries

Q.1986. India's largest coal-producing state is: Ans: Jharkhand (followed by Odisha and Chhattisgarh)
Q.1987. Singareni Collieries Company Limited (SCCL) operates in: Ans: Telangana (coal mining in Godavari Valley coalfields)
Q.1988. India's largest iron ore producing state is: Ans: Odisha (followed by Chhattisgarh, Karnataka, Jharkhand)
Q.1989. Bauxite (aluminium ore) is mainly found in: Ans: Odisha, Gujarat, Jharkhand, Maharashtra, Chhattisgarh
Q.1990. Mica is mainly produced in: Ans: Jharkhand, Andhra Pradesh, Rajasthan (India was once the largest producer)
Q.1991. The Kolar Gold Fields are in: Ans: Karnataka (now largely exhausted)
Q.1992. Mumbai High is famous for: Ans: Offshore petroleum production (in Arabian Sea)
Q.1993. The largest petroleum refinery in India is: Ans: Jamnagar Refinery (Reliance Industries, Gujarat)
Q.1994. The Iron and Steel industry in India was pioneered by: Ans: TISCO (Tata Iron and Steel Company) at Jamshedpur (1907)
Q.1995. Bhilai Steel Plant was set up with the help of: Ans: Soviet Union (Russia)
Q.1996. Rourkela Steel Plant was set up with help of: Ans: Germany
Q.1997. Durgapur Steel Plant was set up with help of: Ans: United Kingdom
Q.1998. The Golden Quadrilateral connects: Ans: Delhi-Mumbai-Chennai-Kolkata (National Highway Development Project)
Q.1999. India's longest river is: Ans: Ganga (2,525 km)
Q.2000. The longest river in South India is: Ans: Godavari (1,465 km – also called Dakshin Ganga)

14.5 Indian Rivers & Dams

Q.2001. The Godavari River originates from: Ans: Trimbakeshwar near Nasik, Maharashtra
Q.2002. The Krishna River originates from: Ans: Mahabaleshwar, Maharashtra (near Jor village)
Q.2003. Major tributaries of Godavari in Telangana are: Ans: Pranahita, Indravati, Manjira, Manair, Penganga
Q.2004. Major tributaries of Krishna in Telangana are: Ans: Tungabhadra, Bhima, Musi, Dindi, Paleru
Q.2005. The Bhakra Nangal Dam is on: Ans: Sutlej River (Himachal Pradesh/Punjab border)
Q.2006. The Tehri Dam (highest in India) is on: Ans: Bhagirathi River, Uttarakhand (260.5 m height)
Q.2007. The Hirakud Dam (longest in India) is on: Ans: Mahanadi River, Odisha
Q.2008. The Sardar Sarovar Dam is on: Ans: Narmada River, Gujarat
Q.2009. The Indus River originates from: Ans: Mansarovar Lake area (near Bokhar Chu glacier) in Tibet
Q.2010. The Brahmaputra River is known as Tsangpo in: Ans: Tibet
Q.2011. West-flowing rivers of India include: Ans: Narmada, Tapti, Mahi, Sabarmati, Luni (flow into Arabian Sea)
Q.2012. East-flowing rivers of Peninsular India include: Ans: Godavari, Krishna, Cauvery, Mahanadi, Pennar (flow into Bay of Bengal)
Q.2013. The Cauvery River dispute is between: Ans: Karnataka and Tamil Nadu
Q.2014. The National River of India is: Ans: Ganga (declared in 2008)
Q.2015. The Namami Gange Programme was launched in: Ans: 2014 (for cleaning and rejuvenation of River Ganga)

14.6 Population & Urbanization

Q.2016. According to Census 2011, India's population was: Ans: 121.08 crore (1.21 billion)
Q.2017. The decadal growth rate (2001-2011) was: Ans: 17.7%
Q.2018. The sex ratio of India (Census 2011) is: Ans: 943 females per 1000 males
Q.2019. The literacy rate of India (Census 2011) is: Ans: 74.04% (Male: 82.14%, Female: 65.46%)
Q.2020. The most populous state in India is: Ans: Uttar Pradesh (about 20 crore)
Q.2021. The least populous state is: Ans: Sikkim (about 6.1 lakh)
Q.2022. The most densely populated state is: Ans: Bihar (1,106 persons per sq km)
Q.2023. The state with highest literacy rate is: Ans: Kerala (93.91%)
Q.2024. The state with highest sex ratio is: Ans: Kerala (1,084 females per 1000 males)
Q.2025. India's urban population (Census 2011) is approximately: Ans: 31.2% of total population
Q.2026. The largest city in India by population is: Ans: Mumbai (Metropolitan area)
Q.2027. Telangana's population (Census 2011) was approximately: Ans: 3.52 crore (35.2 million)
Q.2028. Telangana's literacy rate (Census 2011) is: Ans: 66.46%
Q.2029. Telangana's sex ratio (Census 2011) is: Ans: 988 females per 1000 males
Q.2030. The next Census of India is scheduled for: Ans: Census 2021 (postponed due to COVID-19; yet to be conducted as of 2024)

14.7 Indian Agriculture

Q.2031. The Green Revolution in India was introduced by: Ans: M.S. Swaminathan (with Norman Borlaug's HYV seeds) in 1960s
Q.2032. The Green Revolution primarily benefited: Ans: Wheat and Rice production (mainly in Punjab, Haryana, UP)
Q.2033. The White Revolution (Operation Flood) was related to: Ans: Milk production (led by Dr. Verghese Kurien)
Q.2034. India ranks first in the world in production of: Ans: Milk, pulses, jute, and spices
Q.2035. India ranks second in the world in production of: Ans: Rice, wheat, sugarcane, cotton, fruits, vegetables
Q.2036. Kharif crops are sown in: Ans: June-July and harvested in September-October (rice, jowar, bajra, cotton, sugarcane)
Q.2037. Rabi crops are sown in: Ans: October-November and harvested in March-April (wheat, barley, mustard, gram)
Q.2038. Zaid crops are grown in: Ans: March-June (watermelon, muskmelon, cucumber, vegetables)
Q.2039. The Minimum Support Price (MSP) is announced by: Ans: Government of India on recommendation of CACP (Commission for Agricultural Costs and Prices)
Q.2040. The largest rice-producing state in India is: Ans: West Bengal (followed by UP and Punjab)
Q.2041. The largest wheat-producing state is: Ans: Uttar Pradesh (followed by Punjab and Madhya Pradesh)
Q.2042. The largest cotton-producing state is: Ans: Gujarat (followed by Maharashtra and Telangana)
Q.2043. The largest sugarcane-producing state is: Ans: Uttar Pradesh (followed by Maharashtra)
Q.2044. Blue Revolution is related to: Ans: Fish production (aquaculture)
Q.2045. Yellow Revolution is related to: Ans: Oilseed production

14.8 Transport & Communication

Q.2046. Indian Railways is divided into how many zones? Ans: 18 zones
Q.2047. The South Central Railway zone is headquartered at: Ans: Secunderabad (Telangana)
Q.2048. The longest railway platform in India is at: Ans: Hubballi (Karnataka) – 1,505 meters
Q.2049. The first railway line in India ran between: Ans: Mumbai (Bori Bunder) to Thane in 1853
Q.2050. National Highways are maintained by: Ans: National Highways Authority of India (NHAI) under Ministry of Road Transport
Q.2051. The longest National Highway in India is: Ans: NH-44 (Srinagar to Kanyakumari, 3,745 km)
Q.2052. India's largest port by cargo handling is: Ans: Deendayal Port (Kandla), Gujarat (among major ports)
Q.2053. The Sagarmala Project aims to: Ans: Modernize ports and enhance port-led development
Q.2054. Bharatmala Pariyojana is: Ans: A centrally-sponsored highway development program for border and coastal roads
Q.2055. The Dedicated Freight Corridor connects: Ans: Eastern DFC (Ludhiana-Dankuni) and Western DFC (JNPT-Dadri)

14.9 Telangana Geography Specifics

Q.2056. Telangana is located on which plateau? Ans: Deccan Plateau
Q.2057. The geographical area of Telangana is: Ans: 1,12,077 sq km (about 3.5% of India's area)
Q.2058. Telangana shares borders with: Ans: Maharashtra (north), Chhattisgarh (northeast), Karnataka (west), Andhra Pradesh (south and east)
Q.2059. The major rivers of Telangana are: Ans: Godavari, Krishna, Manjira, Musi, Pranahita, Manair, Penganga, Bhima
Q.2060. The highest point in Telangana is: Ans: Venkatapuram Peak in Kumram Bheem Asifabad district (approximately 965 m)
Q.2061. The average elevation of Telangana is: Ans: 400-600 meters above sea level
Q.2062. The climate of Telangana is: Ans: Semi-arid (hot and dry summers, moderate rainfall 700-1000 mm)
Q.2063. The average annual rainfall of Telangana is: Ans: About 900 mm (mainly from southwest monsoon)
Q.2064. The forest cover of Telangana is approximately: Ans: About 24% of geographical area
Q.2065. Major forest types in Telangana include: Ans: Tropical Dry Deciduous forests (predominant), some Tropical Moist Deciduous in eastern parts
Q.2066. Kawal Tiger Reserve is located in: Ans: Mancherial and Kumram Bheem Asifabad districts
Q.2067. Amrabad Tiger Reserve is located in: Ans: Nagarkurnool and Nalgonda districts (part of Nallamala Hills)
Q.2068. Pakhal Lake is located in: Ans: Warangal district (built by Kakatiya king Ganapati Deva)
Q.2069. Pocharam Wildlife Sanctuary is in: Ans: Medak district
Q.2070. The Pranahita-Chevella Lift Irrigation Scheme is now part of: Ans: Kaleshwaram Lift Irrigation Project

14.10 World Geography Essentials

Q.2071. The largest continent by area is: Ans: Asia (44.58 million sq km)
Q.2072. The smallest continent is: Ans: Australia/Oceania
Q.2073. The longest river in the world is: Ans: Nile River (6,650 km) – some sources say Amazon
Q.2074. The largest freshwater lake by surface area is: Ans: Lake Superior (North America)
Q.2075. The deepest lake in the world is: Ans: Lake Baikal, Russia (1,642 m deep)
Q.2076. The highest mountain peak in the world is: Ans: Mount Everest (8,849 m) – on Nepal-Tibet border
Q.2077. The largest desert in the world is: Ans: Sahara Desert (hot desert); Antarctic is largest overall desert
Q.2078. The Ring of Fire is located around: Ans: Pacific Ocean (zone of frequent earthquakes and volcanic eruptions)
Q.2079. The Prime Meridian (0° longitude) passes through: Ans: Greenwich, London (UK)
Q.2080. The International Date Line roughly follows: Ans: 180° longitude (with deviations to avoid land masses)
Q.2081. The largest country by area is: Ans: Russia (17.1 million sq km)
Q.2082. The most populous country in the world (2023) is: Ans: India (surpassed China)
Q.2083. The Suez Canal connects: Ans: Mediterranean Sea and Red Sea (in Egypt)
Q.2084. The Panama Canal connects: Ans: Atlantic Ocean and Pacific Ocean (in Panama)
Q.2085. The Strait of Malacca is between: Ans: Malay Peninsula and Sumatra (connects Indian Ocean to Pacific Ocean)
Q.2086. The Palk Strait separates: Ans: India and Sri Lanka
Q.2087. The largest island in the world is: Ans: Greenland
Q.2088. The longest mountain range in the world is: Ans: Andes (South America, about 7,000 km)
Q.2089. The Great Barrier Reef is located off the coast of: Ans: Australia (in Coral Sea)
Q.2090. Earthquakes are measured on: Ans: Richter Scale (magnitude) and Modified Mercalli Scale (intensity)
Q.2091. The Earth's crust is divided into how many major tectonic plates? Ans: 7 major plates (Pacific, North American, South American, African, Eurasian, Antarctic, Indo-Australian)
Q.2092. The Himalayan mountain range was formed by collision of: Ans: Indian Plate and Eurasian Plate
Q.2093. The standard meridian of India is: Ans: 82°30' E longitude (passes through Mirzapur, UP)
Q.2094. India's total geographical area is: Ans: 32.87 lakh sq km (3.287 million sq km)
Q.2095. India extends from latitude: Ans: 8°4'N to 37°6'N
Q.2096. The southernmost point of India (mainland) is: Ans: Kanyakumari (Cape Comorin), Tamil Nadu
Q.2097. The southernmost point of India (including islands) is: Ans: Indira Point (Pygmalion Point) in Great Nicobar Island
Q.2098. India has a total coastline of: Ans: 7,516.6 km (mainland: 6,100 km)
Q.2099. The Western Ghats are also known as: Ans: Sahyadri Mountains
Q.2100. The Eastern Ghats are discontinuous and broken by rivers like: Ans: Godavari, Krishna, Cauvery, and Mahanadi

Section 15: Indian Economy & Development (200 Questions)

Topics: Five Year Plans, NITI Aayog, GDP/GNP Concepts, Inflation Types, RBI Monetary Policy, Banking Reforms, Fiscal Policy, Budget Terminology, Taxation (GST, Income Tax), Poverty Alleviation Schemes, Employment Programs, FDI/FII, WTO, IMF, World Bank, SEBI, Stock Markets, Insurance, Microfinance, Digital Economy, UPI

15.1 National Income & GDP Concepts

Q.2101. GDP stands for: Ans: Gross Domestic Product – total value of goods and services produced within a country's borders in a year
Q.2102. GNP stands for: Ans: Gross National Product = GDP + Net Factor Income from Abroad
Q.2103. NNP (Net National Product) = Ans: GNP – Depreciation
Q.2104. National Income is: Ans: NNP at Factor Cost (Net National Product at factor cost)
Q.2105. Per Capita Income = Ans: National Income / Total Population
Q.2106. GDP at current prices is called: Ans: Nominal GDP
Q.2107. GDP at constant prices (adjusted for inflation) is called: Ans: Real GDP
Q.2108. The base year for calculating India's GDP currently is: Ans: 2011-12
Q.2109. GDP is calculated by which organization in India? Ans: Central Statistics Office (CSO), now National Statistical Office (NSO)
Q.2110. The three methods of calculating GDP are: Ans: Production/Output method, Income method, Expenditure method
Q.2111. GDP deflator = Ans: (Nominal GDP / Real GDP) × 100
Q.2112. The largest sector contributing to India's GDP is: Ans: Services sector (about 54%)
Q.2113. The Human Development Index (HDI) was developed by: Ans: Mahbub ul Haq (published by UNDP since 1990)
Q.2114. HDI is based on three dimensions: Ans: Health (life expectancy), Education (mean and expected years of schooling), Standard of living (GNI per capita)
Q.2115. India's HDI rank (2022 report) is approximately: Ans: Around 132 out of 191 countries (Medium Human Development category)

15.2 Planning & Five Year Plans

Q.2116. The Planning Commission was established in: Ans: 1950 (by a resolution of Government of India, not by Constitution)
Q.2117. The First Five Year Plan (1951-56) was based on: Ans: Harrod-Domar Model (focused on agriculture and irrigation)
Q.2118. The Second Five Year Plan (1956-61) was based on: Ans: Mahalanobis Model (focused on heavy industries and industrialization)
Q.2119. The Green Revolution occurred during which plan? Ans: Third Five Year Plan (1961-66) and Annual Plans (1966-69)
Q.2120. The concept of 'Garibi Hatao' was associated with: Ans: Fifth Five Year Plan (1974-79)
Q.2121. Economic liberalization (LPG reforms) was introduced during: Ans: Eighth Five Year Plan (1992-97) under PM Narasimha Rao and FM Manmohan Singh
Q.2122. The last Five Year Plan was: Ans: Twelfth Five Year Plan (2012-2017) – "Faster, More Inclusive and Sustainable Growth"
Q.2123. LPG reforms stand for: Ans: Liberalization, Privatization, Globalization (introduced in 1991)
Q.2124. The 1991 economic crisis was triggered by: Ans: Balance of Payments crisis (forex reserves fell to cover only 2 weeks of imports)
Q.2125. The New Economic Policy (1991) was introduced by: Ans: Finance Minister Dr. Manmohan Singh under PM P.V. Narasimha Rao

15.3 Inflation & Price Index

Q.2126. Inflation means: Ans: Sustained increase in the general price level of goods and services over time
Q.2127. Deflation means: Ans: Sustained decrease in the general price level
Q.2128. Stagflation means: Ans: High inflation combined with high unemployment and stagnant economic growth
Q.2129. Demand-pull inflation is caused by: Ans: Excess demand over supply (too much money chasing too few goods)
Q.2130. Cost-push inflation is caused by: Ans: Increase in production costs (raw materials, wages) pushing up prices
Q.2131. CPI stands for: Ans: Consumer Price Index (measures retail inflation)
Q.2132. WPI stands for: Ans: Wholesale Price Index (measures wholesale inflation)
Q.2133. RBI uses which index for inflation targeting? Ans: CPI (Consumer Price Index) – target is 4% with tolerance band of +/- 2%
Q.2134. The base year for current CPI is: Ans: 2012
Q.2135. The base year for current WPI is: Ans: 2011-12
Q.2136. The Phillips Curve shows relationship between: Ans: Inflation and unemployment (inverse relationship)
Q.2137. Headline inflation includes: Ans: All items including food and fuel
Q.2138. Core inflation excludes: Ans: Food and fuel prices (which are volatile)
Q.2139. Hyperinflation refers to: Ans: Extremely high and accelerating inflation (typically above 50% per month)
Q.2140. The Monetary Policy Committee (MPC) of RBI has how many members? Ans: 6 members (3 from RBI + 3 external members appointed by Government)

15.4 RBI & Monetary Policy

Q.2141. The Reserve Bank of India was established in: Ans: April 1, 1935 (nationalized in 1949)
Q.2142. RBI is headquartered at: Ans: Mumbai
Q.2143. The first Governor of RBI was: Ans: Sir Osborne Smith (first Indian Governor: C.D. Deshmukh)
Q.2144. The Repo Rate is: Ans: The rate at which RBI lends short-term money to commercial banks (against government securities)
Q.2145. The Reverse Repo Rate is: Ans: The rate at which RBI borrows money from commercial banks
Q.2146. CRR (Cash Reserve Ratio) is: Ans: Percentage of deposits that banks must keep with RBI as cash
Q.2147. SLR (Statutory Liquidity Ratio) is: Ans: Percentage of deposits that banks must maintain in form of gold, cash, or government securities
Q.2148. Bank Rate is: Ans: Rate at which RBI provides long-term loans to commercial banks (without collateral)
Q.2149. Open Market Operations (OMO) means: Ans: RBI buying/selling government securities in open market to control money supply
Q.2150. MSF (Marginal Standing Facility) rate is: Ans: Rate at which banks can borrow overnight from RBI (above repo rate, against government securities)
Q.2151. To control inflation, RBI typically: Ans: Increases repo rate, CRR, SLR (contractionary/tight monetary policy)
Q.2152. To boost economic growth, RBI typically: Ans: Decreases repo rate, CRR, SLR (expansionary/easy monetary policy)
Q.2153. The LAF (Liquidity Adjustment Facility) includes: Ans: Repo and Reverse Repo operations
Q.2154. Priority Sector Lending requires banks to lend what percentage to priority sectors? Ans: 40% of Adjusted Net Bank Credit (for domestic banks)
Q.2155. Priority sectors include: Ans: Agriculture, MSMEs, Education, Housing, Social Infrastructure, Renewable Energy, Export Credit, Weaker Sections

15.5 Banking & Financial Sector

Q.2156. Bank nationalization in India occurred in: Ans: 1969 (14 banks) and 1980 (6 banks)
Q.2157. The largest public sector bank in India is: Ans: State Bank of India (SBI)
Q.2158. NABARD stands for: Ans: National Bank for Agriculture and Rural Development (established 1982)
Q.2159. SIDBI stands for: Ans: Small Industries Development Bank of India (established 1990)
Q.2160. NPA stands for: Ans: Non-Performing Asset (loan where interest/principal is overdue for more than 90 days)
Q.2161. The SARFAESI Act (2002) allows banks to: Ans: Recover NPAs without court intervention (Securitisation and Reconstruction of Financial Assets)
Q.2162. The Insolvency and Bankruptcy Code (IBC) was enacted in: Ans: 2016 (for time-bound resolution of insolvency)
Q.2163. MUDRA Bank was launched in: Ans: 2015 (Micro Units Development and Refinance Agency – for loans to micro enterprises)
Q.2164. The three categories of MUDRA loans are: Ans: Shishu (up to Rs. 50,000), Kishore (Rs. 50,000-5 lakh), Tarun (Rs. 5-10 lakh)
Q.2165. Jan Dhan Yojana was launched in: Ans: August 28, 2014 (for financial inclusion – zero balance accounts)
Q.2166. The Deposit Insurance and Credit Guarantee Corporation (DICGC) insures deposits up to: Ans: Rs. 5 lakh per depositor per bank
Q.2167. Payment Banks can accept deposits up to: Ans: Rs. 2 lakh per customer (cannot lend)
Q.2168. Small Finance Banks must lend at least 75% to: Ans: Priority sector
Q.2169. The Basel III norms relate to: Ans: Capital adequacy, stress testing, and market liquidity risk of banks
Q.2170. SWIFT stands for: Ans: Society for Worldwide Interbank Financial Telecommunication

15.6 Fiscal Policy & Budget

Q.2171. Fiscal policy deals with: Ans: Government's revenue (taxation) and expenditure policy
Q.2172. Fiscal Deficit = Ans: Total Expenditure – Total Receipts (excluding borrowings)
Q.2173. Revenue Deficit = Ans: Revenue Expenditure – Revenue Receipts
Q.2174. Primary Deficit = Ans: Fiscal Deficit – Interest Payments
Q.2175. The FRBM Act (2003) aims to: Ans: Fiscal Responsibility and Budget Management – reduce fiscal deficit and eliminate revenue deficit
Q.2176. The Union Budget is presented on: Ans: February 1 (since 2017; earlier it was last working day of February)
Q.2177. Article 112 of the Constitution deals with: Ans: Annual Financial Statement (Union Budget)
Q.2178. The Railway Budget was merged with Union Budget from: Ans: 2017-18
Q.2179. Direct taxes include: Ans: Income Tax, Corporate Tax, Capital Gains Tax, Securities Transaction Tax
Q.2180. Indirect taxes (now mostly subsumed under GST) included: Ans: Excise Duty, Service Tax, VAT, Customs Duty (customs still separate)
Q.2181. The Consolidated Fund of India is under: Ans: Article 266(1) – all revenues, loans, and repayments go here; withdrawals need Parliamentary approval
Q.2182. The Contingency Fund of India is under: Ans: Article 267 – at disposal of President for unforeseen expenditure (later approved by Parliament)
Q.2183. The Public Account of India is under: Ans: Article 266(2) – includes provident funds, small savings, etc. (government acts as banker)
Q.2184. Vote on Account allows government to: Ans: Withdraw money from Consolidated Fund for a part of the year (before full budget is passed)
Q.2185. Appropriation Bill must be passed to: Ans: Authorize withdrawal of money from Consolidated Fund

15.7 Taxation & GST

Q.2186. GST is a: Ans: Destination-based, multi-stage, comprehensive indirect tax on supply of goods and services
Q.2187. The GST rates in India are: Ans: 0%, 5%, 12%, 18%, and 28% (plus cess on some items)
Q.2188. CGST is levied by: Ans: Central Government (on intra-state supply)
Q.2189. SGST is levied by: Ans: State Government (on intra-state supply)
Q.2190. IGST is levied by: Ans: Central Government (on inter-state supply)
Q.2191. The GST Network (GSTN) is: Ans: IT backbone for GST implementation (manages registration, returns, payments)
Q.2192. Input Tax Credit (ITC) under GST means: Ans: Credit for tax paid on inputs can be set off against output tax liability
Q.2193. The Laffer Curve shows relationship between: Ans: Tax rate and tax revenue (revenue increases with rate up to a point, then decreases)
Q.2194. Progressive taxation means: Ans: Tax rate increases as income increases (e.g., income tax slabs)
Q.2195. Regressive taxation means: Ans: Tax burden falls more heavily on lower income groups (e.g., indirect taxes on essentials)

15.8 Poverty & Employment Schemes

Q.2196. The poverty line in India is based on: Ans: Monthly Per Capita Expenditure (MPCE) – Tendulkar Committee methodology
Q.2197. The Tendulkar Committee (2009) estimated poverty at: Ans: Rs. 816/month (rural) and Rs. 1,000/month (urban) at 2004-05 prices
Q.2198. The Rangarajan Committee (2014) estimated poverty line at: Ans: Rs. 972/month (rural) and Rs. 1,407/month (urban)
Q.2199. MGNREGA (Mahatma Gandhi National Rural Employment Guarantee Act) guarantees: Ans: 100 days of wage employment per year to every rural household
Q.2200. MGNREGA was enacted in: Ans: 2005 (implemented from February 2, 2006)
Q.2201. The National Food Security Act (2013) covers: Ans: 75% rural and 50% urban population (5 kg foodgrains per person per month at subsidized rates)
Q.2202. PM Garib Kalyan Anna Yojana provides: Ans: Free foodgrains to beneficiaries under NFSA
Q.2203. The Multidimensional Poverty Index (MPI) is published by: Ans: UNDP and Oxford Poverty and Human Development Initiative (OPHI)
Q.2204. Skill India Mission was launched in: Ans: 2015 (to train 40 crore people in different skills by 2022)
Q.2205. PMEGP (Prime Minister's Employment Generation Programme) is implemented by: Ans: KVIC (Khadi and Village Industries Commission)

15.9 International Trade & Organizations

Q.2206. WTO (World Trade Organization) was established in: Ans: January 1, 1995 (replaced GATT; headquartered in Geneva)
Q.2207. IMF (International Monetary Fund) was established in: Ans: 1945 (Bretton Woods Conference, 1944; HQ: Washington DC)
Q.2208. The World Bank was established in: Ans: 1944 (Bretton Woods; HQ: Washington DC)
Q.2209. SDR (Special Drawing Rights) is the currency of: Ans: IMF (basket of currencies: USD, Euro, Yuan, Yen, Pound)
Q.2210. FDI stands for: Ans: Foreign Direct Investment (long-term investment with management control)
Q.2211. FPI/FII stands for: Ans: Foreign Portfolio Investment / Foreign Institutional Investor (short-term, no management control)
Q.2212. Balance of Payments (BoP) consists of: Ans: Current Account + Capital Account + Financial Account
Q.2213. Current Account includes: Ans: Trade in goods and services, income, and current transfers (remittances)
Q.2214. India's largest trading partner is: Ans: USA (in terms of total trade); China is largest source of imports
Q.2215. BRICS consists of: Ans: Brazil, Russia, India, China, South Africa (expanded in 2024 to include more members)
Q.2216. The New Development Bank (NDB) was established by: Ans: BRICS nations in 2014 (HQ: Shanghai)
Q.2217. The Asian Infrastructure Investment Bank (AIIB) is headquartered at: Ans: Beijing, China (established 2016)
Q.2218. RCEP stands for: Ans: Regional Comprehensive Economic Partnership (India opted out in 2019)
Q.2219. India's forex reserves are managed by: Ans: Reserve Bank of India
Q.2220. The rupee exchange rate is determined by: Ans: Market forces (managed floating exchange rate system since 1993)

15.10 Capital Markets & SEBI

Q.2221. SEBI (Securities and Exchange Board of India) was established in: Ans: 1988 (given statutory powers in 1992)
Q.2222. SEBI's main function is: Ans: Regulate securities market, protect investor interests, promote development of securities market
Q.2223. BSE (Bombay Stock Exchange) was established in: Ans: 1875 (oldest stock exchange in Asia)
Q.2224. NSE (National Stock Exchange) was established in: Ans: 1992 (started trading in 1994)
Q.2225. Sensex is the index of: Ans: BSE (comprises 30 stocks)
Q.2226. Nifty 50 is the index of: Ans: NSE (comprises 50 stocks)
Q.2227. IPO stands for: Ans: Initial Public Offering (first sale of shares to public)
Q.2228. A Bull Market means: Ans: Rising stock prices (optimistic market)
Q.2229. A Bear Market means: Ans: Falling stock prices (pessimistic market)
Q.2230. Demat Account is used for: Ans: Holding shares in electronic/dematerialized form (managed by NSDL and CDSL)

15.11 Insurance & Microfinance

Q.2231. IRDAI stands for: Ans: Insurance Regulatory and Development Authority of India (established 1999)
Q.2232. LIC (Life Insurance Corporation) was established in: Ans: 1956 (by nationalizing 245 private insurance companies)
Q.2233. PM Jeevan Jyoti Bima Yojana provides: Ans: Rs. 2 lakh life insurance cover at premium of Rs. 436/year (age 18-50)
Q.2234. PM Suraksha Bima Yojana provides: Ans: Rs. 2 lakh accidental death/disability insurance at Rs. 20/year (age 18-70)
Q.2235. Atal Pension Yojana provides: Ans: Guaranteed pension of Rs. 1,000-5,000/month after age 60 (for unorganized sector workers)
Q.2236. Self-Help Groups (SHGs) typically consist of: Ans: 10-20 members (usually women) who save and lend among themselves
Q.2237. The SHG-Bank Linkage Programme was started by: Ans: NABARD in 1992
Q.2238. Microfinance in India was pioneered by: Ans: SEWA (Self Employed Women's Association) and organizations like SKS, Bandhan
Q.2239. The Grameen Bank model was developed by: Ans: Muhammad Yunus in Bangladesh (Nobel Peace Prize 2006)
Q.2240. Financial Inclusion means: Ans: Providing access to financial services (banking, credit, insurance) to all sections of society

15.12 Digital Economy & UPI

Q.2241. UPI stands for: Ans: Unified Payments Interface (developed by NPCI, launched in 2016)
Q.2242. NPCI stands for: Ans: National Payments Corporation of India
Q.2243. Digital India programme was launched in: Ans: July 1, 2015
Q.2244. BHIM App stands for: Ans: Bharat Interface for Money (UPI-based payment app)
Q.2245. RuPay card was launched by: Ans: NPCI in 2012 (India's own card payment network)
Q.2246. Demonetization of Rs. 500 and Rs. 1000 notes was announced on: Ans: November 8, 2016
Q.2247. The objective of demonetization was: Ans: Curbing black money, counterfeit currency, and promoting digital payments
Q.2248. E-RUPI is: Ans: A digital payment solution (prepaid voucher) for specific purposes, launched in 2021
Q.2249. India Stack refers to: Ans: Set of APIs (Aadhaar, UPI, DigiLocker, eSign) enabling digital infrastructure
Q.2250. The Central Bank Digital Currency (CBDC) pilot in India is called: Ans: Digital Rupee (e₹) – launched by RBI in 2022

15.13 Miscellaneous Economy

Q.2251. Make in India was launched in: Ans: September 25, 2014 (to boost manufacturing sector)
Q.2252. Startup India was launched in: Ans: January 16, 2016
Q.2253. Stand-Up India scheme provides: Ans: Bank loans between Rs. 10 lakh to Rs. 1 crore to SC/ST and women entrepreneurs
Q.2254. The Production Linked Incentive (PLI) scheme covers: Ans: 14 sectors including electronics, pharma, automobiles, textiles, food processing
Q.2255. Atmanirbhar Bharat Abhiyan was launched in: Ans: May 2020 (Self-Reliant India – Rs. 20 lakh crore economic package during COVID)
Q.2256. The Gig Economy refers to: Ans: Labor market characterized by short-term, freelance, or contract work (e.g., Uber, Swiggy workers)
Q.2257. India's tax-to-GDP ratio is approximately: Ans: Around 11-12% (lower than OECD average of ~34%)
Q.2258. The Ease of Doing Business Index is published by: Ans: World Bank (discontinued after 2020; India ranked 63rd in last edition)
Q.2259. Disinvestment means: Ans: Government selling its stake in public sector enterprises to private investors
Q.2260. DIPAM stands for: Ans: Department of Investment and Public Asset Management (handles disinvestment)
Q.2261. PPP (Public Private Partnership) model is used for: Ans: Infrastructure development where government and private sector collaborate
Q.2262. BOT stands for: Ans: Build-Operate-Transfer (a PPP model)
Q.2263. SEZ stands for: Ans: Special Economic Zone (for promoting exports with tax incentives)
Q.2264. The first SEZ in India was set up at: Ans: Kandla, Gujarat (2000)
Q.2265. MSME stands for: Ans: Micro, Small and Medium Enterprises
Q.2266. Under revised MSME classification, a Micro enterprise has investment up to: Ans: Rs. 1 crore and turnover up to Rs. 5 crore
Q.2267. The National Infrastructure Pipeline (NIP) targets investment of: Ans: Rs. 111 lakh crore during 2020-2025
Q.2268. Sovereign Wealth Fund of India is: Ans: National Investment and Infrastructure Fund (NIIF), established 2015
Q.2269. The Economic Survey is presented by: Ans: Chief Economic Adviser (one day before Union Budget)
Q.2270. India's external debt is primarily denominated in: Ans: US Dollar
Q.2271. The Gini Coefficient measures: Ans: Income inequality (0 = perfect equality, 1 = perfect inequality)
Q.2272. Lorenz Curve graphically represents: Ans: Income distribution/inequality in a society
Q.2273. Purchasing Power Parity (PPP) is used to: Ans: Compare living standards between countries by adjusting for price differences
Q.2274. India's GDP rank in the world (nominal, 2023) is: Ans: 5th largest economy
Q.2275. India's GDP rank by PPP is: Ans: 3rd largest economy
Q.2276. The demographic dividend refers to: Ans: Economic growth potential from a large working-age population relative to dependents
Q.2277. India's working age population (15-64 years) is approximately: Ans: About 67% of total population
Q.2278. The National Monetisation Pipeline (NMP) aims to: Ans: Monetize government's brownfield infrastructure assets (Rs. 6 lakh crore target)
Q.2279. PM GatiShakti is: Ans: National Master Plan for multi-modal connectivity and infrastructure (launched 2021)
Q.2280. The Goods and Services Tax Compensation to states was guaranteed for: Ans: 5 years (2017-2022) at 14% annual growth rate
Q.2281. Angel Tax is levied on: Ans: Startups receiving investment above fair market value (Section 56(2)(viib) of IT Act)
Q.2282. The Tobin Tax is a tax on: Ans: Foreign exchange transactions (to reduce speculation)
Q.2283. Hawala transactions refer to: Ans: Illegal money transfer without actual movement of currency (informal value transfer)
Q.2284. PMLA stands for: Ans: Prevention of Money Laundering Act, 2002
Q.2285. The Enforcement Directorate (ED) deals with: Ans: Economic offences including money laundering and foreign exchange violations
Q.2286. FATF stands for: Ans: Financial Action Task Force (inter-governmental body to combat money laundering and terror financing)
Q.2287. India is a member of FATF since: Ans: 2010
Q.2288. The Fiscal Responsibility and Budget Management (FRBM) Act target for fiscal deficit is: Ans: 3% of GDP (as per original target; revised timelines given)
Q.2289. Ways and Means Advances (WMA) are: Ans: Short-term loans by RBI to Central/State governments to bridge temporary mismatches in receipts and payments
Q.2290. Treasury Bills are issued for: Ans: 91 days, 182 days, and 364 days (short-term government borrowing)
Q.2291. Government Securities (G-Secs) are: Ans: Long-term debt instruments issued by government (considered risk-free)
Q.2292. Sovereign Gold Bond Scheme is issued by: Ans: RBI on behalf of Government of India (alternative to physical gold)
Q.2293. The National Pension System (NPS) was launched in: Ans: 2004 for government employees; extended to all citizens in 2009
Q.2294. EPFO stands for: Ans: Employees' Provident Fund Organisation
Q.2295. The current EPF contribution rate is: Ans: 12% each by employee and employer (total 24% of basic salary)
Q.2296. Cryptocurrency regulation in India: Ans: 30% tax on crypto gains (introduced in Budget 2022-23); no specific regulatory framework yet
Q.2297. The Competition Commission of India (CCI) was established under: Ans: Competition Act, 2002 (to prevent anti-competitive practices)
Q.2298. Dumping in international trade means: Ans: Exporting goods at a price lower than domestic market price (anti-dumping duty can be imposed)
Q.2299. Most Favoured Nation (MFN) principle of WTO means: Ans: Trade concessions given to one member must be extended to all WTO members equally
Q.2300. India's largest source of foreign exchange earnings is: Ans: IT/Software services exports and remittances from abroad

Section 16: General Science Advanced (200 Questions)

Topics: Physics (Mechanics, Optics, Electricity, Magnetism, Modern Physics, Nuclear Energy), Chemistry (Periodic Table, Acids/Bases, Metals, Organic Chemistry, Polymers, Everyday Chemistry), Biology (Human Body Systems, Diseases, Nutrition, Genetics, Ecology, Biodiversity), Space & Technology (ISRO Missions, Satellites, Space Exploration)

16.1 Physics – Mechanics & Properties of Matter

Q.2301. Newton's First Law of Motion states: Ans: A body at rest stays at rest and a body in motion stays in uniform motion unless acted upon by an external force (Law of Inertia)
Q.2302. Newton's Second Law: F = Ans: ma (Force = mass × acceleration)
Q.2303. Newton's Third Law states: Ans: For every action, there is an equal and opposite reaction
Q.2304. The SI unit of force is: Ans: Newton (N) = kg⋅m/s²
Q.2305. Acceleration due to gravity (g) on Earth's surface is approximately: Ans: 9.8 m/s²
Q.2306. The value of g is maximum at: Ans: Poles (and minimum at equator due to Earth's rotation and shape)
Q.2307. Escape velocity from Earth is: Ans: 11.2 km/s
Q.2308. Pascal's Law states: Ans: Pressure applied to a confined fluid is transmitted equally in all directions (used in hydraulic machines)
Q.2309. Archimedes' Principle states: Ans: A body immersed in fluid experiences an upward buoyant force equal to weight of fluid displaced
Q.2310. Bernoulli's Principle relates to: Ans: Fluid dynamics – increase in speed of fluid decreases pressure (explains airplane lift)
Q.2311. The unit of pressure is: Ans: Pascal (Pa) = N/m² (also atm, bar, mmHg)
Q.2312. Atmospheric pressure at sea level is: Ans: 1 atm = 101,325 Pa = 760 mmHg
Q.2313. Surface tension causes: Ans: Liquids to minimize surface area (water drops are spherical, insects walk on water)
Q.2314. Viscosity is: Ans: Internal friction of a fluid (resistance to flow); unit: Poise or Pa⋅s
Q.2315. Hooke's Law states: Ans: Stress is proportional to strain within elastic limit (F = -kx for springs)

16.2 Physics – Heat & Thermodynamics

Q.2316. The three modes of heat transfer are: Ans: Conduction, Convection, and Radiation
Q.2317. Absolute zero temperature is: Ans: 0 K = -273.15°C (lowest possible temperature)
Q.2318. Specific heat capacity of water is: Ans: 4,186 J/(kg⋅K) or 1 cal/(g⋅°C) – highest among common substances
Q.2319. Latent heat of fusion of ice is: Ans: 334 J/g (80 cal/g)
Q.2320. Latent heat of vaporization of water is: Ans: 2,260 J/g (540 cal/g)
Q.2321. The First Law of Thermodynamics is: Ans: Energy can neither be created nor destroyed (conservation of energy); ΔU = Q - W
Q.2322. The Second Law of Thermodynamics states: Ans: Heat flows spontaneously from hot to cold body; entropy of an isolated system always increases
Q.2323. A thermos flask prevents heat transfer by: Ans: Vacuum (prevents conduction and convection), silvered walls (prevents radiation)
Q.2324. The greenhouse effect is caused by: Ans: CO₂, methane, water vapor, and other gases trapping infrared radiation in atmosphere
Q.2325. Global warming is primarily caused by: Ans: Increased CO₂ and greenhouse gas emissions from burning fossil fuels

16.3 Physics – Optics

Q.2326. The speed of light in vacuum is: Ans: 3 × 10⁸ m/s (approximately 300,000 km/s)
Q.2327. Snell's Law relates to: Ans: Refraction of light (n₁ sin θ₁ = n₂ sin θ₂)
Q.2328. Total internal reflection occurs when: Ans: Light travels from denser to rarer medium at angle greater than critical angle (used in optical fibers)
Q.2329. A convex lens is used for: Ans: Correcting hypermetropia (farsightedness), magnifying glass, camera
Q.2330. A concave lens is used for: Ans: Correcting myopia (nearsightedness)
Q.2331. The phenomenon of splitting white light into seven colors is: Ans: Dispersion (as in a prism – VIBGYOR)
Q.2332. Rainbow is formed due to: Ans: Dispersion, refraction, and total internal reflection of sunlight in water droplets
Q.2333. The color of sky appears blue because of: Ans: Rayleigh scattering (shorter wavelength blue light is scattered more)
Q.2334. The sun appears red at sunrise/sunset because: Ans: Blue light is scattered away; only longer wavelength red light reaches observer
Q.2335. LASER stands for: Ans: Light Amplification by Stimulated Emission of Radiation

16.4 Physics – Electricity & Magnetism

Q.2336. Ohm's Law states: Ans: V = IR (Voltage = Current × Resistance)
Q.2337. The SI unit of electric current is: Ans: Ampere (A)
Q.2338. The SI unit of resistance is: Ans: Ohm (Ω)
Q.2339. Electric power P = Ans: VI = I²R = V²/R (unit: Watt)
Q.2340. 1 kilowatt-hour (kWh) = Ans: 3.6 × 10⁶ Joules (1 unit of electricity)
Q.2341. A fuse wire is made of: Ans: Alloy of lead and tin (low melting point, high resistance)
Q.2342. The heating element in electric heaters is made of: Ans: Nichrome (alloy of nickel and chromium – high resistance, high melting point)
Q.2343. Electromagnetic induction was discovered by: Ans: Michael Faraday (1831)
Q.2344. A transformer works on the principle of: Ans: Electromagnetic induction (mutual induction)
Q.2345. An electric motor converts: Ans: Electrical energy to mechanical energy
Q.2346. A generator/dynamo converts: Ans: Mechanical energy to electrical energy
Q.2347. LED stands for: Ans: Light Emitting Diode (semiconductor device)
Q.2348. The Earth's magnetic north pole is near: Ans: Geographic south pole (and vice versa)
Q.2349. Fleming's Left Hand Rule is used for: Ans: Direction of force on current-carrying conductor in magnetic field (motor rule)
Q.2350. Fleming's Right Hand Rule is used for: Ans: Direction of induced current (generator rule)

16.5 Physics – Modern Physics & Nuclear Energy

Q.2351. Radioactivity was discovered by: Ans: Henri Becquerel (1896)
Q.2352. The three types of radioactive emissions are: Ans: Alpha (α) particles, Beta (β) particles, and Gamma (γ) rays
Q.2353. Nuclear fission means: Ans: Splitting of a heavy nucleus into lighter nuclei with release of energy (used in nuclear reactors and atomic bombs)
Q.2354. Nuclear fusion means: Ans: Combining light nuclei to form heavier nucleus with release of energy (occurs in Sun and stars)
Q.2355. E = mc² was given by: Ans: Albert Einstein (mass-energy equivalence)
Q.2356. The fuel used in nuclear reactors is: Ans: Uranium-235 or Plutonium-239
Q.2357. Heavy water (D₂O) is used in nuclear reactors as: Ans: Moderator (to slow down neutrons)
Q.2358. Control rods in nuclear reactors are made of: Ans: Cadmium or Boron (absorb excess neutrons)
Q.2359. India's first nuclear power plant was at: Ans: Tarapur, Maharashtra (1969)
Q.2360. India's three-stage nuclear programme was designed by: Ans: Dr. Homi J. Bhabha
Q.2361. The photoelectric effect was explained by: Ans: Albert Einstein (1905) – light behaves as particles (photons)
Q.2362. X-rays were discovered by: Ans: Wilhelm Röntgen (1895)
Q.2363. The atom bomb is based on: Ans: Uncontrolled nuclear fission chain reaction
Q.2364. The hydrogen bomb is based on: Ans: Nuclear fusion (thermonuclear reaction)
Q.2365. Carbon dating is used to determine: Ans: Age of fossils and archaeological specimens (using C-14 isotope, half-life ~5,730 years)

16.6 Chemistry – Periodic Table & Elements

Q.2366. The Modern Periodic Table is based on: Ans: Atomic number (Moseley's Periodic Law)
Q.2367. The Modern Periodic Table has: Ans: 18 groups and 7 periods
Q.2368. Noble gases are in Group: Ans: 18 (He, Ne, Ar, Kr, Xe, Rn – chemically inert)
Q.2369. Halogens are in Group: Ans: 17 (F, Cl, Br, I, At – most reactive non-metals)
Q.2370. Alkali metals are in Group: Ans: 1 (Li, Na, K, Rb, Cs, Fr – most reactive metals)
Q.2371. The lightest element is: Ans: Hydrogen (atomic number 1)
Q.2372. The heaviest naturally occurring element is: Ans: Uranium (atomic number 92)
Q.2373. The most abundant element in Earth's crust is: Ans: Oxygen (about 46%)
Q.2374. The most abundant element in the universe is: Ans: Hydrogen
Q.2375. The most abundant metal in Earth's crust is: Ans: Aluminium

16.7 Chemistry – Acids, Bases & Salts

Q.2376. pH scale ranges from: Ans: 0 to 14 (7 = neutral, below 7 = acidic, above 7 = basic)
Q.2377. The pH of human blood is: Ans: 7.35-7.45 (slightly alkaline)
Q.2378. The pH of pure water is: Ans: 7 (neutral)
Q.2379. Acid rain has pH less than: Ans: 5.6 (caused by SO₂ and NOₓ dissolving in rainwater)
Q.2380. Baking soda (sodium bicarbonate) formula is: Ans: NaHCO₃
Q.2381. Washing soda formula is: Ans: Na₂CO₃·10H₂O (sodium carbonate decahydrate)
Q.2382. Plaster of Paris formula is: Ans: CaSO₄·½H₂O (calcium sulphate hemihydrate)
Q.2383. Bleaching powder formula is: Ans: Ca(OCl)Cl or CaOCl₂ (calcium hypochlorite)
Q.2384. The acid present in vinegar is: Ans: Acetic acid (CH₃COOH)
Q.2385. The acid present in lemon/citrus fruits is: Ans: Citric acid
Q.2386. The acid present in stomach is: Ans: Hydrochloric acid (HCl)
Q.2387. Antacids contain: Ans: Bases like Mg(OH)₂ or Al(OH)₃ to neutralize excess stomach acid
Q.2388. Hard water contains excess of: Ans: Calcium and Magnesium salts (bicarbonates, chlorides, sulphates)
Q.2389. Temporary hardness of water is removed by: Ans: Boiling (converts bicarbonates to insoluble carbonates)
Q.2390. Permanent hardness of water is removed by: Ans: Adding washing soda (Na₂CO₃) or using ion exchange method

16.8 Chemistry – Metals & Everyday Chemistry

Q.2391. The most ductile metal is: Ans: Gold (can be drawn into thinnest wire)
Q.2392. The most malleable metal is: Ans: Gold (can be beaten into thinnest sheets)
Q.2393. The best conductor of electricity is: Ans: Silver (followed by copper, gold, aluminium)
Q.2394. The metal with highest melting point is: Ans: Tungsten (3,422°C – used in bulb filaments)
Q.2395. The only liquid metal at room temperature is: Ans: Mercury (Hg)
Q.2396. The only liquid non-metal at room temperature is: Ans: Bromine (Br)
Q.2397. Stainless steel is an alloy of: Ans: Iron, Chromium (minimum 10.5%), and Nickel
Q.2398. Bronze is an alloy of: Ans: Copper and Tin
Q.2399. Brass is an alloy of: Ans: Copper and Zinc
Q.2400. Rusting of iron requires: Ans: Both oxygen and moisture (water)
Q.2401. Galvanization is: Ans: Coating iron with zinc to prevent rusting
Q.2402. LPG (Liquefied Petroleum Gas) mainly contains: Ans: Butane and Propane
Q.2403. CNG (Compressed Natural Gas) mainly contains: Ans: Methane (CH₃)
Q.2404. The chemical name of common salt is: Ans: Sodium Chloride (NaCl)
Q.2405. Dry ice is: Ans: Solid carbon dioxide (CO₂) – sublimes directly to gas

16.9 Biology – Human Body Systems

Q.2406. The largest organ of the human body is: Ans: Skin
Q.2407. The largest internal organ is: Ans: Liver
Q.2408. The smallest bone in the human body is: Ans: Stapes (in the middle ear)
Q.2409. The largest bone in the human body is: Ans: Femur (thigh bone)
Q.2410. Total number of bones in adult human body: Ans: 206
Q.2411. The normal human body temperature is: Ans: 37°C or 98.6°F
Q.2412. The normal blood pressure is: Ans: 120/80 mmHg (systolic/diastolic)
Q.2413. The universal blood donor group is: Ans: O negative (O-)
Q.2414. The universal blood recipient group is: Ans: AB positive (AB+)
Q.2415. RBC (Red Blood Cells) are produced in: Ans: Bone marrow
Q.2416. The lifespan of RBC is: Ans: About 120 days
Q.2417. Hemoglobin contains which metal? Ans: Iron (Fe)
Q.2418. The functional unit of kidney is: Ans: Nephron
Q.2419. The functional unit of liver is: Ans: Hepatocyte (liver lobule)
Q.2420. Insulin is produced by: Ans: Beta cells of Islets of Langerhans in Pancreas
Q.2421. Diabetes mellitus is caused by: Ans: Deficiency or ineffectiveness of insulin (leads to high blood sugar)
Q.2422. The master gland of the endocrine system is: Ans: Pituitary gland
Q.2423. Thyroid gland produces: Ans: Thyroxine (T4) and Triiodothyronine (T3) – regulate metabolism
Q.2424. Iodine deficiency causes: Ans: Goitre (enlargement of thyroid gland)
Q.2425. The largest gland in the human body is: Ans: Liver

16.10 Biology – Diseases & Nutrition

Q.2426. Malaria is caused by: Ans: Plasmodium parasite (transmitted by female Anopheles mosquito)
Q.2427. Dengue is transmitted by: Ans: Aedes aegypti mosquito (viral disease)
Q.2428. Tuberculosis (TB) is caused by: Ans: Mycobacterium tuberculosis (bacterial disease affecting lungs)
Q.2429. AIDS is caused by: Ans: HIV (Human Immunodeficiency Virus)
Q.2430. COVID-19 is caused by: Ans: SARS-CoV-2 virus (coronavirus)
Q.2431. Vitamin A deficiency causes: Ans: Night blindness (Nyctalopia)
Q.2432. Vitamin B1 (Thiamine) deficiency causes: Ans: Beriberi
Q.2433. Vitamin C deficiency causes: Ans: Scurvy (bleeding gums, weakness)
Q.2434. Vitamin D deficiency causes: Ans: Rickets (in children) and Osteomalacia (in adults)
Q.2435. Vitamin K is essential for: Ans: Blood clotting
Q.2436. Iron deficiency causes: Ans: Anaemia
Q.2437. Calcium deficiency causes: Ans: Osteoporosis (weak and brittle bones)
Q.2438. Protein deficiency in children causes: Ans: Kwashiorkor and Marasmus
Q.2439. The first vaccine was developed by: Ans: Edward Jenner (1796) – for smallpox
Q.2440. Antibiotics were discovered by: Ans: Alexander Fleming (Penicillin, 1928)

16.11 Biology – Genetics & Ecology

Q.2441. DNA stands for: Ans: Deoxyribonucleic Acid
Q.2442. The structure of DNA (double helix) was discovered by: Ans: Watson and Crick (1953)
Q.2443. Genes are located on: Ans: Chromosomes (made of DNA)
Q.2444. Humans have how many pairs of chromosomes? Ans: 23 pairs (46 chromosomes total)
Q.2445. Sex chromosomes in males are: Ans: XY (females have XX)
Q.2446. The father of genetics is: Ans: Gregor Mendel
Q.2447. GMO stands for: Ans: Genetically Modified Organism
Q.2448. Bt Cotton is: Ans: Genetically modified cotton with Bacillus thuringiensis gene (resistant to bollworm)
Q.2449. The ozone layer is found in: Ans: Stratosphere (15-35 km altitude)
Q.2450. Ozone depletion is caused by: Ans: CFCs (Chlorofluorocarbons), halons, and other ozone-depleting substances
Q.2451. The Montreal Protocol (1987) deals with: Ans: Phasing out ozone-depleting substances
Q.2452. The Kyoto Protocol (1997) deals with: Ans: Reduction of greenhouse gas emissions
Q.2453. The Paris Agreement (2015) aims to: Ans: Limit global temperature rise to well below 2°C (preferably 1.5°C) above pre-industrial levels
Q.2454. Biodiversity hotspots in India include: Ans: Western Ghats, Eastern Himalayas, Indo-Burma, Sundaland (4 out of 36 global hotspots)
Q.2455. The term 'Biodiversity' was coined by: Ans: Walter G. Rosen (1985)

16.12 Space & Technology – ISRO

Q.2456. ISRO was established in: Ans: 1969 (Indian Space Research Organisation; HQ: Bengaluru)
Q.2457. The father of Indian space programme is: Ans: Dr. Vikram Sarabhai
Q.2458. India's first satellite was: Ans: Aryabhata (launched April 19, 1975 by Soviet rocket)
Q.2459. India's first indigenous satellite launch vehicle was: Ans: SLV-3 (launched Rohini satellite in 1980)
Q.2460. PSLV stands for: Ans: Polar Satellite Launch Vehicle (workhorse of ISRO)
Q.2461. GSLV stands for: Ans: Geosynchronous Satellite Launch Vehicle
Q.2462. Chandrayaan-1 (2008) discovered: Ans: Water molecules on the Moon's surface
Q.2463. Chandrayaan-3 successfully landed on Moon on: Ans: August 23, 2023 (near south pole – India became 4th country to soft-land on Moon)
Q.2464. Mangalyaan (Mars Orbiter Mission) was launched in: Ans: November 5, 2013 (reached Mars orbit September 24, 2014 – India's first interplanetary mission)
Q.2465. India became the first country to reach Mars orbit in its first attempt: Ans: True (and at lowest cost – about $74 million)
Q.2466. The first Indian in space was: Ans: Rakesh Sharma (April 3, 1984 – aboard Soviet Soyuz T-11)
Q.2467. Gaganyaan is: Ans: India's first crewed space mission (planned by ISRO)
Q.2468. NavIC is: Ans: Navigation with Indian Constellation – India's regional satellite navigation system (like GPS)
Q.2469. INSAT series satellites are used for: Ans: Communication, broadcasting, meteorology
Q.2470. IRS series satellites are used for: Ans: Indian Remote Sensing (earth observation, resource management)
Q.2471. Aditya-L1 mission is: Ans: India's first solar observation mission (launched September 2, 2023 to Sun-Earth L1 point)
Q.2472. The Satish Dhawan Space Centre is located at: Ans: Sriharikota, Andhra Pradesh (ISRO's launch site)
Q.2473. ISRO set a world record by launching how many satellites in one mission (PSLV-C37)? Ans: 104 satellites (February 15, 2017)
Q.2474. AstroSat is: Ans: India's first dedicated multi-wavelength space observatory (launched 2015)
Q.2475. The Geosynchronous orbit altitude is: Ans: About 35,786 km above Earth's equator

16.13 Science & Technology Miscellaneous

Q.2476. 5G technology operates in which frequency bands? Ans: Sub-6 GHz and mmWave (millimeter wave, 24-100 GHz)
Q.2477. Artificial Intelligence (AI) refers to: Ans: Machines/computers simulating human intelligence (learning, reasoning, problem-solving)
Q.2478. Blockchain technology is the basis of: Ans: Cryptocurrencies (decentralized, distributed ledger technology)
Q.2479. IoT stands for: Ans: Internet of Things (network of physical devices connected to internet)
Q.2480. Quantum computing uses: Ans: Qubits (quantum bits) that can be in superposition of 0 and 1 simultaneously
Q.2481. CRISPR-Cas9 is: Ans: A gene-editing technology (allows precise modification of DNA)
Q.2482. 3D Printing is also known as: Ans: Additive Manufacturing (builds objects layer by layer)
Q.2483. Nanotechnology deals with materials at scale of: Ans: 1-100 nanometers (1 nm = 10⁻⁹ m)
Q.2484. Solar cells convert: Ans: Solar energy (light) directly into electrical energy (photovoltaic effect)
Q.2485. The most common material used in solar cells is: Ans: Silicon (semiconductor)
Q.2486. Hydrogen fuel cells produce electricity by: Ans: Combining hydrogen and oxygen (byproduct is water – clean energy)
Q.2487. DRDO stands for: Ans: Defence Research and Development Organisation
